**Your job:** for EACH finding in your assigned specialist file that has a critic-supplied "Calibration questions for go-deep investigation" block, produce a deep investigation:

   - `grep -rn` for similar shapes already in the codebase (helpers, factories, single-owner seams).

4. **Per finding: emit a recommendation.** Choose ONE:
   - **`KEEP`** — the finding stands as the specialist + critic produced it. Brief justification.

   - **`DROP`** — investigation showed the finding does not hold (false positive on closer reading, already addressed in tests/, declined ≥3 rounds with same context, etc.). The aggregator will omit it from the published findings.
   - **`REFRAME`** — the underlying concern is real but firing rate is observably zero AND remedy is additive at our operating point. Move to Open Questions with cost-naming. Provide the reframed question text.

**Discipline:**
- One investigation block per finding-with-calibration-questions in your assigned specialist file. Findings without calibration questions are <20 LOC remedy and don't need go-deep — skip them silently (the aggregator publishes them as the critic produced them).
- Cite path:line for every claim of evidence. Hand-waving without cites is a failure mode — the aggregator will discard recommendations without grounding.
- Stay within the assigned specialist's findings. Don't drift into other specialists' territory; another go-deep instance is investigating those (or no one is, because no calibration questions surfaced there).
- If your assigned specialist file has zero findings with calibration questions: emit exactly `(no findings ≥20 LOC remedy in this specialist — go-deep not needed)` and exit. The orchestrator only invokes you when at least one such finding exists, but be defensive.
- Investigation is bounded — don't spend tokens roaming the entire repo. Three to five greps + a couple of git-log lookups + reading the cited files is the right shape. If the calibration question can't be answered with those steps, recommend `REFRAME` and let the operator weigh in.

## [tests] findings

### Surveyed
- Prepared `just test` result artifact — missing locally; GitHub PR checks are passing, so no PR-related failure classification was available from scratch output
- `KeepMacAwakeTests` target wiring in `PhoenixTests` — clean
- Failed runtime toggle-on rollback coverage — clean
- Failed launch-from-persisted-true rollback coverage — clean
- Successful acquire, toggle-off release, and teardown coverage — see Finding 1
- `CountingUserDefaults` write-count assertions — see Finding 2

### Finding 1 — medium
Could the tests cover the success/release state transition, not just acquisition failure? Current tests exercise only `kIOReturnError`, while the feature’s core contract lives in successful `acquireAssertion`, `releaseAssertion`, and `teardown`. A regression that stops recording the returned assertion ID, never calls `IOPMAssertionRelease`, or leaves `hasAssertion` stale would pass automated tests and show up as the Mac still sleeping or an assertion lingering until process exit. Concrete seam: inject an `AssertionReleaser` closure or small assertion-client value beside `AssertionCreator`, then assert toggle-on and toggle-off/teardown behavior. Cost is one symmetric test seam, not conditionals or special cases.
Files: app/Phoenix/KeepMacAwake.swift:53, app/Phoenix/KeepMacAwake.swift:74, app/Phoenix/KeepMacAwake.swift:86, app/PhoenixTests/KeepMacAwakeTests.swift:28

### Finding 2 — nit
Under the Broken-Glass Test, can these tests assert the user-visible state instead of exact `UserDefaults` write counts? The assertions at lines 61 and 95 make a private implementation detail part of the contract; final `isEnabled`, final persisted value, and `acquireCallCount` already cover rollback plus no repeated acquire. Keeping the write-count contract makes harmless refactors fail and carries a custom `CountingUserDefaults` helper for one internal choreography check. The Concise Code remedy is to drop the exact write-count assertions/helper unless a single-write behavior is itself a product requirement.
Files: app/PhoenixTests/KeepMacAwakeTests.swift:61, app/PhoenixTests/KeepMacAwakeTests.swift:95, app/PhoenixTests/KeepMacAwakeTests.swift:106

**Calibration questions for go-deep investigation:**
- Will this feature’s core failures be user-visible at launch/toggle time? Yes: a missed release or stale assertion state maps directly to the Mac sleeping or an assertion lingering.
- Can the remedy stay to 1-2 behavior tests plus one small assertion/defaults seam, instead of broad test-target or UI automation churn?

### [tests] Finding 2 — FALSE POSITIVE
The cited `CountingUserDefaults` helper and line references do not exist in the current tree; `rg` finds no `KeepMacAwakeTests.swift` at all. This should not be raised as a brittle-test cleanup.

+
+    /// The connectors screen sizes its window to the measured content height
+    /// (reported via `InstallerContentHeightKey`), capped by the visible
+    /// screen so a long settings list falls back to scrolling inside the
+    /// existing `ScrollView` instead of pushing the window off-screen. The
+    /// remaining screens are intentionally taller than their content
+    /// (Spacer-filled splash layouts) and keep the design height of 530.
+    private func targetWindowHeight(for screen: InstallerScreen) -> CGFloat {
+        let cap = max(420, (NSScreen.main?.visibleFrame.height ?? 900) - 80)
+        if screen == .connectors, measuredContentHeight > 0 {
+            // `measuredContentHeight` is the ScrollView's inner content; add
+            // the window's titlebar plus the bottom-anchored DownloadBarView's
+            // measured height (zero when the bar isn't shown) so the bar
+            // doesn't cover the last settings rows.
+            return min(measuredContentHeight + 28 + measuredOverlayHeight, cap)
+        }
+        return 530
+    }
+}
+
+/// Carries the bottom-anchored `DownloadBarView`'s measured height up to
+/// `InstallerView` so the connectors-screen window can grow to keep the
+/// settings content above the bar (including the taller "retry" state).
+/// Reverts to zero when the bar isn't in the view tree (post-install).
+struct InstallerOverlayHeightKey: PreferenceKey {
+    static var defaultValue: CGFloat = 0
+    static func reduce(value: inout CGFloat, nextValue: () -> CGFloat) {
+        value = nextValue()
+    }
+}
+
+/// SwiftUI preference key carrying the measured intrinsic height of the
+/// active installer screen up to `InstallerView`, which drives the hosting
+/// `NSWindow`'s frame. Emitted by `SettingsView` (the only screen whose

+/// the splash screens, which use a design-set fixed height.

+    /// Releases the assertion deterministically before the app exits, so the
+    /// system can coalesce any pending sleep state at logout/shutdown without
+    /// waiting for process reaping. The kernel reclaims the assertion on
+    /// process exit either way; this is a courtesy, not a leak fix.
+    func teardown() {
+        releaseAssertion()
+    }

+                suppressApply = true
+                isEnabled = false
+                suppressApply = false

1:import Foundation
2:import IOKit.pwr_mgt
3:import Observation
5:/// Holds `kIOPMAssertionTypePreventSystemSleep` while the user has opted in, so
6:/// the system stays in Dark Wake and the OpenClaw VM keeps serving through
7:/// display sleep. On battery the kernel effectively downgrades the assertion to
8:/// idle-sleep-prevention, so a single assertion works in both power states;
9:/// draining the battery is the user's explicit choice when they toggle this on.
10:/// Clamshell sleep on a MacBook without an external display is still enforced
11:/// by the kernel and isn't reachable from a public API.
12:@Observable
13:@MainActor
14:final class KeepMacAwake {
15:    static let preferencesKey = "keepMacAwakeWhileRunning"
17:    private var assertionID: IOPMAssertionID = 0
18:    private var hasAssertion = false
19:    /// Set true while we're rewriting `isEnabled` from inside `applyEnabled` to
20:    /// revert a failed acquire — the recursive `didSet` reads this and bails.
21:    private var suppressApply = false
23:    var isEnabled: Bool = UserDefaults.standard.bool(forKey: KeepMacAwake.preferencesKey) {
24:        didSet { applyEnabled() }
25:    }
27:    init() {
28:        applyEnabled()
29:    }
31:    /// Releases the assertion deterministically before the app exits, so the
32:    /// system can coalesce any pending sleep state at logout/shutdown without
33:    /// waiting for process reaping. The kernel reclaims the assertion on
34:    /// process exit either way; this is a courtesy, not a leak fix.
35:    func teardown() {
36:        releaseAssertion()
37:    }
39:    /// Brings the held IOPMAssertion in line with `isEnabled` and persists the
40:    /// resolved value. If acquire fails, `isEnabled` is reverted to false so
41:    /// the toggle UI matches the actual sleep-prevention state.
42:    private func applyEnabled() {
43:        guard !suppressApply else { return }
44:        if isEnabled {
45:            if !acquireAssertion() {
46:                suppressApply = true
47:                isEnabled = false
48:                suppressApply = false
49:            }
50:        } else {
51:            releaseAssertion()
52:        }
53:        UserDefaults.standard.set(isEnabled, forKey: Self.preferencesKey)
54:    }
56:    private func acquireAssertion() -> Bool {
57:        guard !hasAssertion else { return true }
58:        var id: IOPMAssertionID = 0
59:        let reason = "Plow keeping Mac awake so the OpenClaw VM stays reachable" as CFString
60:        let result = IOPMAssertionCreateWithName(
61:            kIOPMAssertionTypePreventSystemSleep as CFString,
62:            IOPMAssertionLevel(kIOPMAssertionLevelOn),
63:            reason,
64:            &id
65:        )
66:        guard result == kIOReturnSuccess else {
67:            NSLog("[KeepMacAwake] IOPMAssertionCreateWithName failed: %d", result)
68:            return false
69:        }
70:        assertionID = id
71:        hasAssertion = true
72:        return true
73:    }
75:    private func releaseAssertion() {
76:        guard hasAssertion else { return }
77:        IOPMAssertionRelease(assertionID)
78:        hasAssertion = false
79:        assertionID = 0
80:    }
81:}

commit f60cdd31d430065d40cbd64a7546ab7e0da8b951
Author: swagatpatel <swagatpatel@users.noreply.github.com>
Date:   Wed Apr 29 11:18:36 2026 -0700

    feat: 1Password broker — host-side op integration for agent credential retrieval (#538)
    
    Host-side broker that lets an openclaw agent retrieve a user's 1Password credentials via the `op` CLI on the Mac host. No service account; uses the desktop app's biometric integration. Spike-quality — proves the architecture and surfaces productization gaps.
    
    ## What ships
    
    - Plowd broker module (`app/plowd/plowd/onepassword.py`) + three internal HTTP endpoints (`/internal/op/{whoami,list-logins,fetch-credential}`), bearer-auth gated.
    - `plow op-test` CLI for host-side broker smoke testing.
    - Openclaw plugin (`app/openclaw/plugins/onepassword/`) registering `onepassword_list_logins` and `onepassword_fetch_credential` agent tools.
    - SKILL.md teaching the agent the index → match → fetch pattern.
    - VM/Lima/Phoenix wiring to mount the new plugin alongside `plow-cli`.
    - CI: `just test-fast` / `just test-ci` now run `app/openclaw/plugins/*/index.test.js` via a new `test-openclaw-plugins` recipe (also covers previously-orphaned `plow-cli` and `guard` tests).
    
    ## Validation
    
    End-to-end: agent successfully filled login forms on `practicetestautomation.com` and on a real Amazon account using credentials from a real 1Password Personal vault. Plowd log audit confirmed zero credential leakage.
    
    ## Architectural note
    
    The spike's design exposes the credential index AND plaintext to the LLM context. 1Password's official [Agentic Autofill](https://developer.1password.com/docs/agentic-autofill/) explicitly rejects this shape. See [`docs/architecture/2026-04-27-onepassword-broker-spike-findings.md`](docs/architecture/2026-04-27-onepassword-broker-spike-findings.md) for paths forward — Path B (server-side URL match) is the recommended next architectural step.
    
    ## Out of scope (productize later)
    
    TOTP / non-Login categories, multi-account selection UX, vault filter, multi-candidate disambiguation, bundled `op` binary, index TTL/persistence. Encryption-at-rest is N/A — broker stores nothing.

commit 4f76c6f9ea67d6f2cbac2fc6f8df9515565a5ac2
Author: Sam Odio <sam@odio.email>
Date:   Sun Apr 26 07:56:09 2026 -0700

    fix(packaging): pin plowd dist-info in both validators (#492)
    
    * fix(packaging): tighten validator contract for plowd dist-info
    
    PR #490 fixed the regression that left packaged apps without plowd's
    dist-info (importlib.metadata.version("plowd") → PackageNotFoundError →
    plowd dies before binding the HTTP port). #491's review then surfaced a
    follow-on: both validators that gate "is this runtime complete" only
    checked for `site-packages/` as a directory, not for the dist-info inside
    it. So a future packaging regression that drops the install line would
    still pass validation and ship as a structurally-valid-but-unbootable
    bundle. This tightens both halves of that contract.
    
    - `plowd-validate-package`: add a `compgen -G` check for
      `site-packages/plowd-*.dist-info/METADATA` after the existing required-
      paths loop. Fails the validator with a specific error pointing at the
      missing metadata.
    - `Phoenix/DaemonClient.swift`: extend `missingRuntimePaths()` to enumerate
      `site-packages/` and report `site-packages/plowd-*.dist-info` when no
      `plowd-*.dist-info` directory is present. Skip the check when
      `site-packages` itself is missing — that's already reported and
      duplicating it would just be noise. Promoted from `private` to internal
      static so PhoenixTests can exercise it directly (mirrors the pattern
      set by `claimRuntimeLaunchIfNeeded` for #443).
    
    Tests:
    - `test_release_scripts.py`: behavioral test that builds a complete bundle,
      removes the dist-info, and asserts validate-package fails with a
      specific stderr message; static-text test that catches deletion of the
      check from the script. The shared `_create_minimal_valid_app_bundle`
      helper now stages a fake `plowd-0.1.1.dist-info/METADATA` so existing
      tests that exercise the validator continue to pass.
    - `DaemonClientMissingRuntimePathsTests.swift`: three cases covering
      missing dist-info, present dist-info, and the no-double-report rule
      when `site-packages` itself is gone.
    
    Both suites pass locally:
    - `pytest app/plowd/tests/test_release_scripts.py` — 17/17
    - `xcodebuild test -only-testing:PhoenixTests/DaemonClientMissingRuntimePathsTests` — 3/3
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(packaging): Swift validator must require METADATA, not just dist-info name
    
    Code-review feedback on PR #492 (Copilot inline): the original
    `missingRuntimePaths()` only matched the entry name `plowd-*.dist-info`,
    so an empty dist-info directory (or even a file with that name) would
    pass preflight even though `importlib.metadata.version("plowd")` would
    still throw at import. The bash sibling already requires a `METADATA`
    file inside the dist-info via `compgen -G "...METADATA"`, so this brings
    the two validators back into agreement on what "complete" means.
    
    The check now requires `plowd-*.dist-info/METADATA` to exist as a regular
    file (not a directory). Updated the existing "passes when present" test
    to actually write the METADATA file, and added a new edge-case test for
    the empty-dist-info path that catches the gap Copilot flagged.
    
    - 17/17 Python tests pass (`pytest app/plowd/tests/test_release_scripts.py`)
    - 4/4 Swift tests pass (`xcodebuild test -only-testing:PhoenixTests/DaemonClientMissingRuntimePathsTests`)
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * test(daemon-launch): stage plowd dist-info in fixture so it satisfies new strict gate
    
    CI exposed that DaemonLaunchEnvironmentTests.testPackagedDaemonLaunchConfigDisablesBytecodeWrites
    was setting up a runtime tree with python/plowd/site-packages but no
    plowd-*.dist-info — sufficient under the old loose contract, but the new
    missingRuntimePaths() check requires plowd-*.dist-info/METADATA, so
    packagedDaemonLaunchConfig() now throws runtimeIncomplete. Update the
    fixture to stage the dist-info + METADATA file so the test exercises the
    launch-config path that's actually under test.
    
    Local full suite: 177/177 pass.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * fix(app): serialize permission selection on MainActor to fix NSMenu crash
    
    DaemonClient is @Observable but not MainActor-isolated. applyPermissionSelection
    was async without explicit actor annotation, so it ran on a cooperative task
    thread when awaited from InstallerView.finalizePermissionsIfNeeded. Mutating
    @Observable properties off-main fires SwiftUI observation callbacks on the
    mutating actor, which can cascade into NSMenu rebuilds. NSMenu requires main
    thread — off-main cascades crash with '-[NSMenu itemArray]' NSAssertionHandler
    failures.
    
    The crash report shows two threads concurrently in applyPermissionSelection
    (one holding the SwiftUI observation lock while the other hits NSMenu) —
    the textbook signature of this bug.
    
    Annotating applyPermissionSelection + its callers (completePermissions,
    skipPermissions) with @MainActor serializes everything on the main thread.

    * fix: assert OwnerAllowFrom for plow-imessage direct messages so cron is available
    
    cron (and gateway, nodes) are owner-only tools in openclaw. Without an owner
    assertion, senderIsOwner is always false for plow-imessage sessions and these
    tools are stripped from the toolset before the model sees them.
    
    For direct plow-imessage messages the sender is always the account owner —
    plow-imessage is a personal 1:1 assistant and only the registered user can
    send messages to it. Pass OwnerAllowFrom: [normalizedFrom] in the inbound
    context for direct messages so openclaw can identify the sender as owner
    without requiring a wildcard in claw-config.json (which would be insecure).
    
    Group messages are unaffected — no owner assertion is made there.

    into Phoenix/Resources/{bin,share}. The Xcode Resources phase copies

    binary picks up the Developer ID + hardened runtime without extra work.

    clear LimaVMError.limactlNotBundled if the executable is missing. We
    never fall back to the system PATH. VZ backend needs nothing from
    libexec/lima/, so we skip the 33 MB krunkit driver and plugins.

    + templates 0.5 MB).

    * Install zstd in the guest before provisioning openclaw
    
    The Lima guest is Debian 12; the cloud image happens to include zstd but

    * Harden fetch-limactl: arch guard, durable cache, canary-verified staging
    
    Three review findings from 2a360c5:
    
    1. Arch hardcoding. Phoenix is Apple Silicon only, so fail loudly on
       anything but arm64/aarch64 instead of silently bundling an
       unlaunchable binary.
    
    2. Network at build time. Move the tarball cache from `.build/lima-cache/`
       (wiped by `git clean`) to `~/Library/Caches/co.plow/lima/` (override
       via PLOW_LIMA_CACHE_DIR). Once populated, the cache survives repo
       cleaning and worktree re-creation so clean checkouts no longer need
       GitHub reachability on every build. Bump curl retry tolerance
       (--retry 5 --retry-connrefused, three outer attempts) and print an
       explicit offline-bootstrap recipe if all attempts fail.
    
    3. Cache-hit integrity. Fast path now requires both the stamp AND a
       list of canary files — limactl, the Linux guestagent, and the two
       templates our lima.yaml inherits from (`_images/debian-12`,
       `_default/mounts`). A stale checkout missing only the templates
       re-stages from the durable cache instead of silently passing the
       build and failing at VM boot. Also declared the template canaries
       in the Xcode build phase outputPaths for DAG completeness.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Hermetic xcodebuild + race-safe limactl staging
    
    Two review findings from 3cb44ff:
    
    A. Concurrent-build race. The prior script wrote `${TARBALL_PATH}.tmp`
       with a fixed name and did a shell-level `mv NEW_DIR final-dir`, which
       (when the target exists) moves NEW_DIR *inside* final-dir rather than
       replacing it — reliably produced `Resources/bin/bin/limactl` under
       parallel invocations. Now: tarball downloads land in a per-process
       mktemp(1) file and rename atomically into the cache; staging runs
       under a mkdir-based advisory lock in the cache dir (with a 10-minute
       self-heal in case of crashes). Verified with 5 parallel cold
       invocations -- exactly one stages, the other four re-check under the
       lock and exit clean; no leaked stage dirs, no bin/bin, final shas
       match the pin.
    
    B. Network in the target build phase. Split fetch-limactl.sh into a
       default (download + stage) and `--verify` mode (canary-only, no
       network). The Xcode build phase now runs `--verify` and fails the
       build with an actionable error if staging is missing. Added a public
       `just fetch-limactl` recipe and wired it as a prereq on the private
       `xcode-build` recipe and the public `test` recipe, so every normal
       dev path (`just app build` / `up` / `test`) primes the staging area
       before xcodebuild runs. Verified with PATH=/tmp:/usr/bin:/bin (curl
       replaced with a honeypot) + deleted tarball cache: xcodebuild test
       passes on primed state, and fails with a clear "run just app
       fetch-limactl" message when the staged outputs are stripped. CI that
       invokes xcodebuild directly needs to run `just app fetch-limactl`
       as a prior step; the verify-mode error message says so.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Only the lock owner removes the staging lock on exit
    
    cleanup() was installed before the mkdir-acquire, so a waiter that timed
    out, got SIGTERM'd, or errored mid-loop would rmdir the active holder's
    lock directory -- reopening the race the lock was meant to close.
    
    Gate the rmdir behind an I_OWN_LOCK flag that flips to 1 only after the
    mkdir(2) acquire succeeds (including after a stale-lock self-heal where
    the rmdir + retry lands a fresh mkdir). Also trap INT and TERM, not just
    EXIT, so a SIGTERM'd waiter still runs cleanup -- but now that cleanup
    does nothing to the lock because the flag is 0.
    
    Verified: launched a simulated holder (manually-created LOCK_DIR),
    kicked off a waiter in the background, sent it SIGTERM. The holder's
    lock survived the interrupted waiter. Parallel cold-stage (5 waiters,
    1 holder) still produces one `staged Lima` log line, consistent final
    bytes, no leaked lock.

    * Add root .nvmrc; make app/justfile recipes fail on errors
    
    Two small dev-loop fixes:
    
    1. .nvmrc pinning Node 24 at the repo root so fnm/nvm/asdf users get
       the right runtime when they cd into a worktree. Opportunistic —
       no other activation hooks added.
    
    2. app/justfile's shell was "zsh -cu" (no -e), so backslash-continued
       recipes silently swallowed mid-chain failures. qa hit this with
       `just app build` returning 0 after plowd-stage-runtime errored out
       with "runtime directory is missing required Phoenix runtime paths".
    
       Fix: set shell := ["zsh", "-cue", "-o", "pipefail"]. The codebase
       was already defensively annotating soft-fail cases with `|| true`
       (e.g. osascript quits, lsof|xargs kill, hdiutil info) and using
       `grep ... || true` for grep-exits-1-on-no-match, which is strong
       evidence the maintainers had always intended errexit semantics.
    
       Scope: app/justfile only. The root justfile's multi-line recipes
       are either line-by-line (just handles errexit), have their own
       `#!/usr/bin/env bash\nset -euo pipefail` shebangs, or are single
       commands — none exhibit the same bug.
    
    Verified: with the new flag, temporarily renaming
    app/plowd/runtime/manifest.toml aside makes `just app build` fail at
    the plowd-stage-runtime step (exit 1) instead of swallowing the error
    and returning 0.

    * Task 7 regression fix: honor PLOW_VM_BUNDLE in pinnedArtifactFilename
    
    QA found that `just app up` (dev mode) was throwing
    `runtimeIncomplete(missing: ["openclaw tarball", "camoufox tarball"])`
    on cold boot, blocking Lima launch.
    
    Root cause: `pinnedArtifactFilename(for:)` (added in Task 7, 9ed3fda7)
    only looked in `cacheDir/<filename>` via `localPath(for:)`. It did not
    honor the `PLOW_VM_BUNDLE` env override. In dev mode `startDownloads`
    detects that env var and intentionally skips the download step, so
    Application Support's runtime-cache stays empty while the real tarballs
    sit at `app/vm/output/`. The sibling `imageCacheDirectory()` on the
    same class already handled this case; the two functions had drifted
    out of sync.
    
    Fix: resolve the containing directory via `imageCacheDirectory()` (which
    consults PLOW_VM_BUNDLE → envURL when set, falls back to cacheDir in
    prod), then verify sha256 of the candidate in that directory. Three-line
    change as qa suggested.
    
    Cross-mode behaviors:
    - **Dev** (PLOW_VM_BUNDLE=app/vm/output, tarballs staged there):
      imageCacheDirectory() returns envURL → candidate =
      envURL/<manifest-filename> → sha matches → returns filename. ✓
    - **Prod** (tarballs downloaded into runtime-cache):
      imageCacheDirectory() returns cacheDir after openclaw sha check →
      candidate = cacheDir/<manifest-filename> → sha matches → returns
      filename. ✓
    - **Still-downloading** (prod, downloads in flight):
      imageCacheDirectory() returns nil → pinnedArtifactFilename returns
      nil → stageImagesEnv throws runtimeIncomplete, correctly gating
      Lima launch. ✓
    
    Verified: `just app test` exit 0 (Phoenix suite passes).
    
    Observation in the neighborhood (not touched, out of scope): DaemonClient's
    `resolveOpenClawImageDirectoryForMounts` has its own dev-mode branch that
    hard-codes `<repoRoot>/app/vm/output` via resolveRepoRootURL, while
    `imageCacheDirectory` in RuntimeDownloadManager uses the PLOW_VM_BUNDLE
    env var. In `just app up` both resolve to the same dir since the recipe
    exports PLOW_VM_BUNDLE=$(cd vm/output && pwd), but the two sources of
    truth for the "dev images dir" remain duplicated. Worth unifying in a
    follow-up, but it's not what the regression needed.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Fix: move StartLimitIntervalSec=0 from [Service] to [Unit]
    
    `StartLimitIntervalSec` is a [Unit] directive in systemd — placing it
    under [Service] makes the parser log "Unknown key StartLimitIntervalSec
    in section [Service], ignoring" and silently drop the setting, which
    leaves the default 5-restarts-in-10s permanent-failure gate in place.
    
    QA caught this on Task 11 e2e: both `plow-openclaw.service` and
    `plow-camoufox.service` journals reported the "Unknown key" message, so
    the plan-review C2/I7 protection against Firefox-OOM burst failure has
    been inert since it landed. Moving the directive into [Unit] is the
    minimal fix in both unit definitions inside `provision-runtime.sh`.
    
    No post-fix `systemctl cat` evidence in this message because the new
    guest-side systemd state only appears after the next cold boot of the
    Lima VM (which rewrites the unit files from this script). QA will
    re-run the e2e pass and check the journal.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * C1 fix: cleanup keys on URL-basename, not synthetic name+version prefix
    
    The post-merge `cleanupStaleCacheEntries` built its keep-set as
    `"\(artifact.name)-\(artifact.version)"` — e.g. `openclaw-2026.4.14` —
    but cache filenames come from `localPath(for:)`, which pulls the basename
    of `artifact.url`, e.g. `openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.tar.zst`. The openclaw
    name does NOT start with that prefix, so once all downloads finished
    the just-verified tarball got swept into the trash. `imageCacheDirectory`
    and `pinnedArtifactFilename` then found nothing → prod boot regressed
    the moment the cleanup ran.
    
    Camoufox was a lucky survivor (its URL basename does start with
    `camoufox-135.0.1-beta.24`) — so this regression would only bite
    openclaw, and only after a successful download, which is what made
    it invisible to the warm-cache dev loop.
    
    Fix: key the cleanup on the exact URL-basename set. Extract a small
    `RuntimeCacheCleaner` helper so the logic can be unit-tested without
    spinning up a real RuntimeDownloadManager (URLSession + Bundle.main
    side effects). Cache-dir method becomes a thin wrapper:
    
        RuntimeCacheCleaner.prune(
            cacheDir: cacheDir,
            keepFilenames: RuntimeCacheCleaner.keepFilenames(for: manifest)
        )
    
    `keepFilenames` builds a Set by `URL(string: $0.url)?.lastPathComponent`,
    matching what `localPath(for:)` writes and what `verifySHA256` later
    reads. Dotfiles stay excluded for safety.
    
    Tests (new `RuntimeCacheCleanerTests`, 4 cases):
    
      1. testKeepFilenamesUsesURLBasename — documents the bugfix: the
         expected keep-set is `{openclaw-agent-*, camoufox-*}`, not the
         old synthetic `{openclaw-*, camoufox-*}` prefix pair.
      2. testPrunePreservesVerifiedCurrentArtifacts — REGRESSION GUARD.
         Pre-bugfix this failed (openclaw got swept).
      3. testPruneRemovesOlderVersionedTarballs — confirms older beta/
         point-release tarballs still get cleaned up.
      4. testPrunePreservesDotfiles — `.manifest-hash` and friends stay.
    
    Verified: `just app test` → exit 0; filtered xcodebuild run of the
    new class shows 4/4 pass in 5ms.
    
    IMPORTANT finding separately flagged to Task 10 (CI workflow):
    `.github/workflows/build-release-candidate.yml` still reads
    `openclaw_vm_artifact` + `app/vm/gatekeeper/manifest.toml`. Both refer
    to TOML keys / directories that don't exist on this branch. Nightly
    release gate is broken until Task 10 flips the reads at
    `openclaw_artifact` + `camoufox_image_artifact`. Deferred here per
    the merge-commit review.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Add plow-imessage ws node_module to test fixture (post-merge reconciliation)
    
    Main's PR #325 ("stage plow-imessage node_modules so ws resolves at runtime")
    added `openclaw/channels/plow-imessage/node_modules/ws/package.json` to
    the required-paths list in `plowd-validate-package`. The fake-runtime-tree

    * Shared compute_git_ref helper for OCI build scripts
    
    New helper at `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh`. Sourced by
    `build-agent-image.sh` (Task 4) and `build-camoufox-image.sh` (Task 5)
    so both OCI artifacts get a consistent short-ref suffix stamped into
    their filenames + manifest entries.
    
    Resolution order matches PR #297:
      1. `PLOW_GIT_REF` env var, verbatim — CI-pinned builds.
      2. `git rev-parse --short=7 HEAD`, with `-dirty` suffix if tracked
         files other than `app/vm/manifest.toml` differ from HEAD.
    
    The `:!app/vm/manifest.toml` pathspec is load-bearing: build scripts
    rewrite that manifest with the new sha256 / size / git_ref values
    right after the image is built, and without the exclude every
    subsequent build on the same commit would flip to `-dirty`.
    
    Untracked files don't trigger `-dirty` — `git diff HEAD` only sees
    tracked files. The comment calls that out so anyone adding a new
    Dockerfile/script remembers to commit first.
    
    Also updates `.gitignore`: the root has a broad `lib/` rule (Python
    packaging boilerplate — setup.py builds into `lib/`) which was silently
    hiding `app/scripts/lib/`. Added `!app/scripts/lib/` negation so the
    new helper + any future helpers in that dir are tracked.
    
    Verified:
      - `bash -n app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh` → no output, exit 0.
      - Smoke test 1 (plain): prints `aedbca6` followed by newline.
      - Smoke test 2 (`PLOW_GIT_REF=pinned123`): prints `pinned123`,
        skips git entirely.
      - Smoke test 3 (touch tracked pyproject.toml): prints `aedbca6-dirty`;
        after `git checkout --` revert, prints `aedbca6` again — exclude
        and dirty detection both working.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Stamp gitRef into openclaw OCI artifact name and manifest
    
    build-agent-image.sh now sources `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh`, computes a
    short ref via `compute_git_ref`, and names the output tarball
    `openclaw-agent-<version>.<gitref>.tar.zst`. After `docker save | zstd`,
    `sed -i.bak -e …` writes the new openclaw_artifact / sha256 / size /
    git_ref into `app/vm/manifest.toml`. Matches PR #297's "build script
    owns manifest writeback" convention. `trap 'rm -f "${MANIFEST}.bak"' EXIT`
    keeps SIGINT mid-sed from leaving a `.bak` behind.
    
    This commit also carries Task 2's schema edit (the two empty
    `*_git_ref = ""` lines in manifest.toml) — per plan directive the
    Task 2 stage rolls up here so there's no intermediate "fields present
    but empty" commit. `openclaw_git_ref` gets its real value written by
    the build in the same commit; `camoufox_image_git_ref` stays empty
    until Task 5 ships the parallel build-camoufox-image.sh change.
    
    Evidence from running `rm -f app/vm/output/openclaw-agent-*.tar.zst &&
    app/scripts/build-agent-image.sh` (2m 48s, docker+zstd):
    
        artifact=.../app/vm/output/openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.416f152-dirty.tar.zst
        sha256=2bbc14f94c6bcdaac0b9d717f6dfc3e34f336507407234808ac0c918cb6db443
        size=299100052
        git_ref=416f152-dirty
    
    `grep -E '^openclaw_(artifact|git_ref|sha256|size)' app/vm/manifest.toml`
    shows all four fields match the build output byte-for-byte. The
    physical tarball exists at the advertised path (299,100,052 bytes).
    
    The `-dirty` suffix is expected here: at `compute_git_ref` time
    `build-agent-image.sh` itself is modified from HEAD (it's being edited
    by this commit), which is exactly the signal the dirty detector is
    designed to surface. A clean rebuild from the final commit before
    ship will rewrite the manifest with a non-dirty ref; tasks 5/8/13
    will re-exercise the pipeline against whatever ref is current at
    that point.

    * Delegate manifest writes to per-image build scripts with cache-reuse gate
    
    Now that build-agent-image.sh (Task 4) and build-camoufox-image.sh (Task 5)
    each stamp their own manifest slice, the orchestrator only needs to
    decide "rebuild or reuse" per artifact and delegate. Stripped the
    ~60 lines of `set_manifest_string` / `set_manifest_int` awk helpers;
    sources `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh` for `compute_git_ref`.
    
    `maybe_build` gate replaces the old `[ ! -f "$OPENCLAW_PATH" ]` check
    with a two-condition test:
    
        pinned_ref == compute_git_ref()   AND
        file-exists( <output>/<pinned_name> )
    
    Either side going false → delegate to the child. This fixes the prior
    dev-loop footgun: a commit bump would produce a new gitRef in the
    manifest but the stale tarball under the *old* name might still be on
    disk, and the old existence-only check would falsely report "using
    existing artifact" and ship the wrong bytes.
    
    Evidence:
    
    Step 2 — first run (stale pinned refs 416f152/83f90c5 vs current
    9298cd3-dirty, both mismatch → build both):
        time app/scripts/build-runtime-artifacts.sh
        ...
        7:01.38 total  (docker build + `docker save | zstd -19` for both
        artifacts; ~300 MB openclaw and ~670 MB camoufox)
    
    Step 3 — immediate re-run (manifest now pins 9298cd3-dirty, tarballs
    present at pinned paths → reuse both):
        time app/scripts/build-runtime-artifacts.sh
        ==> reusing openclaw tarball: openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.9298cd3-dirty.tar.zst (git_ref=9298cd3-dirty matches HEAD)
        ==> reusing camoufox tarball: camoufox-135.0.1-beta.24.9298cd3-dirty.tar.zst (git_ref=9298cd3-dirty matches HEAD)
        ...
        0.065 total  (65 ms — no docker or zstd invocations, exactly two
        file-exists checks + a git rev-parse)
    
    Step 4 — manifest consistency: all 10 keys populated, both gitRefs
    converge to 9298cd3-dirty, no blank values.
    
    Per plan Step 5 this commit carries only build-runtime-artifacts.sh
    itself. Manifest writebacks (which the orchestrator no longer owns)
    stay in Tasks 4/5's commit authority.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Add gitRef-decode + instance-cleanup tests with non-#if-DEBUG debug seams
    
    Task 7 was largely a no-op for the cleanup *body* — plan Step 1 ships
    via merge (gitRef: String? present on RuntimeArtifact), Step 4's
    cleanupStaleCacheEntries body already landed in acc8ba9a (the C1 fix
    refactored the logic into the RuntimeCacheCleaner static helper and
    re-keyed the keep-set on URL basename). The missing pieces the plan
    still asks for on top of HEAD:
    
    1. gitRef decode tests (Step 2). New `RuntimeArtifactDecodingTests`
       class, two cases:
         - testRuntimeArtifactDecodesGitRef: explicit "gitRef": "abc1234"
           decodes to .gitRef == "abc1234".
         - testRuntimeArtifactDecodesMissingGitRef: omitted field decodes
           to .gitRef == nil (the `String?` is load-bearing — legacy
           manifests without the field must still parse).
    
    2. Instance-path cleanup test (Step 5). New
       `RuntimeDownloadManagerInstanceCleanupTests` class, one case:
       `testCleanupStaleCacheEntriesRemovesUnreferencedTarballs`. Drives
       the test via the public debug seams (see below), populates a tmpdir
       with one live/one stale/one dotfile entry, asserts the right
       three-way split post-cleanup. Complementary to
       RuntimeCacheCleanerTests, which exercises the static helper; this
       one covers the instance plumbing (stateQueue dispatch on
       debugSetManifest + private cleanupStaleCacheEntries path).
    
    3. Debug seams on RuntimeDownloadManager (Step 6). Added three:
         - init(cacheDir: URL) — test-only designated initializer so
           tests can aim at a scratch tmpdir instead of AppPaths.
           runtimeCacheDirectory().
         - debugSetManifest(_:) — injects a manifest without going
           through Bundle.main.
         - debugCleanupStaleCacheEntries() — invokes the private cleanup
           synchronously on stateQueue so tests observe the filesystem
           effect before assertions run.
    
    Per plan revision I7 these are NOT `#if DEBUG`-gated. PhoenixTests
    compiles against Release in CI archive builds / diagnostics-bundle
    repackaging; a symbol that vanishes under Release would break those
    paths. The overhead is a few bytes of metadata and one convenience
    init — fine to ship in release binaries. Doc comment on
    `init(cacheDir:)` spells this out for the next reader.
    
    Verified:
      - targeted `xcodebuild test -only-testing ...` on the three
        cleanup/decode classes → 7 tests pass in 15 ms.
      - `just app test` (full Phoenix suite) → exit 0 (2m 43s).
        (One pre-run codesign failure was artifact-dir pollution from an
        earlier xcodebuild invocation with a different PLOW_APP_NAME
        casing sharing the same derived-data path; clean rebuild after
        `rm -rf .build/xcode-derived-plow.vm-test` clears it.)

    * S3 upload: default bucket + gitRef overwrite guard
    
    Three changes to upload-runtime-artifacts.sh:
    
    1. S3_BUCKET / S3_PREFIX default to releases.plow.co / runtime (was:
       ERROR out if unset). Matches PR #297 — `just app runtime deploy`
       without env overrides is now the happy path.
    2. Collapse the duplicated OpenClaw / Camoufox blocks into a single
       `verify_and_upload "<key_prefix>"` helper. Net ~15 fewer lines;
       same two function invocations instead of two hand-rolled block
       copies.
    3. Overwrite-guard die message spells out the rationale: docker save
       is non-deterministic across machines, so an existing S3 object may
       not match this build's sha256. PR #297's hard-die semantics (no
       skip+log) is deliberately preserved per plan revision C1. Recovery
       instructions inline: bump HEAD, or `aws s3 rm` if the operator
       is certain the remote object is stale.
    
    Deliberate divergences from PR #297 (not hidden):
    - Single-manifest orchestration: PR #297 reads two TOMLs
      (vm/manifest.toml + vm/gatekeeper/manifest.toml); we collapsed to
      one during the Lima migration.
    - `PLOW_GIT_REF` env override honored in `lib/git-ref.sh` (Task 3)
      — CI/pinned-ref builds. Main's inline rev-parse had no override.
    - `lib/git-ref.sh` shared helper vs PR #297's inline git rev-parse
      in each build script. Readability.
    
    Wiring check (plan Step 3):
    
        AWS_PROFILE=__nonexistent__ app/scripts/upload-runtime-artifacts.sh
    
    produces, in order:
      1. "==> openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.b5f006a.tar.zst (sha256=...) verified"
         — proves manifest read + local sha256 verify both ran.
      2. "==> uploading openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.b5f006a.tar.zst to
         s3://releases.plow.co/runtime/openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.b5f006a.tar.zst"
         — proves upload_artifact entered the upload path (s3_exists
         returned false against the nonexistent profile).
      3. "The config profile (__nonexistent__) could not be found"
         — aws s3 cp fails on the bogus profile; script exits 255.
    
    End-to-end wire verified without touching real S3. The actual upload
    gets exercised in Task 13's release validation.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * refactor(plowd): migrate remaining SSH paths to limactl shell, drop vm-shell-key
    
    The OAuth flow (_run_oauth_flow) and the openclaw-gateway-restart path were
    still using raw SSH through the generated vm-shell-key after the user-visible
    shell launcher moved to limactl shell at 2ed76be2. Collapse both flows onto
    limactl shell so the key is no longer load-bearing.
    
    Changes:
    - Replace _build_ssh_command() with _build_limactl_shell_command() in
      app/plowd/plowd/main.py; both _run_oauth_flow() and
      _restart_openclaw_gateway() now invoke the VM via limactl shell. The PTY
      wrapper and stdin paste-back for the OAuth flow are preserved — only the
      host-to-guest transport changes.
    - Drop VM_SHELL_HOST, settings.vm_shell_port, and the unused
      PLOWD_VM_SHELL_HOST/PORT runtime-env exports.
    - Delete vm-shell key generation: AppPaths.vmShellPrivateKeyFile /
      vmShellPublicKeyFile, DaemonClient.ensureVMShellKeypair, and the now-orphan
      setPOSIXPermissions helper.
    - Update DiagnosticsBundlerTests to stop seeding / asserting on vm-shell-key;
      the elision behaviour is still covered by the other openclaw secrets.

    * fix(plowd): land vm-shell at /workspace instead of /
    
    The plowd-vm-shell launcher dropped the user at the ephemeral guest root,
    which is unhelpful for poking at the mounted worktree. Pass --workdir

    Follow-up ID: T2.
    
    * refactor(phoenix): unify dev-mode OpenClaw image directory resolution
    
    RuntimeDownloadManager.imageCacheDirectory() and
    DaemonClient.resolveOpenClawImageDirectoryForMounts() each computed the
    OCI tarball directory in dev mode with different logic — the download
    manager honored PLOW_VM_BUNDLE, while DaemonClient hardcoded
    <repoRoot>/app/vm/output. These agree under `just app up` (which sets
    PLOW_VM_BUNDLE to that same path), but diverge when a Debug .app is
    launched out-of-band from Xcode with only PLOW_REPO_ROOT set.
    
    Collapse onto a single source of truth: RuntimeDownloadManager. Its
    imageCacheDirectory() now consults a shared devImageOverrideDirectory()
    helper that first tries PLOW_VM_BUNDLE and then falls back to
    <PLOW_REPO_ROOT>/app/vm/output, only returning a directory that actually
    contains `.tar.zst` tarballs. startDownloads() uses the same helper so
    it skips downloads for either override consistently. DaemonClient now
    just delegates to imageCacheDirectory(), and the test fixture unsets
    PLOW_REPO_ROOT alongside PLOW_VM_BUNDLE to keep observation tests
    deterministic.

    * chore(phoenix): one-time cleanup of pre-Lima VZ disk artifacts on launch
    
    Existing users upgrading from the pre-Lima (VZ) runtime carry 200MB–1GB of
    dead disk that Lima never touches. Add a small idempotent cleanup that runs
    once per PhoenixApp.init(), targeting only paths wholly owned by the now
    deleted VMManager / GatekeeperVMManager:
    
      <appSupport>/vm/rootfs.img           — writable copy of the VZ OpenClaw disk
      <appSupport>/gatekeeper-vm-state/    — VZ Gatekeeper instance directory
      <appSupport>/gatekeeper-console.log  — VZ Gatekeeper serial-console log
    
    The live-Lima layout writes vm/lima.yaml + vm/provision-runtime.sh into the
    same `vm/` directory, so we delete the VZ-specific file rather than nuking
    the directory. Stale gatekeeper-vm-*.tar.zst tarballs in runtime-cache/ are
    already swept by RuntimeCacheCleaner.prune (anything not named in the live
    manifest goes), so they don't need an explicit entry.
    
    Safe for fresh installs (missing paths are a no-op) and for users who have
    already been cleaned. LegacyVZArtifactCleanup.run(appSupportRoot:) takes an
    explicit root so the behavior can be exercised against a tmpdir — three
    XCTests cover: fresh-install no-op (live lima.yaml preserved), stale-state
    removal (all three legacy paths deleted, lima.yaml preserved), idempotence.

    * VIP calendar lock: restrict VIP sessions to calendar-only tools (#377)
    
    * VIP calendar lock: restrict VIP sessions to calendar-only tools
    
    Two-layer enforcement:
    
    Layer 1 (prompt): When vip_context.sender_role is "vip", inject a
    [system] TOOL RESTRICTION block into the identity hint telling the
    agent it may only use plow_calendar_* tools and must refuse all other
    requests.
    
    Layer 2 (hard gate): GatewayPolicyEngine maintains a set of VIP
    session keys. When a VIP message arrives, channel.ts registers the
    session with plowd via POST /internal/gateway/policy/vip-session.
    evaluate_tool_call() checks the set and blocks any tool not in
    VIP_ALLOWED_TOOLS with "VIP sessions may only use calendar tools".
    
    The prompt handles the happy path (VIP asks nicely). The hard gate
    catches prompt bypass (VIP social-engineers past the instruction).
    
    Includes spec at features/vip-calendar-lock/spec.md.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Fix 4 Codex-flagged bugs in VIP calendar lock
    
    1. CRITICAL: Lock was on shared sessionKey — owner got locked out when
       VIP spoke in the same thread. Fix: replaced permanent session set
       with per-turn TTL lock (120s). Lock is set when VIP sends, expires
       after the agent turn completes. Owner messages don't set the lock,
       so owner always has full tool access.
    
    2. HIGH: Race condition — fetch() was fire-and-forget, tool call could
       bypass the lock. Fix: await the lock registration synchronously
       before dispatching to the agent. Added AbortSignal.timeout(5000).
    
    3. HIGH: Unauthenticated endpoint — /internal/gateway/policy/vip-session
       had no auth check. Fix: added Depends(_require_local_plow_auth) to
       both POST and DELETE endpoints.
    
    4. MEDIUM: No cleanup for stale VIP session keys. Fix: TTL-based expiry
       replaces the permanent set. _prune_vip_turn_locks() runs on every
       set, and is_vip_locked() checks expiry on read.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Fix owner lockout: scope VIP lock to sender phone, not session
    
    The lock key is now "vip:{sessionKey}:{senderPhone}" — the owner
    and VIP share the same sessionKey but different sender phones, so
    the owner is never locked out when they speak in the same thread.
    
    - Lock key includes vipContext.vip_phone in channel.ts and
      senderPhone in the plowd endpoint
    - Reverse index maps sessionKey → set of lock_keys so
      evaluate_tool_call (which only receives sessionKey) can still
      find active VIP locks
    - DELETE cleanup fires after agent response delivery (finally block)
      to eagerly release the lock; TTL remains as fallback
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Simplify VIP lock: sequential message processing guarantees correctness
    
    Codex flagged that evaluate_tool_call only receives session_key, not
    sender_phone, so the lock can't distinguish owner from VIP at tool-check
    time. The fix relies on OpenClaw's sequential message processing:
    
    1. VIP sends → channel.ts sets lock (sender_role === "vip") → agent
       processes → tools blocked → lock cleared (DELETE + TTL fallback)
    2. Owner sends → channel.ts does NOT set lock (sender_role !== "vip") →
       agent processes → tools allowed
    
    Messages in the same session are processed sequentially — the owner's
    message only starts after the VIP turn completes and the lock is cleared.
    
    Simplified from complex reverse-index approach to:
    - _vip_turn_locks: dict[session_key → (sender_phone, expires_at)]
    - set_vip_turn_lock(session_key, sender_phone) — records who locked it
    - clear_vip_turn_lock(session_key) — removes the lock
    - is_vip_locked(session_key) — checks existence + TTL
    
    The sender_phone is recorded for audit logging but not used in the
    check — the presence of a lock is sufficient because only VIP messages
    create locks.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Fix owner lockout: thread sender_phone through tool-check chain
    
    The lock check now compares the CURRENT sender against the STORED
    sender. Owner phone != VIP phone → owner is never locked.
    
    Chain: guard plugin extracts ctx.from → strips "plow-imessage:" prefix
    → sends as senderPhone in tool-check request → main.py passes to
    evaluate_tool_call(sender_phone=) → is_vip_locked(session_key,
    sender_phone) compares sender_phone == locked_sender → returns False
    if they don't match.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * Scope VIP calendar access: read=full, create=yes, update/delete=own events only
    
    VIP can read the full calendar (availability, search, today) and create
    events freely. But update/delete is restricted to events where the VIP's
    email is in the attendee list. Before any update/delete, the agent must
    search for the event and verify the VIP is an attendee.
    
    Replaces the previous "FULL calendar access" prompt with granular rules:
    - READ: always allowed, execute directly
    - CREATE: always allowed, VIP added as attendee automatically
    - UPDATE/DELETE: must verify VIP email in event attendees first
    - Refusal: "I can only modify events you're part of"

    * Use vip_phone (authoritative) instead of vip_email (caller-controlled)
    
    srosro blocker: vip_email was caller-controlled — the LLM could pass
    any email and bypass the attendee check. Fix: use vip_phone which is
    authoritative (from the webhook via the turn lock, not the LLM).
    
    The calendar router now:
    1. Receives vip_phone (not vip_email) in update/delete requests
    2. Looks up VipContact by phone from the database
    3. Reads the email from the VipContact record (server-derived)
    4. Uses that email for the attendee check
    
    The LLM cannot fake the phone because the policy engine verifies
    senderPhone matches the turn lock (which was set from the webhook).
    
    Note: VipContact.email column doesn't exist yet — VIP update/delete
    will return 403 "no email on file" until the migration is added.
    This is correct fail-closed behavior: the feature becomes available
    when the email column is added and populated.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Remove vip_phone/vip_email from tool interface entirely
    
    The authoritative VIP identity lives in the turn lock (from the
    webhook), not in tool params. No model-supplied value can be trusted.
    
    Fix: remove update/delete from VIP_ALLOWED_TOOLS until VipContact.email
    migration ships. The policy engine blocks them with "VIP sessions may
    only use calendar tools." This is correct:
    - No model-supplied identifier to bypass
    - No dead code path that always 403s
    - Clear message to the agent and VIP
    
    Removed from the entire stack:
    - vip_phone/vip_email from schemas, CLI, plugin, router
    - _VIP_ATTENDEE_REQUIRED_TOOLS and the param-checking logic
    - VipContact lookup and check_vip_attendee calls in router
    
    When VipContact.email migration ships, update/delete will be re-added
    with server-side attendee verification using the turn lock's
    senderPhone → VipContact.email (never from tool params).

    * hotfix(release): drop stale --gatekeeper-manifest flag (#390)
    
    * hotfix(release): remove stale gatekeeper manifest arg
    
    * docs(vm-publish): rewrite for Lima/OCI release flow
    
    * hotfix(release): preserve virtualization entitlement on bundled limactl
    
    plowd-beta-package-signed re-signs every nested Mach-O inside the staged app before signing the top-level app bundle. That re-sign loop was stripping the com.apple.security.virtualization entitlement from Contents/Resources/bin/limactl, which makes Virtualization.framework refuse to start the VZ VM on production installs.
    
    Fix it by signing the bundled limactl with a dedicated entitlements plist during the nested re-sign step so the virtualization entitlement is preserved in the final app bundle.
    
    * hotfix(vm): scope limactl list to target instance (multi-instance JSONL parse fail)
    
    * hotfix(plowd): reload openclaw gateway when config changes on upgrade
    
    * hotfix(plowd): fix openclaw gateway restart (use nerdctl restart, not sh kill)
    
    The old restart path shelled into the VM, found openclaw-gateway with pgrep, and sent SIGUSR1. In both dev and prod this was failing with 'kill: Operation not permitted', so config-change reloads never actually refreshed the running gateway process.
    
    Switch the restart path to 'nerdctl restart openclaw' inside the VM. That cleanly restarts the gateway container and forces OpenClaw to re-read openclaw.json.
    
    Safety:
    - If openclaw is running with stale config, nerdctl restart cleanly stops and starts the container, so the updated config is applied.
    - If openclaw is not running, nerdctl restart returns a non-zero error that the existing caller already treats as a warning-only restart failure; it does not change startup control flow.
    - If the VM is stopped, the limactl shell command still fails cleanly and the existing caller already logs and returns without escalating.
    
    * hotfix(plowd): use systemctl to restart openclaw (nerdctl restart corrupts task state) + unconditional restart on plowd startup
    
    Replace the limactl shell restart path from 'nerdctl restart openclaw' to 'systemctl restart plow-openclaw.service'. The nerdctl restart path was leaving containerd task state behind ('mkdir ... file exists') and sometimes dropping the openclaw container entirely, which kept production stuck degraded.
    
    Also restart openclaw unconditionally once during plowd lifespan startup after openclaw.json has been written. That closes the upgrade-path gap where the on-disk config already matches the desired config, so config-change detection does not fire and a stale gateway process never reloads.
    
    Safety:
    - If openclaw is running with stale config, systemd cleanly restarts the service and the gateway re-reads openclaw.json.
    - If openclaw is not running, systemctl starts the unit as part of restart.
    - If the VM is stopped, limactl shell fails cleanly and the existing warning-only handling remains in place.
    
    * hotfix(vm): preserve images.env during runtime-cache pruning
    
    * hotfix(vm): treat missing Lima instance as create-new
    
    Handle the specific limactl single-instance lookup failure for an absent instance as a structured nil result instead of a fatal command error. limactl list --format json <instance> returns rc=1 with empty stdout and stderr containing 'No instance matching ... found.' plus 'unmatched instances' when the instance does not exist.
    
    LimaVMManager.currentInstance() now accepts that exact outcome and lets LimaStartStrategy.resolve(instance: nil) proceed to .createNew. Other non-zero exits still throw normally. Adds a regression test for the absence signal.

    * fix(openclaw): expose bundled node_modules to agent scripts via NODE_PATH (#404)
    
    Agents that followed the browser-usage SKILL hit `MODULE_NOT_FOUND` on
    their first `require('playwright-core')`. Audit logs from a real
    session confirm the pattern:
    
        exec: node -e "const { firefox } = require('playwright-core'); …"
        -> Error: Cannot find module 'playwright-core'
           requireStack: [ '/workspace/[eval]' ]
    
    The agent recovered by `npm install playwright-core` in /workspace,
    which works but adds ~tens of seconds per use and clutters the
    workspace with a huge transitive tree.
    
    playwright-core is already shipped inside the container as a transitive
    dep of the `openclaw` npm package, at
    `/usr/local/lib/node_modules/openclaw/node_modules/playwright-core`.
    It's just not at a path Node's default resolver reaches from an
    agent-authored script whose cwd is /workspace.
    
    Set `NODE_PATH=/usr/local/lib/node_modules/openclaw/node_modules` so
    every transitive dep openclaw already bundles is resolvable from
    /workspace. NODE_PATH is additive after the script's own
    node_modules, so an agent that installs its own version still wins.
    This covers future skills that reach for other bundled modules without
    requiring per-module symlink maintenance.
    
    openclaw's own process is unaffected — it still resolves its deps
    through its package directory, which takes precedence over NODE_PATH.
    
    Co-authored-by: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * fix(test): capture startup timing writer at enqueue time to prevent double-fulfill crash
    
    appendStartupTimingLog was reading startupTimingTestingWriter inside the
    async block (at execution time). If the app called appendStartupTimingLog
    multiple times before a test installed its writer, all those queued items
    would later execute with the test writer and double-fulfill the
    XCTestExpectation, aborting via NSAssertionHandler.
    
    Fix: read the writer under the lock before dispatching so each call
    captures a snapshot of whoever the writer was at call time.
    
    Crash ref: StartupTimingLogTests.testAppendStartupTimingLogDispatchesWriterOffCallerThread
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Sonnet 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix: release lock before calling appendStartupTimingLog from appendStartupTimingStateLog
    
    appendStartupTimingStateLog held startupTimingLogLock while calling
    appendStartupTimingLog, which now also acquires the same non-recursive
    NSLock. This deadlocked the main thread, causing the XCTest process to
    hang for the full 332-second connection timeout before xcodebuild killed it.
    
    Fix: drop the lock and then call appendStartupTimingLog outside it.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Sonnet 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(test): drain write queue in installStartupTimingLogTestingWriter
    
    Cleaner fix for the double-fulfill crash: instead of capturing the writer
    at enqueue time in appendStartupTimingLog (which introduced a deadlock with
    appendStartupTimingStateLog), drain the serial write queue via sync {} before
    swapping in the test writer. This ensures items queued from app init run with
    the default file writer, not the test writer. Production code is unchanged.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Sonnet 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * chore(pre-commit): pin skeleton SHAs to force taxonomy reading on drift
    
    Replaces the blunt "block any USER.md / IDENTITY.md modification" rule
    with a content-based skeleton-drift check. Each pinned file has a SHA256
    stored in scripts/protected-skeleton-hashes.txt; the guard fails if the
    staged content doesn't match.
    
    There is no PLOW_GUARD_ALLOW override for skeleton-drift on purpose —
    updating the pinned hash IS the override, and it's visible to reviewers
    in the diff. The pin file's header points back to
    docs/architecture/file-taxonomy.md, so any skeleton change forces a pause
    to re-read the (a/b/c) taxonomy before proceeding.
    
    Side benefit: `pre-commit run --all-files` no longer false-positives on
    unchanged USER.md / IDENTITY.md. Only app/vm/manifest.toml still requires
    an override in that mode (still correct — intentional bumps are rare).
    
    HEARTBEAT.md stays as a path-based block (it's gitignored and has no
    canonical skeleton to pin).

    * fix(vm): add systemd-resolved FallbackDNS for Lima usernet flakes
    
    Lima's default /etc/resolv.conf points at a single nameserver
    (192.168.5.2, the `limactl usernet` gateway process). When usernet
    stumbles, DNS dies inside the VM and every outbound LLM call from the
    openclaw container fails. Drop-in form so Lima's managed base config
    is untouched; FallbackDNS is only consulted when the primary is
    unreachable, so steady-state behavior is unchanged.
    
    Incident context and options for the four latent bugs this cascade
    surfaced (duplicate cron names, no circuit-breaker, HTML-in-iMessage,
    no out-of-band control) are documented in
    docs/architecture/2026-04-22-heartbeat-cascade.md.

    * fix(vm): stop orphan Lima VM at launch to refresh virtiofs mounts
    
    On macOS Cmd+Q the app schedules vmManager.stop() on a fire-and-forget
    Task from applicationWillTerminate, which the process often exits before
    completing — and force-quit / crash skip the notification entirely. A
    reinstall of Plow.app while the VM is running leaves virtiofs handles
    pointing at the old bundle inode: /plow-imessage, /plugin, /cli-packages
    appear empty inside the guest even though the host paths have files, and
    the openclaw container crash-loops on config validation (plugin path not
    found). The UI sits at "Warming up Plow" forever.
    
    Fix: on the first start() call per process, if the instance is running
    it's an orphan from a prior session, so stop it before proceeding. The
    normal strategy resolution then picks resumeStopped and the subsequent
    boot rebinds virtiofs to the current bundle.

    * fix(test): make installStartupTimingLogTestingWriter atomic to prevent XCTestExpectation over-fulfillment
    
    The previous implementation drained the write queue with sync{} then
    installed the writer in a separate lock section. New async items from
    background DaemonClient polls could slip into the queue between the
    drain and the install, fire with the test writer, and call
    expectation.fulfill() more times than expectedFulfillmentCount, which
    aborts via NSAssertionHandler (SIGABRT on co.plow.startup-timing-log).
    
    Moving the lock + install inside the sync block makes drain-and-install
    atomic: no item queued concurrently can execute between them.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Sonnet 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(vm): run provisioner on every boot so drift fixes apply without a VM reset
    
    Lima mode: system runs the provisioner only at instance creation. That
    means every shipped change to provision-runtime.sh — notably the DNS
    drop-in added in 972ee374 — silently skips existing installations. The
    user-visible symptom: we ship a fix, users upgrade the app, nothing
    improves until they manually rm -rf the VM support dir.
    
    Switch the provisioner to mode: boot and guard the two expensive steps
    (daemon-reload, containerd restart) behind a content-hash stamp over
    the written systemd unit files. Steady-state re-runs are sub-second
    no-ops; a unit-file change in a future release triggers a one-time
    reload. Without the guard, containerd would restart on every VM boot
    and briefly kill openclaw/camoufox before Restart=always brought them
    back — needless downtime.

    * fix(vm): re-exec provisioner under bash; guard containerd restart
    
    PR #__ flipped the provisioner from `mode: system` → `mode: boot` so
    drift fixes land on reboot instead of silently skipping existing
    installs. Two bugs surfaced on the first boot under `mode: boot`:
    
    1. Cloud-init's `bootcmd` runs the script inline via `/bin/sh` (dash on
       Debian), not by exec'ing the shebanged file. Dash chokes on
       `set -o pipefail` with exit 2, aborting the provisioner before any
       systemd unit is written. VM stays half-provisioned, app loops forever
       on `Failed to start plow-camoufox.service: Unit ... not found`.
       Fix: wrap the whole script body in `exec /bin/bash <<'GUARD'...GUARD`.
       /bin/sh runs the wrapper, replaces itself with bash, bash honors
       pipefail + bashisms (`[[ ]]`, `$'...'`, process substitution). Env
       vars Lima sets in the params.env preamble are inherited across exec.
    
    2. `systemctl restart containerd.service` lives in the unit-file-hash
       conditional and used to run unguarded. Under `mode: boot`, Lima's
       own `40-install-containerd.sh` doesn't run until the later `runcmd`
       phase — so on first boot containerd isn't installed yet and the
       restart returns exit 5 ("not installed"). `set -e` aborts the
       script before the stamp file is written, so boot 2 re-runs the
       whole path. Fix: presence-check the containerd unit before restart,
       matching the pattern already used for systemd-resolved above.
       Skipping on first boot is safe — Lima starts containerd fresh with
       the DNS drop-in we already wrote.
    
    Also: AGENTS.md gains a "Installing a local build over /Applications/
    Plow.app" runbook. macOS `cp -R src.app dst.app/` nests rather than
    replaces when dst exists, and `RuntimeDownloadManager.cleanupStaleCache
    Entries()` prunes cache files not in the *running* app's manifest — so
    you must kill Plow before ditto'ing the new bundle, and stage any
    locally-built tarballs *after* the install.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * feat: upgrade openclaw 2026.4.14 → 2026.4.21 (fixes #412)
    
    Adopts upstream openclaw/openclaw PR #69336 (commit 8a2d7f2), which
    changes the `openai-codex` provider base URL from
    `https://chatgpt.com/backend-api` to `https://chatgpt.com/backend-api/codex`.
    
    Root cause of #412: OpenAI removed the `/backend-api/responses` alias on
    chatgpt.com server-side. The OpenAI SDK appends `/responses` to the
    configured baseUrl, so openclaw's prior baseUrl resolved to
    `/backend-api/responses` and hit a Cloudflare 403 HTML block page. The
    SDK's error classifier surfaced the HTML body as either
    "⚠️ API rate limit reached. Please try again later." (the bundled
    `RATE_LIMIT_ERROR_USER_MESSAGE`, matched by HTTP-status shape) or raw
    CSS from the CF challenge page (sanitizer pattern-miss). From the
    user's perspective the agent looked rate-limited while `codex --yolo`
    on the same account kept working — the fingerprint differs per client,
    but the actual failure was the dead path, not bot detection.
    
    Upstream fix points requests at `/backend-api/codex/responses` directly,
    which OpenAI keeps working. Verified by the commit author with live
    curl using the stored OAuth token: new path returns HTTP 200 streaming
    SSE, old path returns HTTP 403 HTML.
    
    Artifact values stamped via `OPENCLAW_VERSION=2026.4.21 PLOW_GIT_REF=
    acd8cc7 app/scripts/build-agent-image.sh` on an M-series host:
    
    - openclaw-agent-2026.4.21.acd8cc7.tar.zst
      sha256 4883fe9d…ca0f64, 265,386,127 bytes (vs 4.14's 288,958,699)
    
    The tarball is NOT yet uploaded to releases.plow.co. `just runtime
    deploy` must run before this merges to main, otherwise downstream users
    boot with a stale cache and get `Runtime artifact openclaw failed`.
    
    No openclaw plugin-SDK breaking changes surfaced in the channel
    typecheck on this 4.14 → 4.21 jump (contrast: 3.12 → 4.12 in #283
    needed three symbol renames).
    
    Full investigation, evidence, misclassification mechanism, and the
    options/decisions considered — see
    docs/architecture/2026-04-23-openai-codex-cloudflare-challenge.md.
    Closes cncorp/plow#412.

    * fix(vm): actually-working containerd guard + --no-block target + host-visible provisioner log
    
    Three fixes falling out of first-boot testing of commit 1c9e449c:
    
    1. `systemctl list-unit-files <unit>` returns exit 0 even when the unit
       is absent — it prints "UNIT FILE STATE" header + "0 unit files
       listed" footer and exits cleanly. The containerd presence check I
       wrote in 1c9e449c was therefore a no-op; the restart still fired on
       first boot, returned exit 5 ("not installed"), and `set -e` aborted
       the script. Switched to `systemctl cat`, which exits non-zero when
       the unit file can't be resolved.
    
    2. `systemctl start plow-runtime.target` blocked waiting for its
       Wants=plow-openclaw.service dependency to go active, which in turn
       waits on containerd (still pending install by Lima's runcmd on
       first boot). Blocking + `set -e` meant cloud-init bootcmd never
       finished → sshd never came up → "Warming up Plow / Waiting for
       operator" forever, with zero actionable logs on the host side.
       Added `--no-block` so systemctl returns immediately; systemd's
       Restart=always on plow-openclaw brings the container up after Lima
       installs containerd a few seconds later.
    
    3. `startup_log` now mirrors every line to `/vm-logs/provision-runtime.log`.
       That directory is virtiofs-mounted from the host's
       `~/Library/Application Support/co.plow.app/vm-logs/`, so the full
       provisioner timeline is readable from the host even when the guest
       has no working SSH (today's failure mode — diagnosing required
       manually extracting the inlined bootcmd from `/mnt/lima-cidata/user-data`
       after stopping + restarting the VM). A `trap ... EXIT` at the top
       captures the final rc, so a failed-with-`set -e` abort leaves a
       clear "exit rc=N" on the final line.
    
    All changes in `app/vm/provision-runtime.sh` — (b) our wrapper code,
    no (a/c) paths touched. 24 insertions, 5 deletions.
    
    Verified on a fresh VM with the updated build: `cloud-init status`
    reports `done` (was `error` on every prior boot), plow-openclaw reaches
    `active` 66s after launch, zero manual intervention.

    * docs(agents): steer agent to pick the right cron scheduler + flag injection risk
    
    The two schedulers are drastically different but trivially confusable:
    `crontab` runs pure Python in the VM at $0/fire, deterministic; `cron.add`
    fires a full agent turn (5k–150k tokens, non-deterministic) and puts
    anything the agent reads that turn onto the prompt-injection surface.
    
    Agent was already aware of the two paths but wasn't surfacing cost /
    risk tradeoffs to users when creating schedules. Seven lines in
    AGENTS.md §Tooling inject the decision rule into every session via the
    bootstrap file.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(vm): force VM recreate on bundle-swap (Sparkle / DMG / dev rebuild)
    
    When the installed app bundle is replaced while Plow is running — Sparkle
    auto-update, manual DMG drag-replace, or a dev `just build` — the Lima VM
    keeps its existing virtiofs mounts pointing at the *prior* bundle's
    inodes. The install unlinks those inodes; the VM sees /plow-imessage,
    /plugin, /cli-packages as empty; openclaw's plugin loader fails with
    "plugin path not found: /plow-imessage/dist" and the systemd unit
    crash-loops. There is no in-VM remediation — Lima has to be told to
    recreate the instance so cidata + virtiofs rebind to the current bundle.
    
    Today's manual workaround is `limactl delete -f plow-runtime-co-plow-app`
    (documented in AGENTS.md). Real users won't run that — they'll see
    "Warming up Plow / Waiting for operator" forever after every Sparkle
    update and assume the app is broken.
    
    Detection signal: SHA-256 of `Contents/MacOS/Plow`. Changes on every
    real rebuild (Swift compilation artifacts always vary); reinstalling
    byte-identical bytes leaves the hash unchanged so we don't recreate
    spuriously. Costs ~200 ms at launch on a ~4 MB Release binary.
    
    Flow:
    1. `LimaVMManager.start()` computes the current binary's SHA-256.
    2. Reads the last-known fingerprint from
       `~/Library/Application Support/co.plow.app/vm/last-bundle-fingerprint`.
    3. If both present and different AND a VM exists → `limactl delete -f`
       *before* the existing strategy resolution, so the strategy then
       takes the `createNew` branch and Lima generates fresh cidata.
    4. Records the new fingerprint only after a successful start (so a
       failed start leaves the prior marker and the next launch retries).
    
    Coverage:
    - Sparkle auto-update: binary changes → recreate ✓
    - Manual DMG / ditto over running app: binary changes → recreate ✓
    - Fresh install (no prior VM): no-op delete + createNew ✓
    - Reopen same install: hash matches → no recreate ✓
    - Dev `just build` (any code change): binary changes → recreate ✓
    - Plow restart of byte-identical bundle: hash matches → no recreate ✓
    
    Cost on a triggered recreate: re-loading openclaw OCI from the cached
    host tarball (~30s) + Lima's runcmd reinstalling containerd (~10s).
    No host-side state lost — agent sessions, auth profiles, cron, and all
    of `/config` live in virtiofs-mounted host paths.
    
    8 BundleFingerprintTests cover SHA correctness (known vector for "abc"),
    missing-file → nil, content-change → different hash, byte-identical →
    same hash (the no-spurious-recreate guarantee), record/read round-trip,
    nested-parent-dir creation, whitespace trim, empty-file → nil.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * feat(ui): finer-grained warmup sub-phases under "Warming up Plow"
    
    Before this change, everything from "gateway process up" to "openclaw
    container connected" collapsed into a single `.waitingForOperator`
    sub-label. That phase regularly holds for ~80 s on first boot (VM
    creating fresh containerd, openclaw OCI re-loading, crashloop retries
    until containerd is live), so users saw an indefinite-looking spinner
    with no indication of forward progress. Today's user report: "UGH
    still waiting for operator?! still hanging??"
    
    Phoenix already gets rich state from plowd's `/status` payload
    (`gateway.{running, node_running, operator_running, operator_connected}`)
    but only read two of the four booleans when deriving the phase. Wire
    the remaining two in and split `.waitingForOperator` into the sub-stages
    they actually distinguish:
    
      running=false                                        → waitingForGateway
      running=true, node_running=false                     → startingAgentNode   (new)
      node_running=true, operator_running=false            → startingOperator    (new)
      operator_running=true, operator_connected=false      → waitingForOperator  (reworded)
      operator_connected=true                              → ready
    
    The `.waitingForOperator` label also changes from "Waiting for operator"
    to "Connecting to agent container (first launch can take 1–2 min)" so
    the longest phase sets expectations instead of implying a hang.
    
    The cascade lives as a pure function `StartupPhase.warmupPhase(...)` —
    10 unit tests cover every combination plus the ready short-circuit.
    DaemonClient calls it per `/status` poll; the same call site that
    previously had an if/else on two booleans.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * test(phoenix): update StartupPhase subLabel assertions after rename
    
    cab6e00e reworded `.waitingForOperator` from "Waiting for operator" to
