    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(phoenix): drain startup-timing queue before clearing testing writer
    
    Asymmetric race with `installStartupTimingLogTestingWriter` that caused
    `just test` to SIGABRT at shutdown on otherwise-green runs (crashed
    thread `co.plow.startup-timing-log`, `std::terminate` via NSException
    from dispatch callout).
    
    `appendStartupTimingLog` captures the writer under lock then calls it
    outside the lock:
    
        startupTimingWriteQueue.async {
            lock()
            let writer = startupTimingTestingWriter ?? default
            unlock()
            writer(formatted)        // ← captured closure called here
        }
    
    A block in that read-then-call window survives the subsequent main-thread
    tearDown that nils the writer. The block's *local* reference to the test-
    installed closure still points at the old closure, which captures
    `XCTestExpectation`s that XCTest has now torn down. `.fulfill()` on a
    deallocated expectation throws an NSException; the exception escapes the
    dispatch callout → `std::terminate` → SIGABRT. Production never hits
    this because `defaultStartupTimingFileWriter` captures no test state.
    
    `installStartupTimingLogTestingWriter` already does the right thing —
    wraps the state change in `startupTimingWriteQueue.sync { ... }` so
    all prior async blocks have completed (including their `writer()` call)
    before the new writer is swapped in. `resetStartupTimingLogTestingHooks`
    was asymmetric: it just grabbed the lock and nilled, leaving queued
    blocks to execute against state XCTest had already released.
    
    Fix mirrors the install path: do the clear inside a `sync` block on the
    serial write queue. After this returns, no pending block can still be
    holding a captured reference to the test-installed writer.
    
    4 lines. Same pattern, same reasoning, same lock scope — only the
    outer sync wrapper is new.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    All (c) user state is on host-side virtiofs mounts; the VM filesystem
    holds no user-valuable data, so a limactl delete + re-provision is safe.

    * test(phoenix): tolerate concurrent writer fulfillments in startup-timing test
    
    The test installs a writer that fulfills two XCTestExpectations and
    explicitly logs once. But `appendStartupTimingLog` is module-level
    state — *any* concurrent call from the test host (e.g. the SwiftUI
    PhoenixApp lifecycle, or `appendStartupTimingStateLog` reacting to a
    DaemonClient state change during the 2-second wait) also runs the
    installed writer. Each extra invocation re-fulfills the expectations.
    With `assertForOverFulfill` defaulting to true, the second `fulfill()`
    throws NSException, escapes the dispatch callout, and SIGABRTs the test
    runner at shutdown.
    
    Companion to 1f30686c (drain queue before clearing testing writer).
    That fix prevents use-after-tearDown; this fix prevents over-fulfill
    during the drain.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(test): root scenarios shared_dir under $HOME so it propagates via Colima
    
    `just test` had been creating the fake-openclaw token-handoff dir under
    ${TMPDIR:-/tmp}, which on macOS resolves to /var/folders/.../T. Colima
    doesn't share /var/folders by default — only $HOME — so the bind mount
    into fake-openclaw fell through to an empty per-container ext4 directory.
    The host writes the token to `$shared_dir/token`; the container sees an
    empty `/shared`. fake-openclaw's `resolve_token()` polls `/shared/token`
    for TOKEN_FILE_TIMEOUT (60s) and never enters its poll loop. Test
    inbounds reach the API with no agent registered → API sends the canned
    "Unable to reach your agent" outbound → `wait_for_reply(contains="data")`
    times out at 30s.
    
    Why it worked before: Docker Desktop's default file-sharing covers
    /var/folders. Tests pass on Desktop and silently fail on Colima.
    
    Verified by reproducing both states with a one-shot alpine container:
    
      /var/folders/...  →  bind mount type ext4, /shared empty
      $HOME/.cache/...  →  bind mount type virtiofs, file content visible
    
    Switch to $HOME/.cache (XDG-style, honors $XDG_CACHE_HOME). Works under
    both Colima ($HOME-only default) and Docker Desktop (sharing-everything
    default). No compose.test.yaml change needed — the path flows through
    SCENARIO_SHARED_DIR already.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * fix(vm): recreate existing VM when no last-known fingerprint
    
    Users upgrading from a build that predates BundleFingerprint tracking
    (or whose first start aborted before recording one) land in start()
    with `lastFingerprint == nil`. The previous bundle-swap detection
    required both fingerprints to be non-nil, so the existing VM was
    silently preserved — whatever state it was in.
    
    Observed outcome: a user on srosro/released-main whose VM was
    provisioned during the 1c9e449c→cf2a44f5 containerd-guard bug window
    ended up with plow-openclaw.service declaring Requires=containerd.service
    but with containerd.service absent. `systemctl restart
    plow-openclaw.service` returned rc=5 ("Unit containerd.service not
    found") and plowd retried forever — the Plow app stuck on "Warming
    up Plow / Waiting for operator".
    
    Extract the recreate decision into BundleRecreateDecision so it's
    unit-testable, and add the new trigger: existing VM + no recorded
    fingerprint → force-delete. Upgraders get a clean VM on their first
    launch of a fingerprint-aware build; fresh installs are unaffected
    (no existing VM, hits createNew).
    
    Also log the fingerprint decision on every start() call (not only
    on the recreate branch) so future "why did we keep this user's
    broken VM?" questions are answerable from logs alone.

    * fix(vm): call vmManager.start() unconditionally on every launch
    
    Users installing a new build (DMG or Sparkle) while the previous
    build's Lima VM was still running hit "Warming up Plow / Connecting
    to agent container" indefinitely. Inside the VM, plow-openclaw.service
    crash-looped on "plugin path not found: /plow-imessage/dist" — virtiofs
    still held handles to the replaced bundle's now-unlinked inodes, so the
    mount appeared empty to the guest. plowd's gateway-operator kept
    retrying :18789 with connection-refused every 10s and the UI never
    progressed.
    
    The orphan-stop (807f9e11) and bundle-fingerprint recreate (ab36036d,
    20aa7b1e) safeguards for this exact scenario all live inside
    LimaVMManager.start(). ensureDaemonRunningIfNeeded gated the call on
    `if !vmManager.isRunning()`, so the entire safeguard path was skipped
    whenever the prior session's VM was still up — which is precisely the
    "upgrade while running" case they were written to handle. app.log
    confirms: zero `bundle-fingerprint` decisions recorded across many
    launches; at the user's 19:14 launch the only marker was
    `vmManager.start skipped alreadyRunning=true`.
    
    Call vmManager.start(config:) unconditionally and let it decide.
    LimaStartStrategy.reuseRunning already returns after a fast
    waitForReady for the healthy running-VM case, so there is no cost
    to the common path. Directory creation and host-share manifest
    rewriting are also now unconditional — all idempotent and cheap, and
    matching the new bundle's configuredHostShares is the whole point on
    the upgrade path.
    
    Add a source-level regression test that fails if the
    `if !vmManager.isRunning() { ... vmManager.start(... } `pattern
    reappears in DaemonClient.swift. A full behavior-level test would
    require protocol-izing LimaVMManager and adding DI through
    DaemonClient's init; worth doing eventually but too invasive for this
    fix. The source-inspection test directly encodes the architectural
    invariant ("vmManager.start is the single authoritative entry point;
    no caller gates it externally") and has already prevented the bad
    shape from creeping back in during local refactors.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * refactor(vm): extract VMStartupOrchestrator + LimaVMManaging protocol
    
    Follows up on the previous commit's one-line guard removal with the
    structural fix. The 2026-04-23 "Warming up Plow" hang was possible
    because DaemonClient could gate `vmManager.start(config:)` on
    `vmManager.isRunning()`, bypassing the orphan-stop and
    bundle-fingerprint recreate safeguards that live inside start(). This
    commit makes that bad shape architecturally unrepresentable and
    replaces the source-inspection regression test with real behavior
    coverage.
    
    LimaVMManaging protocol (in LimaVMManager.swift) names the four
    members DaemonClient depends on: onPhaseChange, start, stop,
    isRunning. Docstrings state the invariant ("callers must not gate
    start() on isRunning()"). LimaVMManager conforms unchanged.
    
    VMStartupOrchestrator (new file) owns the "prepare dirs, resolve host
    shares, write manifest, call vmManager.start" flow that used to live
    inline in ensureDaemonRunningIfNeeded. Holds `any LimaVMManaging` and
    never queries isRunning() — the buggy pattern is literally uncodable
    here because the reference doesn't exist. The healthy running-VM case
    is LimaStartStrategy.reuseRunning's concern and returns in
    milliseconds.
    
    DaemonClient now holds `any LimaVMManaging` (optional init parameter
    for DI), instantiates VMStartupOrchestrator with closures that keep
    the remaining couplings (resolveOpenClawLimaConfigURL, Plow sidebar
    icon) on the caller side. HostShare and ConfiguredHostShare move
    to VMStartupOrchestrator.swift as internal types. The private
    writeHostShareManifest is now a static on the orchestrator. 112
    lines out of DaemonClient, 70 in (net -42).
    
    VMStartupOrchestratorTests replaces the source-inspection test with
    six behavior tests against a FakeLimaVMManager that records
    interactions: start is always invoked; start is invoked even when the
    fake reports isRunning=true AND isRunning is never queried by the
    orchestrator; host shares resolve; manifest TSV is written; the
    "plow"-share callback fires exactly once; start errors and config
    resolution errors propagate. The critical invariant (start() is
    called, isRunning is not consulted) is now proven by test, not by
    grepping source for a bad pattern.
    
    The six remaining vmManager.isRunning() call sites in DaemonClient
    are untouched — they gate actions that need a running VM (browser
    config refresh, camoufox start, post-stop cleanup), which is a
    legitimate use. Only the start-gating pattern is the bug.
    
    just test passes on macOS incl. test-fast (Python + Phoenix XCTests)
    and test-scenarios (LLM judge + via-twin gmail/slack).

    * fix(daemon): clear runtimeLaunchState on every launch exit path (#443) (#449)
    
    * fix(daemon): clear runtimeLaunchState on every launch exit path (#443)
    
    Pair runtimeLaunchState transitions with the claim/finish lifecycle.
    Previously the `.launching → .idle` transition lived only at the deep
    success point inside waitForDaemonReady(), which polls for 45s. When the
    gateway took longer than that to report ok (first install, VM warmup on
    slower Macs), the wait loop timed out and returned; the periodic status
    poll later flipped isConnected = true but never touched runtimeLaunchState,
    leaving isRuntimeLaunchInProgress stuck at true forever.
    
    Symptom: in StatusView's tools menu, "Restart Plow" (gated only on
    isRuntimeLaunchInProgress) and the OpenClaw Dashboard/Shell entries
    (gated on !isConnected || isRuntimeLaunchInProgress) were grayed out even
    though the Plow Starter icons — which don't check this state — worked
    fine. Reported on M3 Air / Tahoe 26.4.1.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(daemon): guard launch-state cleanup against newer claims + add tests
    
    Addresses PR #449 review findings:
    
    1. Race (medium): the async cleanup Task in finishClaimedRuntimeLaunch
       was unversioned, so under adverse scheduling a stale cleanup from an
       older launch could clobber a newer claim's .launching back to .idle.
       The cleanup now re-reads isLaunching (the synchronous gate a new claim
       sets before scheduling its own .launching write) via a small sync
       helper and skips the write if another launch is already in flight.
       Extracted isAnotherLaunchInFlight() to keep NSLock out of async scope
       (Swift 6 warns otherwise).
    
    2. Regression tests (low): made claim/finish internal and added
       DaemonClientLaunchStateTests with two tests:
         - testFinishClaimedRuntimeLaunchClearsLaunchingState: the #443
           regression — would have caught the original stuck state.
         - testFinishDoesNotClobberNewerClaim: pins the race fix above.

    * fix(guard): log success=false for plow_cp timed_out/denied/failed (#466)
    
    * fix(guard): log success=false for plow_cp timed_out/denied/failed
    
    The guard plugin inferred success solely from `event.error`, which is only
    set when a tool throws. plow_cp returns HTTP 200 with status="timed_out"
    (or "denied"/"failed") — no thrown error — so all three failure cases were
    logged as success=True.
    
    Fix: check `event.result?.status`. A non-null status that isn't "delivered"
    is a logical failure. Tools without a status field are unaffected (null
    passes through). Fails closed: any unknown future status is treated as
    failure rather than silently misclassified.
    
    Closes #459

    * feat(openclaw): plow_find — model-driven Spotlight fallback for plow_cp (#468)
    
    * feat(openclaw): plow_find — model-driven Spotlight fallback for plow_cp
    
    When the turn-start file-catalog hint returns zero candidates, the agent
    currently asks the user for a folder instead of trying to locate the file
    itself. That hides real Spotlight hits from the user: a message like
    "move Screenshot 2026-04-23 at 5.30.34 AM to ~/Plow" bypasses the literal
    fast-path (no extension in the user's text) and the hint's semantic path
    isn't reliable enough to surface it on its own.
    
    Add a model-callable search tool so the agent can retry with rephrased
    queries before giving up:
    
    - New `plow find --query ... [--file-type X] [--limit N]` CLI subcommand
      that POSTs to plowd's existing /internal/file_catalog/find endpoint and
      prints the candidates JSON.
    - New `plow_find` tool in the plow-cli openclaw plugin that shells out to
      `plow find`. Description coaches the agent to use it as the fallback
      before asking the user, and to rephrase 2-3 times before giving up.
    - Update `plow_cp` description: on missing path info, call `plow_find`
      first; only ask the user after plow_find comes back empty.
    
    Explicitly *not* extending `parse_literal_tokens` with screenshot or
    other filename-shape regexes — that is exactly the heuristic accretion
    AGENTS.md prohibits. The generalizable fix is the tool.

    * fix(plow_find): address knightwatch review findings (#468)
    
    Three valid findings from sam's ai review bot, all addressed:
    
    1. Prompt-stack drift — workspace AGENTS.md and plow-file-discovery SKILL
       still taught hint → plow_cp → ask user, making the new fallback
       prompt-order-dependent and at risk of regressing to "what folder is
       it in?" in production. Both files now teach
       hint → plow_cp (direct) or plow_find → plow_cp, explicitly.
    
    2. limit silent misbehavior — JS wrapper used `if (params.limit)` so 0
       silently fell back to plowd's default, and negative values flowed
       through to `merged[:limit]` for a wrong-slice result. For an
       LLM-driven tool, silent wrong results are worse than a loud error
       (fail-fast). The wrapper now rejects non-integer, zero, and negative
       limit values with a clear error envelope.
    
    3. file_type description mismatch — the backend uses file_type as a
       ranking bias (additive score bonus), not a hard filter. The tool
       description now says "ranking hint" and explicitly notes that
       off-type candidates can still appear.
    
    No behavior change on the happy path. Tests updated for limit
    validation (3 new cases); docs aligned.

    * fix: file-cp approval reliability (bug #458) (#471)
    
    * fix(ws): actively close evicted socket on register replacement
    
    Prior behavior left the old WS open (half-dead) after replacement,
    so the evicted plowd saw no disconnect until the ALB eventually TCP-
    closed the idle socket. That was the root cause of the multi-device
    thrashing surfaced in bug #458.
    
    Refs #458
    
    * fix(ws): hold strong ref on evicted-WS close task
    
    Mirrors the established pattern in webhook.py. Without this, CPython
    3.11+ can GC the pending Task mid-flight, which emits 'Task was
    destroyed but it is pending' and potentially skips the close.
    
    Addresses code-review finding on PR commit 2a8bbad0.
    Refs #458
    
    * refactor(plowd): surface server token from _create_batch_approval_record
    
    No behavior change. The token becomes needed for the HTTP poll fallback
    in plow_cp (later commit).
    
    Refs #458
    
    * fix(plowd): drop premature server_token binding in plow_cp
    
    Task 4 will add the binding together with its use. Keeping a dead
    local with a noqa and a plan-task cross-reference is brittle — task
    numbers are ephemeral and the noqa would need to be removed anyway.
    
    Addresses code-review finding on PR commit 2b2dad85.
    Refs #458
    
    * feat(plowd): atomic claim on file_request resolution
    
    Guards against double-execute when WS push and HTTP poll both reach
    _handle_file_request_push for the same request_id. Single-threaded
    event loop makes the check-then-set atomic; no asyncio.Lock needed.
    
    Refs #458
    
    * feat(plowd): HTTP poll fallback in plow_cp
    
    Race the WS-driven Future against a 10s poll of GET /v1/files/requests/
    {token}. First to complete wins. Backstops any missed WS push — multi-
    device eviction, edge flap, or transient drops. Matches the behavior
    the server's approve_file_request comment already assumes exists.
    
    Refs #458
    
    * fix(plowd): retrieve poll_task exceptions and terminate poll on 404
    
    Two code-review findings on PR commit 470579d2:
    
    1. finally block's add_done_callback(_background_tasks.discard) dropped
       the ref but never called t.exception(), leaving unretrieved-exception
       warnings at GC time if _run_poll ever raised. Replaced with a named
       callback that both discards and logs.
    
    2. poll_for_resolution swallowed 404 responses as transient and retried
       every 10s for the full 120s timeout. Now terminates the poll on 404
       so plow_cp times out cleanly without spamming the log.
    
    Refs #458

    * fix(plowd): plow_cp_cancel flips 'resolving' state to failed
    
    Task 3 introduced 'resolving' as a transitional state for file_request
    claims. plow_cp_cancel's status check didn't include it, so a cancel
    arriving while resolution was mid-flight would leave the store entry
    in 'resolving' indefinitely.
    
    Follow-up from code review on Task 3.
    Refs #458
    
    * fix(plowd): include 'resolving' in FileRequestStore.pending()
    
    A request in the 'resolving' transitional state (copy in progress) is
    still in-flight and should be visible to callers that enumerate
    pending work. Currently pending() has no production caller — this
    closes a latent diagnostic gap rather than fixing an observable bug.
    
    Final code-review finding on bug #458 branch.
    Refs #458
    
    * fix(plowd): drop exc_info from poll_failed log to prevent token disclosure
    
    httpx exceptions include the full request URL (containing the capability
    token) in their repr. Logging exc_info=True on transient poll failures
    would write the token to plowd logs; type(exc).__name__ is enough
    diagnostic info without the leak.

    * fix(vm): actually mount ~/Plow at /workspace/host (#476)
    
    * fix(vm): actually mount ~/Plow at /workspace/host
    
    The openclaw gateway's AGENTS.md has long promised the agent that
    `~/Plow` is mounted at `/workspace/host`, and `plow_cp` returns a
    `/workspace/host/<name>` path on success — but `lima.yaml` never
    declared the mount, so that promise was a lie.
    
    Side effects:
    - `plow_cp` returns success, then the agent reads the advertised
      workspace path, sees nothing, and reports "the copy failed" even
      though the file really is on disk at `~/Plow/<name>`. (#452)
    - iMessage attachments saved to `~/Plow/iMessage Downloads/` on the
      host are invisible from inside the VM, so the agent refuses to
      `ls ~/Plow` because what it sees at `/workspace/host` is empty.
    
    `VMStartupOrchestrator` was already creating `~/Plow` on the host,
    writing `/mounts/host-shares.tsv`, wiring the Finder sidebar entry,
    and serializing the share into `PLOWD_OPENCLAW_ACTIVE_HOST_SHARES`.
    But `host-shares.tsv` had no consumer on the guest side, and
    `lima.yaml` had no entry for the path — so nothing actually
    materialized the mount.
    
    Fix: add the mount that the rest of the system already assumes.
    
    - `app/vm/lima.yaml`: declare `__PLOW_HOME_PLOW_DIR__` → `/workspace/host`
      as a writable virtiofs mount, nested inside `/workspace`.
    - `LimaConfigRenderContext`: add `homePlowDir` and wire the
      `__PLOW_HOME_PLOW_DIR__` substitution.
    - `DaemonClient.writeDaemonLaunchLimaConfig`: pass
      `resolvePlowFolderHostPath()` (same resolver `ConfiguredHostShare`
      already uses).
    
    Container exposure comes for free: `run-openclaw-container.sh` already
    bind-mounts `/workspace:/workspace`, which captures the nested
    `/workspace/host` virtiofs mount into the openclaw container.
    
    Existing VMs pick this up on the next app launch via the bundle
    fingerprint recreate path — no manual `limactl delete` needed.
    
    Fixes #452
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * refactor(vm): derive lima host-share mounts from ConfiguredHostShare (#479)
    
    Before: ~/Plow → /workspace/host was declared in two independent places
    that had to agree by hand — the ConfiguredHostShare list (used by plowd
    and VMStartupOrchestrator) and a separate homePlowDir field plus a
    hardcoded mount stanza in app/vm/lima.yaml. That drift class is what
    caused the missing-mount bug fixed in PR #476.
    
    Now: ConfiguredHostShare is the single source of truth. DaemonClient
    renders the YAML mount block from that list and substitutes it into
    the lima.yaml template via __PLOW_HOST_SHARE_MOUNTS__. The hostPath,
    guestPath, and writable flag all flow from one declaration.
    
    Bonus: ConfiguredHostShare.readOnly was previously unused; it now
    drives the writable: line in the rendered YAML.
    
    Net -12 LOC.
    
    Co-authored-by: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * test(plowd): make test_plow_cp_poll_recovers_missed_ws_push env-independent
    
    The prior fixture used `tempfile.mkdtemp(dir=Path.home())` to satisfy
    `_execute_file_copy`'s home-only source check, which crashes with
    `OSError: [Errno 30] Read-only file system` in any environment where
    `$HOME` is not writable (containerized CI, reviewer sandboxes).
    
    Monkeypatch `plowd.main.Path.home` to a tmp_path subdirectory — the same
    pattern already used in tests/test_file_request_e2e.py — so the source
    lives under the test-controlled fake home and the home-check still passes.

    feat: Slack Participate mode, VMStartupOrchestrator refactor, iMessage debounce, and related fixes (#437)
    
    * baseline: re-apply feat/slack-participate onto post-revert main
    
    Applies all changes from feat/slack-participate (PR #392, reverted in
    #433) onto the current main tip. No logic changes from the original
    branch — this is a clean rebase point before the pending fail-fast fix
    in the daemon's participate routing branch.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Sonnet 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(slack-daemon): strip dead opty_engine code, fix test hang and slowness (#435)
    
    * fix(slack): close SocketModeClient on task cancellation to prevent test hang
    
    SocketModeClient.connect() spawns a background thread that schedules
    coroutines onto the event loop via run_coroutine_threadsafe. Without
    client.close(), cancelling the daemon task leaves that thread running,
    preventing the event loop from stopping and hanging thread.join() in the
    TestClient context manager indefinitely. The fix wraps the keep-alive
    loop in try/finally to guarantee client.close() on any exit path.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Sonnet 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(slack): remove future.result() to prevent shutdown deadlock
    
    SocketModeClient.close() calls message_workers.shutdown(wait=True) from
    within the event loop thread (the finally block). If a worker is blocked
    on future.result() waiting for the event loop to process a coroutine, and
    the event loop is waiting for the worker, the result is a deadlock that
    hangs thread.join() indefinitely in TestClient.__exit__.
    
    Remove future.result() — the coroutine is fire-and-forget from the Slack
    SDK thread perspective. Errors are surfaced inside _handle_socket_request_async
    via normal exception handling. The try/finally: client.close() added in
    the previous commit is kept; without the blocking future.result(), it
    completes cleanly in ≤1s (dominated by message_processor queue drain).
    
    Validated: test_ws.py completes in ~5s instead of hanging for 10+ minutes.
    Root cause tracked to PR #392 which added enough new tests to give the
    Slack WebSocket time to fully connect before the test suite reached
    TestClient-based ws tests.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Sonnet 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>

    Co-Authored-By: Claude Sonnet 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(app): serialize permission selection on MainActor to fix NSMenu crash
    
    DaemonClient is @Observable but not MainActor-isolated. applyPermissionSelection
    was async without explicit actor annotation, so it ran on a cooperative task
    thread when awaited from InstallerView.finalizePermissionsIfNeeded. Mutating
    @Observable properties off-main fires SwiftUI observation callbacks on the
    mutating actor, which can cascade into NSMenu rebuilds. NSMenu requires main
    thread — off-main cascades crash with '-[NSMenu itemArray]' NSAssertionHandler
    failures.
    
    The crash report shows two threads concurrently in applyPermissionSelection
    (one holding the SwiftUI observation lock while the other hits NSMenu) —
    the textbook signature of this bug.
    
    Annotating applyPermissionSelection + its callers (completePermissions,
    skipPermissions) with @MainActor serializes everything on the main thread.

    * fix: assert OwnerAllowFrom for plow-imessage direct messages so cron is available
    
    cron (and gateway, nodes) are owner-only tools in openclaw. Without an owner
    assertion, senderIsOwner is always false for plow-imessage sessions and these
    tools are stripped from the toolset before the model sees them.
    
    For direct plow-imessage messages the sender is always the account owner —
    plow-imessage is a personal 1:1 assistant and only the registered user can
    send messages to it. Pass OwnerAllowFrom: [normalizedFrom] in the inbound
    context for direct messages so openclaw can identify the sender as owner
    without requiring a wildcard in claw-config.json (which would be insecure).
    
    Group messages are unaffected — no owner assertion is made there.

    * Bundle limactl inside the .app, no system PATH fallback
    
    Pin Lima 2.1.1 and fetch the arm64 macOS release tarball in a pre-build
    script, staging limactl, the Linux guestagent, and the template tree
    into Phoenix/Resources/{bin,share}. The Xcode Resources phase copies
    the two folder references into .app/Contents/Resources, and the Release
    notarization loop already signs every Mach-O it finds -- so the new
    binary picks up the Developer ID + hardened runtime without extra work.
    
    LimaVMManager now resolves limactl strictly from Bundle.main, raising a
    clear LimaVMError.limactlNotBundled if the executable is missing. We
    never fall back to the system PATH. VZ backend needs nothing from
    libexec/lima/, so we skip the 33 MB krunkit driver and plugins.
    
    Size delta on a Release build: ~39 MB (limactl 31 MB + guestagent 7 MB
    + templates 0.5 MB).

    * Install zstd in the guest before provisioning openclaw
    
    The Lima guest is Debian 12; the cloud image happens to include zstd but

    * Harden fetch-limactl: arch guard, durable cache, canary-verified staging
    
    Three review findings from 2a360c5:
    
    1. Arch hardcoding. Phoenix is Apple Silicon only, so fail loudly on
       anything but arm64/aarch64 instead of silently bundling an
       unlaunchable binary.
    
    2. Network at build time. Move the tarball cache from `.build/lima-cache/`
       (wiped by `git clean`) to `~/Library/Caches/co.plow/lima/` (override
       via PLOW_LIMA_CACHE_DIR). Once populated, the cache survives repo
       cleaning and worktree re-creation so clean checkouts no longer need
       GitHub reachability on every build. Bump curl retry tolerance
       (--retry 5 --retry-connrefused, three outer attempts) and print an
       explicit offline-bootstrap recipe if all attempts fail.
    
    3. Cache-hit integrity. Fast path now requires both the stamp AND a
       list of canary files — limactl, the Linux guestagent, and the two
       templates our lima.yaml inherits from (`_images/debian-12`,
       `_default/mounts`). A stale checkout missing only the templates
       re-stages from the durable cache instead of silently passing the
       build and failing at VM boot. Also declared the template canaries
       in the Xcode build phase outputPaths for DAG completeness.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Hermetic xcodebuild + race-safe limactl staging
    
    Two review findings from 3cb44ff:
    
    A. Concurrent-build race. The prior script wrote `${TARBALL_PATH}.tmp`
       with a fixed name and did a shell-level `mv NEW_DIR final-dir`, which
       (when the target exists) moves NEW_DIR *inside* final-dir rather than
       replacing it — reliably produced `Resources/bin/bin/limactl` under
       parallel invocations. Now: tarball downloads land in a per-process
       mktemp(1) file and rename atomically into the cache; staging runs
       under a mkdir-based advisory lock in the cache dir (with a 10-minute
       self-heal in case of crashes). Verified with 5 parallel cold
       invocations -- exactly one stages, the other four re-check under the
       lock and exit clean; no leaked stage dirs, no bin/bin, final shas
       match the pin.
    
    B. Network in the target build phase. Split fetch-limactl.sh into a
       default (download + stage) and `--verify` mode (canary-only, no
       network). The Xcode build phase now runs `--verify` and fails the
       build with an actionable error if staging is missing. Added a public
       `just fetch-limactl` recipe and wired it as a prereq on the private
       `xcode-build` recipe and the public `test` recipe, so every normal
       dev path (`just app build` / `up` / `test`) primes the staging area
       before xcodebuild runs. Verified with PATH=/tmp:/usr/bin:/bin (curl
       replaced with a honeypot) + deleted tarball cache: xcodebuild test
       passes on primed state, and fails with a clear "run just app
       fetch-limactl" message when the staged outputs are stripped. CI that
       invokes xcodebuild directly needs to run `just app fetch-limactl`
       as a prior step; the verify-mode error message says so.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Only the lock owner removes the staging lock on exit
    
    cleanup() was installed before the mkdir-acquire, so a waiter that timed
    out, got SIGTERM'd, or errored mid-loop would rmdir the active holder's
    lock directory -- reopening the race the lock was meant to close.
    
    Gate the rmdir behind an I_OWN_LOCK flag that flips to 1 only after the
    mkdir(2) acquire succeeds (including after a stale-lock self-heal where
    the rmdir + retry lands a fresh mkdir). Also trap INT and TERM, not just
    EXIT, so a SIGTERM'd waiter still runs cleanup -- but now that cleanup
    does nothing to the lock because the flag is 0.
    
    Verified: launched a simulated holder (manually-created LOCK_DIR),
    kicked off a waiter in the background, sent it SIGTERM. The holder's
    lock survived the interrupted waiter. Parallel cold-stage (5 waiters,
    1 holder) still produces one `staged Lima` log line, consistent final
    bytes, no leaked lock.

    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Add root .nvmrc; make app/justfile recipes fail on errors
    
    Two small dev-loop fixes:
    
    1. .nvmrc pinning Node 24 at the repo root so fnm/nvm/asdf users get
       the right runtime when they cd into a worktree. Opportunistic —
       no other activation hooks added.
    
    2. app/justfile's shell was "zsh -cu" (no -e), so backslash-continued
       recipes silently swallowed mid-chain failures. qa hit this with
       `just app build` returning 0 after plowd-stage-runtime errored out
       with "runtime directory is missing required Phoenix runtime paths".
    
       Fix: set shell := ["zsh", "-cue", "-o", "pipefail"]. The codebase
       was already defensively annotating soft-fail cases with `|| true`
       (e.g. osascript quits, lsof|xargs kill, hdiutil info) and using
       `grep ... || true` for grep-exits-1-on-no-match, which is strong
       evidence the maintainers had always intended errexit semantics.
    
       Scope: app/justfile only. The root justfile's multi-line recipes
       are either line-by-line (just handles errexit), have their own
       `#!/usr/bin/env bash\nset -euo pipefail` shebangs, or are single
       commands — none exhibit the same bug.
    
    Verified: with the new flag, temporarily renaming
    app/plowd/runtime/manifest.toml aside makes `just app build` fail at
    the plowd-stage-runtime step (exit 1) instead of swallowing the error
    and returning 0.

    * Task 7 regression fix: honor PLOW_VM_BUNDLE in pinnedArtifactFilename
    
    QA found that `just app up` (dev mode) was throwing
    `runtimeIncomplete(missing: ["openclaw tarball", "camoufox tarball"])`
    on cold boot, blocking Lima launch.
    
    Root cause: `pinnedArtifactFilename(for:)` (added in Task 7, 9ed3fda7)
    only looked in `cacheDir/<filename>` via `localPath(for:)`. It did not
    honor the `PLOW_VM_BUNDLE` env override. In dev mode `startDownloads`
    detects that env var and intentionally skips the download step, so
    Application Support's runtime-cache stays empty while the real tarballs
    sit at `app/vm/output/`. The sibling `imageCacheDirectory()` on the
    same class already handled this case; the two functions had drifted
    out of sync.
    
    Fix: resolve the containing directory via `imageCacheDirectory()` (which
    consults PLOW_VM_BUNDLE → envURL when set, falls back to cacheDir in
    prod), then verify sha256 of the candidate in that directory. Three-line
    change as qa suggested.
    
    Cross-mode behaviors:
    - **Dev** (PLOW_VM_BUNDLE=app/vm/output, tarballs staged there):
      imageCacheDirectory() returns envURL → candidate =
      envURL/<manifest-filename> → sha matches → returns filename. ✓
    - **Prod** (tarballs downloaded into runtime-cache):
      imageCacheDirectory() returns cacheDir after openclaw sha check →
      candidate = cacheDir/<manifest-filename> → sha matches → returns
      filename. ✓
    - **Still-downloading** (prod, downloads in flight):
      imageCacheDirectory() returns nil → pinnedArtifactFilename returns
      nil → stageImagesEnv throws runtimeIncomplete, correctly gating
      Lima launch. ✓
    
    Verified: `just app test` exit 0 (Phoenix suite passes).
    
    Observation in the neighborhood (not touched, out of scope): DaemonClient's
    `resolveOpenClawImageDirectoryForMounts` has its own dev-mode branch that
    hard-codes `<repoRoot>/app/vm/output` via resolveRepoRootURL, while
    `imageCacheDirectory` in RuntimeDownloadManager uses the PLOW_VM_BUNDLE
    env var. In `just app up` both resolve to the same dir since the recipe
    exports PLOW_VM_BUNDLE=$(cd vm/output && pwd), but the two sources of
    truth for the "dev images dir" remain duplicated. Worth unifying in a
    follow-up, but it's not what the regression needed.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Fix: move StartLimitIntervalSec=0 from [Service] to [Unit]
    
    `StartLimitIntervalSec` is a [Unit] directive in systemd — placing it
    under [Service] makes the parser log "Unknown key StartLimitIntervalSec
    in section [Service], ignoring" and silently drop the setting, which
    leaves the default 5-restarts-in-10s permanent-failure gate in place.
    
    QA caught this on Task 11 e2e: both `plow-openclaw.service` and
    `plow-camoufox.service` journals reported the "Unknown key" message, so
    the plan-review C2/I7 protection against Firefox-OOM burst failure has
    been inert since it landed. Moving the directive into [Unit] is the
    minimal fix in both unit definitions inside `provision-runtime.sh`.
    
    No post-fix `systemctl cat` evidence in this message because the new
    guest-side systemd state only appears after the next cold boot of the
    Lima VM (which rewrites the unit files from this script). QA will
    re-run the e2e pass and check the journal.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * C1 fix: cleanup keys on URL-basename, not synthetic name+version prefix
    
    The post-merge `cleanupStaleCacheEntries` built its keep-set as
    `"\(artifact.name)-\(artifact.version)"` — e.g. `openclaw-2026.4.14` —
    but cache filenames come from `localPath(for:)`, which pulls the basename
    of `artifact.url`, e.g. `openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.tar.zst`. The openclaw
    name does NOT start with that prefix, so once all downloads finished
    the just-verified tarball got swept into the trash. `imageCacheDirectory`
    and `pinnedArtifactFilename` then found nothing → prod boot regressed
    the moment the cleanup ran.
    
    Camoufox was a lucky survivor (its URL basename does start with
    `camoufox-135.0.1-beta.24`) — so this regression would only bite
    openclaw, and only after a successful download, which is what made
    it invisible to the warm-cache dev loop.
    
    Fix: key the cleanup on the exact URL-basename set. Extract a small
    `RuntimeCacheCleaner` helper so the logic can be unit-tested without
    spinning up a real RuntimeDownloadManager (URLSession + Bundle.main
    side effects). Cache-dir method becomes a thin wrapper:
    
        RuntimeCacheCleaner.prune(
            cacheDir: cacheDir,
            keepFilenames: RuntimeCacheCleaner.keepFilenames(for: manifest)
        )
    
    `keepFilenames` builds a Set by `URL(string: $0.url)?.lastPathComponent`,
    matching what `localPath(for:)` writes and what `verifySHA256` later
    reads. Dotfiles stay excluded for safety.
    
    Tests (new `RuntimeCacheCleanerTests`, 4 cases):
    
      1. testKeepFilenamesUsesURLBasename — documents the bugfix: the
         expected keep-set is `{openclaw-agent-*, camoufox-*}`, not the
         old synthetic `{openclaw-*, camoufox-*}` prefix pair.
      2. testPrunePreservesVerifiedCurrentArtifacts — REGRESSION GUARD.
         Pre-bugfix this failed (openclaw got swept).
      3. testPruneRemovesOlderVersionedTarballs — confirms older beta/
         point-release tarballs still get cleaned up.
      4. testPrunePreservesDotfiles — `.manifest-hash` and friends stay.
    
    Verified: `just app test` → exit 0; filtered xcodebuild run of the
    new class shows 4/4 pass in 5ms.
    
    IMPORTANT finding separately flagged to Task 10 (CI workflow):
    `.github/workflows/build-release-candidate.yml` still reads
    `openclaw_vm_artifact` + `app/vm/gatekeeper/manifest.toml`. Both refer
    to TOML keys / directories that don't exist on this branch. Nightly
    release gate is broken until Task 10 flips the reads at
    `openclaw_artifact` + `camoufox_image_artifact`. Deferred here per
    the merge-commit review.

    * Shared compute_git_ref helper for OCI build scripts
    
    New helper at `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh`. Sourced by
    `build-agent-image.sh` (Task 4) and `build-camoufox-image.sh` (Task 5)
    so both OCI artifacts get a consistent short-ref suffix stamped into
    their filenames + manifest entries.
    
    Resolution order matches PR #297:
      1. `PLOW_GIT_REF` env var, verbatim — CI-pinned builds.
      2. `git rev-parse --short=7 HEAD`, with `-dirty` suffix if tracked
         files other than `app/vm/manifest.toml` differ from HEAD.
    
    The `:!app/vm/manifest.toml` pathspec is load-bearing: build scripts
    rewrite that manifest with the new sha256 / size / git_ref values
    right after the image is built, and without the exclude every
    subsequent build on the same commit would flip to `-dirty`.
    
    Untracked files don't trigger `-dirty` — `git diff HEAD` only sees
    tracked files. The comment calls that out so anyone adding a new
    Dockerfile/script remembers to commit first.
    
    Also updates `.gitignore`: the root has a broad `lib/` rule (Python
    packaging boilerplate — setup.py builds into `lib/`) which was silently
    hiding `app/scripts/lib/`. Added `!app/scripts/lib/` negation so the
    new helper + any future helpers in that dir are tracked.
    
    Verified:
      - `bash -n app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh` → no output, exit 0.
      - Smoke test 1 (plain): prints `aedbca6` followed by newline.
      - Smoke test 2 (`PLOW_GIT_REF=pinned123`): prints `pinned123`,
        skips git entirely.
      - Smoke test 3 (touch tracked pyproject.toml): prints `aedbca6-dirty`;
        after `git checkout --` revert, prints `aedbca6` again — exclude
        and dirty detection both working.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Stamp gitRef into openclaw OCI artifact name and manifest
    
    build-agent-image.sh now sources `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh`, computes a
    short ref via `compute_git_ref`, and names the output tarball
    `openclaw-agent-<version>.<gitref>.tar.zst`. After `docker save | zstd`,
    `sed -i.bak -e …` writes the new openclaw_artifact / sha256 / size /
    git_ref into `app/vm/manifest.toml`. Matches PR #297's "build script
    owns manifest writeback" convention. `trap 'rm -f "${MANIFEST}.bak"' EXIT`
    keeps SIGINT mid-sed from leaving a `.bak` behind.
    
    This commit also carries Task 2's schema edit (the two empty
    `*_git_ref = ""` lines in manifest.toml) — per plan directive the
    Task 2 stage rolls up here so there's no intermediate "fields present
    but empty" commit. `openclaw_git_ref` gets its real value written by
    the build in the same commit; `camoufox_image_git_ref` stays empty
    until Task 5 ships the parallel build-camoufox-image.sh change.
    
    Evidence from running `rm -f app/vm/output/openclaw-agent-*.tar.zst &&
    app/scripts/build-agent-image.sh` (2m 48s, docker+zstd):
    
        artifact=.../app/vm/output/openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.416f152-dirty.tar.zst
        sha256=2bbc14f94c6bcdaac0b9d717f6dfc3e34f336507407234808ac0c918cb6db443
        size=299100052
        git_ref=416f152-dirty
    
    `grep -E '^openclaw_(artifact|git_ref|sha256|size)' app/vm/manifest.toml`
    shows all four fields match the build output byte-for-byte. The
    physical tarball exists at the advertised path (299,100,052 bytes).
    
    The `-dirty` suffix is expected here: at `compute_git_ref` time
    `build-agent-image.sh` itself is modified from HEAD (it's being edited
    by this commit), which is exactly the signal the dirty detector is
    designed to surface. A clean rebuild from the final commit before
    ship will rewrite the manifest with a non-dirty ref; tasks 5/8/13
    will re-exercise the pipeline against whatever ref is current at
    that point.

    * Delegate manifest writes to per-image build scripts with cache-reuse gate
    
    Now that build-agent-image.sh (Task 4) and build-camoufox-image.sh (Task 5)
    each stamp their own manifest slice, the orchestrator only needs to
    decide "rebuild or reuse" per artifact and delegate. Stripped the
    ~60 lines of `set_manifest_string` / `set_manifest_int` awk helpers;
    sources `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh` for `compute_git_ref`.
    
    `maybe_build` gate replaces the old `[ ! -f "$OPENCLAW_PATH" ]` check
    with a two-condition test:
    
        pinned_ref == compute_git_ref()   AND
        file-exists( <output>/<pinned_name> )
    
    Either side going false → delegate to the child. This fixes the prior
    dev-loop footgun: a commit bump would produce a new gitRef in the
    manifest but the stale tarball under the *old* name might still be on
    disk, and the old existence-only check would falsely report "using
    existing artifact" and ship the wrong bytes.
    
    Evidence:
    
    Step 2 — first run (stale pinned refs 416f152/83f90c5 vs current
    9298cd3-dirty, both mismatch → build both):
        time app/scripts/build-runtime-artifacts.sh
        ...
        7:01.38 total  (docker build + `docker save | zstd -19` for both
        artifacts; ~300 MB openclaw and ~670 MB camoufox)
    
    Step 3 — immediate re-run (manifest now pins 9298cd3-dirty, tarballs
    present at pinned paths → reuse both):
        time app/scripts/build-runtime-artifacts.sh
        ==> reusing openclaw tarball: openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.9298cd3-dirty.tar.zst (git_ref=9298cd3-dirty matches HEAD)
        ==> reusing camoufox tarball: camoufox-135.0.1-beta.24.9298cd3-dirty.tar.zst (git_ref=9298cd3-dirty matches HEAD)
        ...
        0.065 total  (65 ms — no docker or zstd invocations, exactly two
        file-exists checks + a git rev-parse)
    
    Step 4 — manifest consistency: all 10 keys populated, both gitRefs
    converge to 9298cd3-dirty, no blank values.
    
    Per plan Step 5 this commit carries only build-runtime-artifacts.sh
    itself. Manifest writebacks (which the orchestrator no longer owns)
    stay in Tasks 4/5's commit authority.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Add gitRef-decode + instance-cleanup tests with non-#if-DEBUG debug seams
    
    Task 7 was largely a no-op for the cleanup *body* — plan Step 1 ships
    via merge (gitRef: String? present on RuntimeArtifact), Step 4's
    cleanupStaleCacheEntries body already landed in acc8ba9a (the C1 fix
    refactored the logic into the RuntimeCacheCleaner static helper and
    re-keyed the keep-set on URL basename). The missing pieces the plan
    still asks for on top of HEAD:
    
    1. gitRef decode tests (Step 2). New `RuntimeArtifactDecodingTests`
       class, two cases:
         - testRuntimeArtifactDecodesGitRef: explicit "gitRef": "abc1234"
           decodes to .gitRef == "abc1234".
         - testRuntimeArtifactDecodesMissingGitRef: omitted field decodes
           to .gitRef == nil (the `String?` is load-bearing — legacy
           manifests without the field must still parse).
    
    2. Instance-path cleanup test (Step 5). New
       `RuntimeDownloadManagerInstanceCleanupTests` class, one case:
       `testCleanupStaleCacheEntriesRemovesUnreferencedTarballs`. Drives
       the test via the public debug seams (see below), populates a tmpdir
       with one live/one stale/one dotfile entry, asserts the right
       three-way split post-cleanup. Complementary to
       RuntimeCacheCleanerTests, which exercises the static helper; this
       one covers the instance plumbing (stateQueue dispatch on
       debugSetManifest + private cleanupStaleCacheEntries path).
    
    3. Debug seams on RuntimeDownloadManager (Step 6). Added three:
         - init(cacheDir: URL) — test-only designated initializer so
           tests can aim at a scratch tmpdir instead of AppPaths.
           runtimeCacheDirectory().
         - debugSetManifest(_:) — injects a manifest without going
           through Bundle.main.
         - debugCleanupStaleCacheEntries() — invokes the private cleanup
           synchronously on stateQueue so tests observe the filesystem
           effect before assertions run.
    
    Per plan revision I7 these are NOT `#if DEBUG`-gated. PhoenixTests
    compiles against Release in CI archive builds / diagnostics-bundle
    repackaging; a symbol that vanishes under Release would break those
    paths. The overhead is a few bytes of metadata and one convenience
    init — fine to ship in release binaries. Doc comment on
    `init(cacheDir:)` spells this out for the next reader.
    
    Verified:
      - targeted `xcodebuild test -only-testing ...` on the three
        cleanup/decode clas…

    * fix(app): serialize permission selection on MainActor to fix NSMenu crash
    
    DaemonClient is @Observable but not MainActor-isolated. applyPermissionSelection
    was async without explicit actor annotation, so it ran on a cooperative task
    thread when awaited from InstallerView.finalizePermissionsIfNeeded. Mutating
    @Observable properties off-main fires SwiftUI observation callbacks on the
    mutating actor, which can cascade into NSMenu rebuilds. NSMenu requires main
    thread — off-main cascades crash with '-[NSMenu itemArray]' NSAssertionHandler
    failures.
    
    The crash report shows two threads concurrently in applyPermissionSelection
    (one holding the SwiftUI observation lock while the other hits NSMenu) —
    the textbook signature of this bug.
    
    Annotating applyPermissionSelection + its callers (completePermissions,
    skipPermissions) with @MainActor serializes everything on the main thread.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * fix: assert OwnerAllowFrom for plow-imessage direct messages so cron is available
    
    cron (and gateway, nodes) are owner-only tools in openclaw. Without an owner
    assertion, senderIsOwner is always false for plow-imessage sessions and these
    tools are stripped from the toolset before the model sees them.
    
    For direct plow-imessage messages the sender is always the account owner —
    plow-imessage is a personal 1:1 assistant and only the registered user can
    send messages to it. Pass OwnerAllowFrom: [normalizedFrom] in the inbound
    context for direct messages so openclaw can identify the sender as owner
    without requiring a wildcard in claw-config.json (which would be insecure).
    
    Group messages are unaffected — no owner assertion is made there.

    binary picks up the Developer ID + hardened runtime without extra work.

    + templates 0.5 MB).

    * Harden fetch-limactl: arch guard, durable cache, canary-verified staging
    
    Three review findings from 2a360c5:
    
    1. Arch hardcoding. Phoenix is Apple Silicon only, so fail loudly on
       anything but arm64/aarch64 instead of silently bundling an
       unlaunchable binary.
    
    2. Network at build time. Move the tarball cache from `.build/lima-cache/`
       (wiped by `git clean`) to `~/Library/Caches/co.plow/lima/` (override
       via PLOW_LIMA_CACHE_DIR). Once populated, the cache survives repo
       cleaning and worktree re-creation so clean checkouts no longer need
       GitHub reachability on every build. Bump curl retry tolerance
       (--retry 5 --retry-connrefused, three outer attempts) and print an
       explicit offline-bootstrap recipe if all attempts fail.
    
    3. Cache-hit integrity. Fast path now requires both the stamp AND a
       list of canary files — limactl, the Linux guestagent, and the two
       templates our lima.yaml inherits from (`_images/debian-12`,
       `_default/mounts`). A stale checkout missing only the templates
       re-stages from the durable cache instead of silently passing the
       build and failing at VM boot. Also declared the template canaries
       in the Xcode build phase outputPaths for DAG completeness.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Hermetic xcodebuild + race-safe limactl staging
    
    Two review findings from 3cb44ff:
    
    A. Concurrent-build race. The prior script wrote `${TARBALL_PATH}.tmp`
       with a fixed name and did a shell-level `mv NEW_DIR final-dir`, which
       (when the target exists) moves NEW_DIR *inside* final-dir rather than
       replacing it — reliably produced `Resources/bin/bin/limactl` under
       parallel invocations. Now: tarball downloads land in a per-process
       mktemp(1) file and rename atomically into the cache; staging runs
       under a mkdir-based advisory lock in the cache dir (with a 10-minute
       self-heal in case of crashes). Verified with 5 parallel cold
       invocations -- exactly one stages, the other four re-check under the
       lock and exit clean; no leaked stage dirs, no bin/bin, final shas
       match the pin.
    
    B. Network in the target build phase. Split fetch-limactl.sh into a
       default (download + stage) and `--verify` mode (canary-only, no
       network). The Xcode build phase now runs `--verify` and fails the
       build with an actionable error if staging is missing. Added a public
       `just fetch-limactl` recipe and wired it as a prereq on the private
       `xcode-build` recipe and the public `test` recipe, so every normal
       dev path (`just app build` / `up` / `test`) primes the staging area
       before xcodebuild runs. Verified with PATH=/tmp:/usr/bin:/bin (curl
       replaced with a honeypot) + deleted tarball cache: xcodebuild test
       passes on primed state, and fails with a clear "run just app
       fetch-limactl" message when the staged outputs are stripped. CI that
       invokes xcodebuild directly needs to run `just app fetch-limactl`
       as a prior step; the verify-mode error message says so.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Only the lock owner removes the staging lock on exit
    
    cleanup() was installed before the mkdir-acquire, so a waiter that timed
    out, got SIGTERM'd, or errored mid-loop would rmdir the active holder's
    lock directory -- reopening the race the lock was meant to close.
    
    Gate the rmdir behind an I_OWN_LOCK flag that flips to 1 only after the
    mkdir(2) acquire succeeds (including after a stale-lock self-heal where
    the rmdir + retry lands a fresh mkdir). Also trap INT and TERM, not just
    EXIT, so a SIGTERM'd waiter still runs cleanup -- but now that cleanup
    does nothing to the lock because the flag is 0.
    
    Verified: launched a simulated holder (manually-created LOCK_DIR),
    kicked off a waiter in the background, sent it SIGTERM. The holder's
    lock survived the interrupted waiter. Parallel cold-stage (5 waiters,
    1 holder) still produces one `staged Lima` log line, consistent final
    bytes, no leaked lock.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * Add root .nvmrc; make app/justfile recipes fail on errors
    
    Two small dev-loop fixes:
    
    1. .nvmrc pinning Node 24 at the repo root so fnm/nvm/asdf users get
       the right runtime when they cd into a worktree. Opportunistic —
       no other activation hooks added.
    
    2. app/justfile's shell was "zsh -cu" (no -e), so backslash-continued
       recipes silently swallowed mid-chain failures. qa hit this with
       `just app build` returning 0 after plowd-stage-runtime errored out
       with "runtime directory is missing required Phoenix runtime paths".
    
       Fix: set shell := ["zsh", "-cue", "-o", "pipefail"]. The codebase
       was already defensively annotating soft-fail cases with `|| true`
       (e.g. osascript quits, lsof|xargs kill, hdiutil info) and using
       `grep ... || true` for grep-exits-1-on-no-match, which is strong
       evidence the maintainers had always intended errexit semantics.
    
       Scope: app/justfile only. The root justfile's multi-line recipes
       are either line-by-line (just handles errexit), have their own
       `#!/usr/bin/env bash\nset -euo pipefail` shebangs, or are single
       commands — none exhibit the same bug.
    
    Verified: with the new flag, temporarily renaming
    app/plowd/runtime/manifest.toml aside makes `just app build` fail at
    the plowd-stage-runtime step (exit 1) instead of swallowing the error
    and returning 0.

    * Task 6 (camoufox-on-lima): Provision both openclaw and camoufox from a single runtime script
    
    - Rename `provision-openclaw.sh` → `provision-runtime.sh`. One provisioner
      now installs units for both containers.
    - Systemd topology per plan-review C2: `plow-runtime.target` only `Wants=`
      the two services (no `Requires=`, no `PartOf=`), so a Camoufox crash
      loop cannot cascade a stop into openclaw. `StartLimitIntervalSec=0` on
      both units disables systemd's default 5-restarts-in-10s permanent-failure
      gate; Lima itself is the lifecycle boundary we want. `--init` added to
      both `nerdctl run` invocations so `tini` reaps Playwright/Firefox
      subprocesses cleanly.
    - Shared image loader reads `/images/images.env` for the exact pinned
      tarball filename instead of `find | sort | tail` (not semver-safe:
      `135.0.1-beta.10` sorts after `.2`). Per-role SHA stamps under
      `/var/lib/plow-<role>/` keep the two loads independent.
    - Bump lima.yaml to 4 vCPU / 5 GiB per head chef's sizing: sum of the
      old 2+2 GiB VZ splits plus a 1 GiB cushion for container overhead and
      correlated peaks (Firefox GC during a large openclaw turn). Drop the
      now-stale "future browser container" comment and switch the `provision.file.url`
      reference to the renamed script.
    - Phoenix side: `RuntimeDownloadManager.pinnedArtifactFilename(for:)`
      returns the manifest-pinned filename for an artifact (openclaw or
      camoufox), gated on SHA verification. `DaemonClient.stageImagesEnv(in:)`
      writes those names into `<images>/images.env` right before rendering
      the Lima config, and `resolveOpenClawLimaConfigURL` calls it after
      resolving `imagesDir`. Staging/provisioner copy paths + error strings
      updated to the new filename.

    - `openclawImageDirectory()` → `imageCacheDirectory()`. Both openclaw and
      camoufox live in the same cache dir; Lima mounts it at /images.
    - `openclawImagePath(in:)` → `hasOCITarball(in:)` returning `Bool` (its
      callers only ever checked non-nil presence).
    
    The gatekeeper VZ VM wiring in Phoenix (DaemonClient's `prepareGatekeeperVM`
    startup, StatusView/DownloadBarView/ActivationState pattern matches on
    `Status.extracting`, `gatekeeperStatus`, `gatekeeperBytesWritten/Expected`,
    `vmBundlePath(for:)`) is the subject of Task 8. To keep this commit's build
    green without spilling Task 8's scope, the public surface stays as
    compile-safe shims — `gatekeeperVMReady` returns `true` (falls through to
    `vmBundlePath(for:) == nil`, which now always nils out and short-circuits
    the gatekeeper startup path); `gatekeeperStatus` / bytes fields are `.idle`
    / 0 constants; `Status.extracting` is retained in the enum but never
    emitted. Each shim carries a "Task 8 removes this" comment so the next
    commit knows exactly what to strip.
    
    Document the single `/images` mount decision in lima.yaml above the mounts
    block: both tarballs are ours, splitting the mount per-container would add
    plumbing without a real trust boundary.
    
    Verified: clean xcodebuild Debug build; 100 Phoenix unit tests pass.

    * Task 7 regression fix: honor PLOW_VM_BUNDLE in pinnedArtifactFilename
    
    QA found that `just app up` (dev mode) was throwing
    `runtimeIncomplete(missing: ["openclaw tarball", "camoufox tarball"])`
    on cold boot, blocking Lima launch.
    
    Root cause: `pinnedArtifactFilename(for:)` (added in Task 7, 9ed3fda7)
    only looked in `cacheDir/<filename>` via `localPath(for:)`. It did not
    honor the `PLOW_VM_BUNDLE` env override. In dev mode `startDownloads`
    detects that env var and intentionally skips the download step, so
    Application Support's runtime-cache stays empty while the real tarballs
    sit at `app/vm/output/`. The sibling `imageCacheDirectory()` on the
    same class already handled this case; the two functions had drifted
    out of sync.
    
    Fix: resolve the containing directory via `imageCacheDirectory()` (which
    consults PLOW_VM_BUNDLE → envURL when set, falls back to cacheDir in
    prod), then verify sha256 of the candidate in that directory. Three-line
    change as qa suggested.
    
    Cross-mode behaviors:
    - **Dev** (PLOW_VM_BUNDLE=app/vm/output, tarballs staged there):
      imageCacheDirectory() returns envURL → candidate =
      envURL/<manifest-filename> → sha matches → returns filename. ✓
    - **Prod** (tarballs downloaded into runtime-cache):
      imageCacheDirectory() returns cacheDir after openclaw sha check →
      candidate = cacheDir/<manifest-filename> → sha matches → returns
      filename. ✓
    - **Still-downloading** (prod, downloads in flight):
      imageCacheDirectory() returns nil → pinnedArtifactFilename returns
      nil → stageImagesEnv throws runtimeIncomplete, correctly gating
      Lima launch. ✓
    
    Verified: `just app test` exit 0 (Phoenix suite passes).
    
    Observation in the neighborhood (not touched, out of scope): DaemonClient's
    `resolveOpenClawImageDirectoryForMounts` has its own dev-mode branch that
    hard-codes `<repoRoot>/app/vm/output` via resolveRepoRootURL, while
    `imageCacheDirectory` in RuntimeDownloadManager uses the PLOW_VM_BUNDLE
    env var. In `just app up` both resolve to the same dir since the recipe
    exports PLOW_VM_BUNDLE=$(cd vm/output && pwd), but the two sources of
    truth for the "dev images dir" remain duplicated. Worth unifying in a
    follow-up, but it's not what the regression needed.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Fix: move StartLimitIntervalSec=0 from [Service] to [Unit]
    
    `StartLimitIntervalSec` is a [Unit] directive in systemd — placing it
    under [Service] makes the parser log "Unknown key StartLimitIntervalSec
    in section [Service], ignoring" and silently drop the setting, which
    leaves the default 5-restarts-in-10s permanent-failure gate in place.
    
    QA caught this on Task 11 e2e: both `plow-openclaw.service` and
    `plow-camoufox.service` journals reported the "Unknown key" message, so
    the plan-review C2/I7 protection against Firefox-OOM burst failure has
    been inert since it landed. Moving the directive into [Unit] is the
    minimal fix in both unit definitions inside `provision-runtime.sh`.
    
    No post-fix `systemctl cat` evidence in this message because the new
    guest-side systemd state only appears after the next cold boot of the
    Lima VM (which rewrites the unit files from this script). QA will
    re-run the e2e pass and check the journal.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * C1 fix: cleanup keys on URL-basename, not synthetic name+version prefix
    
    The post-merge `cleanupStaleCacheEntries` built its keep-set as
    `"\(artifact.name)-\(artifact.version)"` — e.g. `openclaw-2026.4.14` —
    but cache filenames come from `localPath(for:)`, which pulls the basename
    of `artifact.url`, e.g. `openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.tar.zst`. The openclaw
    name does NOT start with that prefix, so once all downloads finished
    the just-verified tarball got swept into the trash. `imageCacheDirectory`
    and `pinnedArtifactFilename` then found nothing → prod boot regressed
    the moment the cleanup ran.
    
    Camoufox was a lucky survivor (its URL basename does start with
    `camoufox-135.0.1-beta.24`) — so this regression would only bite
    openclaw, and only after a successful download, which is what made
    it invisible to the warm-cache dev loop.
    
    Fix: key the cleanup on the exact URL-basename set. Extract a small
    `RuntimeCacheCleaner` helper so the logic can be unit-tested without
    spinning up a real RuntimeDownloadManager (URLSession + Bundle.main
    side effects). Cache-dir method becomes a thin wrapper:
    
        RuntimeCacheCleaner.prune(
            cacheDir: cacheDir,
            keepFilenames: RuntimeCacheCleaner.keepFilenames(for: manifest)
        )
    
    `keepFilenames` builds a Set by `URL(string: $0.url)?.lastPathComponent`,
    matching what `localPath(for:)` writes and what `verifySHA256` later
    reads. Dotfiles stay excluded for safety.
    
    Tests (new `RuntimeCacheCleanerTests`, 4 cases):
    
      1. testKeepFilenamesUsesURLBasename — documents the bugfix: the
         expected keep-set is `{openclaw-agent-*, camoufox-*}`, not the
         old synthetic `{openclaw-*, camoufox-*}` prefix pair.
      2. testPrunePreservesVerifiedCurrentArtifacts — REGRESSION GUARD.
         Pre-bugfix this failed (openclaw got swept).
      3. testPruneRemovesOlderVersionedTarballs — confirms older beta/
         point-release tarballs still get cleaned up.
      4. testPrunePreservesDotfiles — `.manifest-hash` and friends stay.
    
    Verified: `just app test` → exit 0; filtered xcodebuild run of the
    new class shows 4/4 pass in 5ms.
    
    IMPORTANT finding separately flagged to Task 10 (CI workflow):
    `.github/workflows/build-release-candidate.yml` still reads
    `openclaw_vm_artifact` + `app/vm/gatekeeper/manifest.toml`. Both refer
    to TOML keys / directories that don't exist on this branch. Nightly
    release gate is broken until Task 10 flips the reads at
    `openclaw_artifact` + `camoufox_image_artifact`. Deferred here per
    the merge-commit review.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * Shared compute_git_ref helper for OCI build scripts
    
    New helper at `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh`. Sourced by
    `build-agent-image.sh` (Task 4) and `build-camoufox-image.sh` (Task 5)
    so both OCI artifacts get a consistent short-ref suffix stamped into
    their filenames + manifest entries.
    
    Resolution order matches PR #297:
      1. `PLOW_GIT_REF` env var, verbatim — CI-pinned builds.
      2. `git rev-parse --short=7 HEAD`, with `-dirty` suffix if tracked
         files other than `app/vm/manifest.toml` differ from HEAD.
    
    The `:!app/vm/manifest.toml` pathspec is load-bearing: build scripts
    rewrite that manifest with the new sha256 / size / git_ref values
    right after the image is built, and without the exclude every
    subsequent build on the same commit would flip to `-dirty`.
    
    Untracked files don't trigger `-dirty` — `git diff HEAD` only sees
    tracked files. The comment calls that out so anyone adding a new
    Dockerfile/script remembers to commit first.
    
    Also updates `.gitignore`: the root has a broad `lib/` rule (Python
    packaging boilerplate — setup.py builds into `lib/`) which was silently
    hiding `app/scripts/lib/`. Added `!app/scripts/lib/` negation so the
    new helper + any future helpers in that dir are tracked.
    
    Verified:
      - `bash -n app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh` → no output, exit 0.
      - Smoke test 1 (plain): prints `aedbca6` followed by newline.
      - Smoke test 2 (`PLOW_GIT_REF=pinned123`): prints `pinned123`,
        skips git entirely.
      - Smoke test 3 (touch tracked pyproject.toml): prints `aedbca6-dirty`;
        after `git checkout --` revert, prints `aedbca6` again — exclude
        and dirty detection both working.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Stamp gitRef into openclaw OCI artifact name and manifest
    
    build-agent-image.sh now sources `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh`, computes a
    short ref via `compute_git_ref`, and names the output tarball
    `openclaw-agent-<version>.<gitref>.tar.zst`. After `docker save | zstd`,
    `sed -i.bak -e …` writes the new openclaw_artifact / sha256 / size /
    git_ref into `app/vm/manifest.toml`. Matches PR #297's "build script
    owns manifest writeback" convention. `trap 'rm -f "${MANIFEST}.bak"' EXIT`
    keeps SIGINT mid-sed from leaving a `.bak` behind.
    
    This commit also carries Task 2's schema edit (the two empty
    `*_git_ref = ""` lines in manifest.toml) — per plan directive the
    Task 2 stage rolls up here so there's no intermediate "fields present
    but empty" commit. `openclaw_git_ref` gets its real value written by
    the build in the same commit; `camoufox_image_git_ref` stays empty
    until Task 5 ships the parallel build-camoufox-image.sh change.
    
    Evidence from running `rm -f app/vm/output/openclaw-agent-*.tar.zst &&
    app/scripts/build-agent-image.sh` (2m 48s, docker+zstd):
    
        artifact=.../app/vm/output/openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.416f152-dirty.tar.zst
        sha256=2bbc14f94c6bcdaac0b9d717f6dfc3e34f336507407234808ac0c918cb6db443
        size=299100052
        git_ref=416f152-dirty
    
    `grep -E '^openclaw_(artifact|git_ref|sha256|size)' app/vm/manifest.toml`
    shows all four fields match the build output byte-for-byte. The
    physical tarball exists at the advertised path (299,100,052 bytes).
    
    The `-dirty` suffix is expected here: at `compute_git_ref` time
    `build-agent-image.sh` itself is modified from HEAD (it's being edited
    by this commit), which is exactly the signal the dirty detector is
    designed to surface. A clean rebuild from the final commit before
    ship will rewrite the manifest with a non-dirty ref; tasks 5/8/13
    will re-exercise the pipeline against whatever ref is current at
    that point.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Stamp gitRef into camoufox OCI artifact name and manifest
    
    Mirror of Task 4 for camoufox. build-camoufox-image.sh now sources the
    shared `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh`, computes `GIT_REF` before the
    docker build, names the tarball `camoufox-<version>.<gitref>.tar.zst`,
    and sed-writes the four `camoufox_image_{artifact,sha256,size,git_ref}`
    keys into `app/vm/manifest.toml`. Same `trap 'rm -f …bak' EXIT` SIGINT
    hygiene.
    
    The `camoufox_image_` prefix (vs. bare `openclaw_` in Task 4) is the
    existing TOML asymmetry — don't rename per plan note.
    
    Evidence from `rm -f app/vm/output/camoufox-*.tar.zst &&
    app/scripts/build-camoufox-image.sh` (2m 40s, docker+zstd):
    
        artifact=.../app/vm/output/camoufox-135.0.1-beta.24.83f90c5-dirty.tar.zst
        sha256=9e53dca35b9454f59b8fda9a119bcef83807426aacda944b9f74991e7464d4dc
        size=670527749
        git_ref=83f90c5-dirty

    shows all four fields match byte-for-byte. Physical tarball lives at
    the advertised path (670,527,749 bytes).
    
    The openclaw (416f152) and camoufox (83f90c5) gitRefs intentionally
    differ in this intermediate state — each was built against the commit
    current at the time. A clean rebuild from the final pre-ship commit
    will unify them; Task 13's E2E exercises the full pipeline.
    
    As with Task 4, `-dirty` is the correct signal: `build-camoufox-image.sh`
    itself was modified from HEAD when `compute_git_ref` ran.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Delegate manifest writes to per-image build scripts with cache-reuse gate
    
    Now that build-agent-image.sh (Task 4) and build-camoufox-image.sh (Task 5)
    each stamp their own manifest slice, the orchestrator only needs to
    decide "rebuild or reuse" per artifact and delegate. Stripped the
    ~60 lines of `set_manifest_string` / `set_manifest_int` awk helpers;
    sources `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh` for `compute_git_ref`.
    
    `maybe_build` gate replaces the old `[ ! -f "$OPENCLAW_PATH" ]` check
    with a two-condition test:
    
        pinned_ref == compute_git_ref()   AND
        file-exists( <output>/<pinned_name> )
    
    Either side going false → delegate to the child. This fixes the prior
    dev-loop footgun: a commit bump would produce a new gitRef in the
    manifest but the stale tarball under the *old* name might still be on
    disk, and the old existence-only check would falsely report "using
    existing artifact" and ship the wrong bytes.
    
    Evidence:
    
    Step 2 — first run (stale pinned refs 416f152/83f90c5 vs current
    9298cd3-dirty, both mismatch → build both):
        time app/scripts/build-runtime-artifacts.sh
        ...
        7:01.38 total  (docker build + `docker save | zstd -19` for both
        artifacts; ~300 MB openclaw and ~670 MB camoufox)
    
    Step 3 — immediate re-run (manifest now pins 9298cd3-dirty, tarballs
    present at pinned paths → reuse both):
        time app/scripts/build-runtime-artifacts.sh
        ==> reusing openclaw tarball: openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.9298cd3-dirty.tar.zst (git_ref=9298cd3-dirty matches HEAD)
        ==> reusing camoufox tarball: camoufox-135.0.1-beta.24.9298cd3-dirty.tar.zst (git_ref=9298cd3-dirty matches HEAD)
        ...
        0.065 total  (65 ms — no docker or zstd invocations, exactly two
        file-exists checks + a git rev-parse)
    
    Step 4 — manifest consistency: all 10 keys populated, both gitRefs
    converge to 9298cd3-dirty, no blank values.
    
    Per plan Step 5 this commit carries only build-runtime-artifacts.sh
    itself. Manifest writebacks (which the orchestrator no longer owns)
    stay in Tasks 4/5's commit authority.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Add gitRef-decode + instance-cleanup tests with non-#if-DEBUG debug seams
    
    Task 7 was largely a no-op for the cleanup *body* — plan Step 1 ships
    via merge (gitRef: String? present on RuntimeArtifact), Step 4's
    cleanupStaleCacheEntries body already landed in acc8ba9a (the C1 fix
    refactored the logic into the RuntimeCacheCleaner static helper and
    re-keyed the keep-set on URL basename). The missing pieces the plan
    still asks for on top of HEAD:
    
    1. gitRef decode tests (Step 2). New `RuntimeArtifactDecodingTests`
       class, two cases:
         - testRuntimeArtifactDecodesGitRef: explicit "gitRef": "abc1234"
           decodes to .gitRef == "abc1234".
         - testRuntimeArtifactDecodesMissingGitRef: omitted field decodes
           to .gitRef == nil (the `String?` is load-bearing — legacy
           manifests without the field must still parse).
    
    2. Instance-path cleanup test (Step 5). New
       `RuntimeDownloadManagerInstanceCleanupTests` class, one case:
       `testCleanupStaleCacheEntriesRemovesUnreferencedTarballs`. Drives
       the test via the public debug seams (see below), populates a tmpdir
       with one live/one stale/one dotfile entry, asserts the right
       three-way split post-cleanup. Complementary to
       RuntimeCacheCleanerTests, which exercises the static helper; this
       one covers the instance plumbing (stateQueue dispatch on
       debugSetManifest + private cleanupStaleCacheEntries path).
    
    3. Debug seams on RuntimeDownloadManager (Step 6). Added three:
         - init(cacheDir: URL) — test-only designated initializer so
           tests can aim at a scratch tmpdir instead of AppPaths.
           runtimeCacheDirectory().
         - debugSetManifest(_:) — injects a manifest without going
           through Bundle.main.
         - debugCleanupStaleCacheEntries() — invokes the private cleanup
           synchronously on stateQueue so tests observe the filesystem
           effect before assertions run.
    
    Per plan revision I7 these are NOT `#if DEBUG`-gated. PhoenixTests
    compiles against Release in CI archive builds / diagnostics-bundle
    repackaging; a symbol that vanishes under Release would break those
    paths. The overhead is a few bytes of metadata and one convenience
    init — fine to ship in release binaries. Doc comment on
    `init(cacheDir:)` spells this out for the next reader.
    
    Verified:
      - targeted `xcodebuild test -only-testing ...` on the three

    * feat(imessage): debounce inbound to merge iMessage link-splits (#442)
    
    * feat(imessage): debounce inbound to merge iMessage link-splits
    
    iMessage commonly splits a single user intent into two near-simultaneous
    deliveries (text bubble + rich link preview), which were being processed
    as independent turns — producing two separate agent replies where one was
    intended. Buffer inbound messages per (chat_id, from) with a 1000ms
    timer that resets on each arrival, flush on timer fire or on abort, and
    merge text with blank-line separators + concatenate media arrays.

    * fix(daemon): suppress misleading gateway error during VM install/boot
    
    waitForDaemonReady() was surfacing "Plow gateway is unavailable:
    status=degraded, operator_connected=false" after its 45s timeout, even
    when the gateway was simply still booting or installing — a normal
    transient state. Only a real gateway startError warrants an error
    message; the degraded-but-booting case is handled gracefully by the
    existing status polling loop which shows .connecting until ready.

    fields, waitForDaemonReady() returns (false, nil) when /status is
    reachable but not yet ok. The log message "still unavailable" was
    misleading in that case — the endpoint IS available, just degraded.

    * fix(participate): take advisory lock before sibling-clear UPDATE
    
    The cross-row "disable siblings, then enable target" write pattern needs
    the same (user, connector) advisory lock used by upsert/delete. Without it,
    two concurrent enable-A / enable-B requests can deadlock: each takes a
    row-level lock on the sibling it cleared, then blocks waiting for the other.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Sonnet 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>
