    * Delegate manifest writes to per-image build scripts with cache-reuse gate
    
    Now that build-agent-image.sh (Task 4) and build-camoufox-image.sh (Task 5)
    each stamp their own manifest slice, the orchestrator only needs to
    decide "rebuild or reuse" per artifact and delegate. Stripped the
    ~60 lines of `set_manifest_string` / `set_manifest_int` awk helpers;
    sources `app/scripts/lib/git-ref.sh` for `compute_git_ref`.
    
    `maybe_build` gate replaces the old `[ ! -f "$OPENCLAW_PATH" ]` check
    with a two-condition test:
    
        pinned_ref == compute_git_ref()   AND
        file-exists( <output>/<pinned_name> )
    
    Either side going false → delegate to the child. This fixes the prior
    dev-loop footgun: a commit bump would produce a new gitRef in the
    manifest but the stale tarball under the *old* name might still be on
    disk, and the old existence-only check would falsely report "using
    existing artifact" and ship the wrong bytes.
    
    Evidence:
    
    Step 2 — first run (stale pinned refs 416f152/83f90c5 vs current
    9298cd3-dirty, both mismatch → build both):
        time app/scripts/build-runtime-artifacts.sh
        ...
        7:01.38 total  (docker build + `docker save | zstd -19` for both
        artifacts; ~300 MB openclaw and ~670 MB camoufox)
    
    Step 3 — immediate re-run (manifest now pins 9298cd3-dirty, tarballs
    present at pinned paths → reuse both):
        time app/scripts/build-runtime-artifacts.sh
        ==> reusing openclaw tarball: openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.9298cd3-dirty.tar.zst (git_ref=9298cd3-dirty matches HEAD)
        ==> reusing camoufox tarball: camoufox-135.0.1-beta.24.9298cd3-dirty.tar.zst (git_ref=9298cd3-dirty matches HEAD)
        ...
        0.065 total  (65 ms — no docker or zstd invocations, exactly two
        file-exists checks + a git rev-parse)
    
    Step 4 — manifest consistency: all 10 keys populated, both gitRefs
    converge to 9298cd3-dirty, no blank values.
    
    Per plan Step 5 this commit carries only build-runtime-artifacts.sh
    itself. Manifest writebacks (which the orchestrator no longer owns)
    stay in Tasks 4/5's commit authority.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Add gitRef-decode + instance-cleanup tests with non-#if-DEBUG debug seams
    
    Task 7 was largely a no-op for the cleanup *body* — plan Step 1 ships
    via merge (gitRef: String? present on RuntimeArtifact), Step 4's
    cleanupStaleCacheEntries body already landed in acc8ba9a (the C1 fix
    refactored the logic into the RuntimeCacheCleaner static helper and
    re-keyed the keep-set on URL basename). The missing pieces the plan
    still asks for on top of HEAD:
    
    1. gitRef decode tests (Step 2). New `RuntimeArtifactDecodingTests`
       class, two cases:
         - testRuntimeArtifactDecodesGitRef: explicit "gitRef": "abc1234"
           decodes to .gitRef == "abc1234".
         - testRuntimeArtifactDecodesMissingGitRef: omitted field decodes
           to .gitRef == nil (the `String?` is load-bearing — legacy
           manifests without the field must still parse).
    
    2. Instance-path cleanup test (Step 5). New
       `RuntimeDownloadManagerInstanceCleanupTests` class, one case:
       `testCleanupStaleCacheEntriesRemovesUnreferencedTarballs`. Drives
       the test via the public debug seams (see below), populates a tmpdir
       with one live/one stale/one dotfile entry, asserts the right
       three-way split post-cleanup. Complementary to
       RuntimeCacheCleanerTests, which exercises the static helper; this
       one covers the instance plumbing (stateQueue dispatch on
       debugSetManifest + private cleanupStaleCacheEntries path).
    
    3. Debug seams on RuntimeDownloadManager (Step 6). Added three:
         - init(cacheDir: URL) — test-only designated initializer so
           tests can aim at a scratch tmpdir instead of AppPaths.
           runtimeCacheDirectory().
         - debugSetManifest(_:) — injects a manifest without going
           through Bundle.main.
         - debugCleanupStaleCacheEntries() — invokes the private cleanup
           synchronously on stateQueue so tests observe the filesystem
           effect before assertions run.
    
    Per plan revision I7 these are NOT `#if DEBUG`-gated. PhoenixTests
    compiles against Release in CI archive builds / diagnostics-bundle
    repackaging; a symbol that vanishes under Release would break those
    paths. The overhead is a few bytes of metadata and one convenience
    init — fine to ship in release binaries. Doc comment on
    `init(cacheDir:)` spells this out for the next reader.
    
    Verified:
      - targeted `xcodebuild test -only-testing ...` on the three
        cleanup/decode classes → 7 tests pass in 15 ms.
      - `just app test` (full Phoenix suite) → exit 0 (2m 43s).
        (One pre-run codesign failure was artifact-dir pollution from an
        earlier xcodebuild invocation with a different PLOW_APP_NAME
        casing sharing the same derived-data path; clean rebuild after
        `rm -rf .build/xcode-derived-plow.vm-test` clears it.)

    * S3 upload: default bucket + gitRef overwrite guard
    
    Three changes to upload-runtime-artifacts.sh:
    
    1. S3_BUCKET / S3_PREFIX default to releases.plow.co / runtime (was:
       ERROR out if unset). Matches PR #297 — `just app runtime deploy`
       without env overrides is now the happy path.
    2. Collapse the duplicated OpenClaw / Camoufox blocks into a single
       `verify_and_upload "<key_prefix>"` helper. Net ~15 fewer lines;
       same two function invocations instead of two hand-rolled block
       copies.
    3. Overwrite-guard die message spells out the rationale: docker save
       is non-deterministic across machines, so an existing S3 object may
       not match this build's sha256. PR #297's hard-die semantics (no
       skip+log) is deliberately preserved per plan revision C1. Recovery
       instructions inline: bump HEAD, or `aws s3 rm` if the operator
       is certain the remote object is stale.
    
    Deliberate divergences from PR #297 (not hidden):
    - Single-manifest orchestration: PR #297 reads two TOMLs
      (vm/manifest.toml + vm/gatekeeper/manifest.toml); we collapsed to
      one during the Lima migration.
    - `PLOW_GIT_REF` env override honored in `lib/git-ref.sh` (Task 3)
      — CI/pinned-ref builds. Main's inline rev-parse had no override.
    - `lib/git-ref.sh` shared helper vs PR #297's inline git rev-parse
      in each build script. Readability.
    
    Wiring check (plan Step 3):
    
        AWS_PROFILE=__nonexistent__ app/scripts/upload-runtime-artifacts.sh
    
    produces, in order:
      1. "==> openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.b5f006a.tar.zst (sha256=...) verified"
         — proves manifest read + local sha256 verify both ran.
      2. "==> uploading openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.b5f006a.tar.zst to
         s3://releases.plow.co/runtime/openclaw-agent-2026.4.14.b5f006a.tar.zst"
         — proves upload_artifact entered the upload path (s3_exists
         returned false against the nonexistent profile).
      3. "The config profile (__nonexistent__) could not be found"
         — aws s3 cp fails on the bogus profile; script exits 255.
    
    End-to-end wire verified without touching real S3. The actual upload
    gets exercised in Task 13's release validation.

    * fix(plowd): land vm-shell at /workspace instead of /
    
    The plowd-vm-shell launcher dropped the user at the ephemeral guest root,
    which is unhelpful for poking at the mounted worktree. Pass --workdir
    /workspace so the shell opens in the worktree mount directly.
    
    Follow-up ID: T2.
    
    * refactor(phoenix): unify dev-mode OpenClaw image directory resolution
    
    RuntimeDownloadManager.imageCacheDirectory() and
    DaemonClient.resolveOpenClawImageDirectoryForMounts() each computed the
    OCI tarball directory in dev mode with different logic — the download
    manager honored PLOW_VM_BUNDLE, while DaemonClient hardcoded
    <repoRoot>/app/vm/output. These agree under `just app up` (which sets
    PLOW_VM_BUNDLE to that same path), but diverge when a Debug .app is
    launched out-of-band from Xcode with only PLOW_REPO_ROOT set.
    
    Collapse onto a single source of truth: RuntimeDownloadManager. Its
    imageCacheDirectory() now consults a shared devImageOverrideDirectory()
    helper that first tries PLOW_VM_BUNDLE and then falls back to
    <PLOW_REPO_ROOT>/app/vm/output, only returning a directory that actually
    contains `.tar.zst` tarballs. startDownloads() uses the same helper so
    it skips downloads for either override consistently. DaemonClient now
    just delegates to imageCacheDirectory(), and the test fixture unsets
    PLOW_REPO_ROOT alongside PLOW_VM_BUNDLE to keep observation tests
    deterministic.
    
    Follow-up ID: T3.
    
    * chore(phoenix): one-time cleanup of pre-Lima VZ disk artifacts on launch
    
    Existing users upgrading from the pre-Lima (VZ) runtime carry 200MB–1GB of
    dead disk that Lima never touches. Add a small idempotent cleanup that runs
    once per PhoenixApp.init(), targeting only paths wholly owned by the now
    deleted VMManager / GatekeeperVMManager:
    
      <appSupport>/vm/rootfs.img           — writable copy of the VZ OpenClaw disk
      <appSupport>/gatekeeper-vm-state/    — VZ Gatekeeper instance directory
      <appSupport>/gatekeeper-console.log  — VZ Gatekeeper serial-console log
    
    The live-Lima layout writes vm/lima.yaml + vm/provision-runtime.sh into the
    same `vm/` directory, so we delete the VZ-specific file rather than nuking
    the directory. Stale gatekeeper-vm-*.tar.zst tarballs in runtime-cache/ are
    already swept by RuntimeCacheCleaner.prune (anything not named in the live
    manifest goes), so they don't need an explicit entry.
    
    Safe for fresh installs (missing paths are a no-op) and for users who have
    already been cleaned. LegacyVZArtifactCleanup.run(appSupportRoot:) takes an
    explicit root so the behavior can be exercised against a tmpdir — three
    XCTests cover: fresh-install no-op (live lima.yaml preserved), stale-state
    removal (all three legacy paths deleted, lima.yaml preserved), idempotence.
    
    Follow-up ID: T4.
    
    * chore(vm): delete dead PLOW_VM_SHELL_PORT / ssh.localPort plumbing
    
    With the remaining SSH paths migrated to `limactl shell` in 50d844a0, no
    runtime path still reads the VM shell port — the config kept propagating

    - app/Phoenix/ServiceURLs.swift: drop `vmShellPort()` and its call from

    - app/Phoenix/DaemonClient.swift: drop the vmShellPort render-context arg.
    - app/scripts/plow-dev-env: stop deriving/exporting PLOW_VM_SHELL_PORT.

    * fix(plowd): update stale SSH error string in OAuth flow
    
    After migrating _run_oauth_flow to limactl shell in 50d844a0, the

    Follow-up ID: T1 (review fix 2).
    
    * fix(phoenix): gate PLOW_REPO_ROOT dev image override on PLOW_LAUNCH_MODE=dev
    
    devImageOverrideDirectory()'s PLOW_REPO_ROOT fallback — introduced in
    a94e747c to unify DaemonClient and RuntimeDownloadManager — was not gated
    on launch mode. A packaged .app launched from a shell that happens to
    export PLOW_REPO_ROOT (common: the user cd'd into the repo) would silently
    prefer source-tree tarballs over the downloaded, SHA-pinned cache.
    
    Require PLOW_LAUNCH_MODE=dev for the PLOW_REPO_ROOT branch so the override
    only activates in developer builds. PLOW_VM_BUNDLE is still honored
    unconditionally — `just app up` sets it explicitly, and its presence is
    itself an opt-in signal.
    
    Follow-up ID: T3 (review fix 3).
    
    * fix(vm): fail fast on CAMOUFOX_ENDPOINT_FILE write error
    
    Endpoint file is the browser-ready handoff contract to Phoenix;
    swallowing a write error wedged the app at "Browser skill starting".

    * fix(vm/openclaw): stop deleting docs dir — contains runtime workspace templates
    
    The image-slim pass was dropping /usr/local/lib/node_modules/openclaw/docs,
    which is where openclaw keeps its built-in workspace templates
    (docs/reference/templates/AGENTS.md, SOUL.md, TOOLS.md, IDENTITY.md,

    message hit "Missing workspace template: AGENTS.md (/usr/local/lib/node_modules/
    openclaw/docs/reference/templates/AGENTS.md). Ensure docs/reference/templates
    are packaged." Bug has been present since the OCI image was introduced in
    6eb70b29; only surfaced at runtime when a message triggered bootstrap.
    
    Nothing in the image-build or start-up flow writes custom docs to that
    path, and the repo carries no override copy — the rm was pure image-slim
    reflex. /root/.npm and openclaw/qa deletions remain.

    * fix(plowd/stage): cross-install plow CLI for linux-gnu, not musl (Debian container expects glibc)
    
    Our openclaw OCI image is Debian bookworm (glibc), but plowd-stage-runtime
    was cross-installing the CLI's binary-wheel deps for
    aarch64-unknown-linux-musl. pydantic_core shipped a musl-linked .so, Python
    couldn't load it in a glibc process, and /cli-packages/bin/plow exited 1
    with ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'pydantic_core._pydantic_core'.
    
    Cherry-picks the exact 2-line platform-target change from 37152be3 on
    vm/debian-migration ("Align runtime tooling with Debian packaging"), which
    never landed on main or vm/lima-migration.
    
    Verified the .so is now aarch64-linux-gnu inside the container. A separate
    CPython-ABI mismatch (manifest pins 3.12, container ships 3.11) still
    blocks `plow --version`; flagging that as follow-up.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * fix(vm): gate launch readiness on all required runtime artifacts
    
    Previously, installer + daemon launch gated on openclawVMReady alone, but Lima launch requires both openclaw and camoufox artifacts and throws runtimeIncomplete if either is missing. Users could see "ready" with camoufox missing and hit a cryptic downstream error.
    
    Introduces a declarative requiredRuntimeArtifacts list and a runtimeLaunchReady property that iterates it. The abstraction is a stepping stone to the planned multi-agent runtime architecture — new runtimes will be added to the list, not wired through new hardcoded branches.
    
    Fixes review finding from srosro on PR #310.

    * fix(vm): drop limactl-shell wait from plowd launch gate
    
    Plowd does not require limactl shell reachability before launch. Its guest-facing clients already reconnect asynchronously, so blocking the launch gate on guestAgentIsReady() added pre-plowd dead time without satisfying a real launch prerequisite.
    
    This narrows Lima readiness to the same practical condition Phoenix actually needs to start host plowd: the instance is running. Gateway/operator convergence still happens after plowd launch via the existing async retry loops, which matches the pre-Lima shape of launching the host daemon and letting the guest handshake settle afterward.
    
    * fix(vm): decouple camoufox from limactl-start critical path
    
    Restore the pre-Lima shape where the main runtime boots first and the browser sidecar comes up asynchronously afterward.
    
    plow-runtime.target now starts only openclaw, so limactl start no longer waits on camoufox image load/decompress or container start. Phoenix starts plow-camoufox.service on demand after the main daemon path is already in flight, then refreshes browser config once camoufox publishes its Playwright endpoint.
    
    This keeps the implementation close to the earlier Gatekeeper/Camoufox sidecar pattern while leaving room for a future projects/compose-style dependency declaration without introducing a new generic abstraction now.
    
    * chore(vm): add startup timing instrumentation
    
    * fix(vm): reuse stopped Lima instance instead of delete+recreate on launch
    
    The previous launch path deleted any non-running instance, so a clean app quit followed by relaunch paid Lima's full create/provision cost again. For a normal Stopped instance, Lima can resume natively with `limactl start <instance>`, which comes back in about 14 seconds instead of re-running the cold create path.
    
    Keep delete+recreate as the fallback for non-Stopped, non-Running states where reuse may be unsafe. Startup timing logs stay in place so the branch choice is visible in app.log.
    
    * chore(vm): restamp runtime manifests after second main merge
    
    * chore(vm): stamp runtime manifests against parent commit for clean rebuild
    
    * fix(vm): move startup-timing I/O off the main thread
    
    UI-facing getters like rootScreenPhase(), runtimeHeaderState(), and DaemonClient.headerState must stay pure. The startup-timing helper was still opening and appending app.log synchronously from those code paths, which is the same class of regression as dcbc44b6.
    
    Keep the greppable [startup-timing] NSLog output synchronous, but dispatch the file append work onto a serial background queue. Add a regression test that proves appendStartupTimingLog returns before the injected writer finishes and that the writer does not run on the caller thread.
    
    * chore(vm): restamp runtime manifests for current tip
    
    * fix(vm): surface aggregate runtime-artifact failures + wire retry
    
    publishStatus() now aggregates across all required runtime artifacts
    instead of reading openclaw only. If any required artifact fails
    (e.g. camoufox download hangs while openclaw succeeds), the UI
    surfaces the failure as .downloadFailed and exposes a retry
    affordance, instead of stranding the user in an infinite
    "Preparing runtime" state.

commit 1d2ff98a5e446ef6a2dcb3a96f2d6a4b6e455e2b
Author: Sam Odio <sam@odio.email>
Date:   Thu Apr 16 21:00:29 2026 -0700

    fix: off-main @Observable mutation in RuntimeDownloadManager (#335)
    
    Fixes a SIGABRT at launch when OpenClaw / Gatekeeper runtime artifacts
    are already cached from a previous install
    (incident 013D7DED-0772-443F-9A6D-92D93849F210).
    
    RuntimeDownloadManager is @Observable. markArtifactVerified mutated
    the backing flags for openclawVMReady / gatekeeperVMReady from the
    co.plow.runtime-download.state stateQueue. SwiftUI's observation
    callbacks fire synchronously on the setter's thread and touch AppKit,
    which throws an NSException — libdispatch's _dispatch_client_callout
    has no handler, so std::terminate aborts.
    
    - Dispatch the flag mutation to main, matching the existing
      publishStatus pattern.
    - Mark the five `var` queue-owned internal fields @ObservationIgnored
      so a future stored-property addition next to them doesn't silently
      reintroduce the bug.
    - Add RuntimeDownloadManagerTests covering the invariant via
      withObservationTracking from a background queue; clears
      PLOW_VM_BUNDLE / PLOW_GATEKEEPER_VM_BUNDLE in setUp so the tracked
      read doesn't short-circuit on dev machines, and NSLock-wraps the
      thread-capture box for TSAN correctness.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.7 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

commit 45c7f55e1491e109764b275213206e3247b72e76
Author: Sam Odio <sam@odio.email>

    Auto-enumerate skills into AGENTS.md + drop dead service_url (#271)
    
    * feat(plowd): auto-enumerate skills into AGENTS.md + drop dead service_url
    
    Two changes that share the same spirit — make agent-facing state flow
    deterministic instead of relying on silent dual sources of truth.
    
    Skills manifest
    ---------------
    Agents were not discovering user-authored workspace skills (e.g. a new
    colton-agent/SKILL.md dropped into /workspace/skills/) even though the
    dashboard reported them eligible. Root cause: AGENTS.md hardcoded three
    skills by name and relied on a vague "scan the skills dir if you think
    you might need something" directive for everything else. That directive
    is a coin flip — it fires only when the incoming request heuristically
    matches a description the agent has not yet seen.
    
    Fix: gateway.write_workspace_guidance() now walks
    ${workspace_dir}/skills/*/SKILL.md, parses frontmatter, and inlines a
    sorted ## Installed Skills section into AGENTS.md on every plowd start.
    Each bullet is "name — description → path", so every installed skill is
    in the system prompt by name. A sha256 skills-manifest-hash HTML comment
    plus a "debug skills" echo directive lets compliance be verified from
    outside the agent — ask "debug skills" in chat and the agent should
    respond with the current hash verbatim.
    
    The template's hardcoded plow-file-discovery / plow-vip-contacts /
    browser-usage lines and the lazy-scan fallback sentence are removed;
    all three now flow through the auto-generated manifest.
    
    Drop dead service_url from setup.json activation
    -------------------------------------------------
    Phoenix's writeActivationToken() was persisting serviceURL into
    setup.json, and _consume_pending_token() was reading it as a fallback
    via `settings.vm_plow_api_url.strip() or service_url`. But Phoenix also
    sets PLOW_VM_PLOW_API_URL in the launcher env every time it spawns
    plowd (DaemonClient.swift:2401,2463), using the same
    ServiceURLs.vmPlowAPIURL() value. In production, settings.vm_plow_api_url
    is always non-empty — so the `or service_url` branch was dead code and
    the setup.json field was pure redundancy.
    
    Fix: drop PhoenixActivationSetup.serviceURL entirely. plowd reads
    settings.vm_plow_api_url directly and logs + aborts cleanly if it is
    empty (meaning the launcher env is broken). One source of truth: Phoenix
    resolves the VM API URL, writes it to the process env, plowd reads it
    from the env.
    
    Drive-by fixes to 3 pre-existing test_gateway.py assertions that still
    asserted tmp_path would appear in rendered AGENTS.md — stale since
    default_workspace_dir was pinned to /workspace.
    
    Test state
    ----------
    - app/plowd just test: 337 passed, 7 failed (all 7 pre-existing failures
      live in test_daemon_client_source.py, test_release_scripts.py, and
      test_runtime_distribution.py — stale string-match and stale fixture
      tests from Swift refactors and runtime-artifact refactors, documented
      separately, none touch anything in this branch).

    * fix(plowd): use on-disk directory slug for SKILL.md path in manifest
    
    The ## Installed Skills manifest was emitting SKILL.md paths using the
    frontmatter `name:` field, which defeats the purpose in the exact case
    the feature targets: a user authoring a new skill whose frontmatter name
    doesn't match the directory slug. Example: a skill at
    `/workspace/skills/my-skill/SKILL.md` with `name: "My Fancy Skill"`
    would have produced a broken
    `/workspace/skills/My Fancy Skill/SKILL.md` path, so the agent could
    never read the actual skill file.
    
    Fix: carry the on-disk directory slug (`skill_dir.name`) alongside
    parsed frontmatter and use it for both the path and the display label.
    Sort by slug too, so ordering is deterministic based on filesystem
    truth rather than author-controlled frontmatter.

    * fix(plowd): address skill-manifest review nits
    
    Three followups from the post-approval self-review on PR #271.
    
    1. Drop redundant entries.sort in _build_installed_skills_section.
       `sorted(skills_dir.iterdir())` already yields subdirs in alphabetical
       order and the slug is set from `skill_dir.name` in that same loop,
       so the downstream `entries.sort(key=slug)` was dead work on every

       directory under `workspace/skills/` would previously be scanned

       into the manifest). Add an explicit guard so hidden dirs never
       enter the enumeration, regardless of contents. Includes regression
       test that plants a parseable SKILL.md inside `.git` and asserts
       it's excluded from the manifest.

       parser's behavior on realistic YAML edges was underspecified; add
       two tests that lock in current behavior — quoted values with
       internal colons (`description: "time: 10:00"`) are preserved
       intact, and indented fields nested under a parent block are
       rejected (only column-0 top-level keys are matched). Expand the

       scalars (`description: >` / `|`).

    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * bd init: initialize beads issue tracking
    
    * feat(plowd): compute per-skill partial hash for installed skills manifest
    
    Reintroduce hashlib (retired in 37eddb81) to compute
    sha256(skill_file_bytes).hexdigest()[:8] for each skill installed under
    workspace/skills/. Emit the prefix in each ## Installed Skills bullet
    as a 🔐 partial-hash marker. This is the routing-table layer of an
    arsenal-style hash gate — the agent cannot produce a valid full-hash
    response token without running `plow skill print`, and the prefix in
    the bullet is what its response hash must match. The gate directive
    prose will be wired into the AGENTS.md template in the next commit.
    
    New helper _compute_skill_file_prefix takes a Path to SKILL.md and
    returns the first SKILL_HASH_PREFIX_LEN (=8) hex chars of the sha256,
    or None if the file is unreadable. Eight hex chars = 32 bits of
    entropy, comfortably collision-free for a handful of skills.
    
    Tests:
    - test_build_installed_skills_section_emits_partial_hash_prefix asserts
      each bullet carries a backticked 8-hex-char prefix after the 🔐
      marker.
    - test_build_installed_skills_section_partial_hash_matches_sha256_of_file
      documents the contract: the prefix equals sha256(raw_bytes)[:8]
      computed directly from the file, and _compute_skill_file_prefix
      returns the same value.
    - test_build_installed_skills_section_partial_hash_changes_when_body_changes
      confirms content-sensitivity — any edit invalidates the prefix.
    - test_build_installed_skills_section_retires_canary_echo_directive is
      the rename of the old "no longer embeds full hash" test, which was
      misleadingly named since we now DO embed a partial. Its assertions
      still hold: no skills-manifest-hash HTML comment, no debug-skills
      echo directive.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * feat(workspace-template): require full-hash echo as arsenal-style gate
    
    Rewrite the ## Using Installed Skills directive to use the partial-hash
    puzzle as the forcing function, not a MUST-run directive. The previous
    version told the agent to run plow skill print before acting — which
    worked via prompt compliance but left no visible proof in the reply.
    
    New contract:
    
    1. Every skill bullet shows a partial-hash prefix (🔐 cb0a630e) — the
       first 8 chars of the skill file's sha256, computed at manifest
       render time by _build_installed_skills_section.
    2. When the user's request matches a skill, the agent MUST start its
       reply with a line like "🔐 <slug>: <64-char-sha256>", and the first
       8 chars of the echoed hash MUST match the prefix shown.
    3. The only way to obtain the full hash is to run plow skill print
       <path>, which reads the file — and the command also prints the
       skill body the agent needs to follow. Reading the file is the side
       effect; echoing the hash is the proof.
    4. Faking the hash doesn't work: sha256 is deterministic, the prefix
       is derivable from the file on disk, and any reviewer can re-verify
       compliance by grepping the reply.
    
    Compliance is now visible in the response text itself (the 🔐 line at
    the top of the reply), not buried in shell-tool exec logs. Arsenal's
    bootstrap-token pattern, ported to Plow's dynamic manifest.
    
    The example directive uses daily-rampup's current hash prefix
    (cb0a630e) so the format is obvious. The integration test
    test_write_workspace_guidance_uses_plow_owned_agents_template now
    asserts the new directive text and regexes over first-party bullets
    to confirm each has an 8-hex 🔐 prefix.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * feat(hash-gate): wrap compliance marker in HTML comment, strip on outbound
    
    Pivot the visible format of the skill-gate compliance marker from a
    plain-text "🔐 <slug>: <hash>" line to an HTML comment
    "<!-- 🔐 hash-gate <slug> <hash> -->", and strip it on the outbound
    path of the plow-imessage channel before the reply leaves the VM.
    
    The forcing function is unchanged: the agent still has to run
    `plow skill print <path>` to obtain the full sha256, whose first 8
    chars must match the partial prefix shown in the `## Installed Skills`
    manifest bullet. What's new is the UX — end users no longer see the
    gate line in their iMessage thread, but dev dogfooding still does
    (the strip is skipped when PLOW_LAUNCH_MODE=dev).
    
    The channel-side strip lives in stripHashGateComment() in send.ts
    (exported for unit testability) and runs as the first step inside
    sendMessage() before the outbound fetch. Fail-closed semantics: any
    PLOW_LAUNCH_MODE value other than "dev" — including the env var being
    unset — runs the strip, so accidental misconfiguration cannot leak
    the gate to production users. Regex matches any HTML comment whose
    body contains the literal `hash-gate` keyword, permissive by design
    so future tweaks to the marker (version strings, priority tags) don't
    silently bypass the strip.
    
    Bullet format in `## Installed Skills` drops the 🔐 emoji (since the
    bullets themselves are invisible to end users — AGENTS.md is
    agent-only) and switches to middle-dot separation:
    
        - `cb0a630e` · `daily-rampup` — Morning ramp-up brief … → …
    
    AGENTS.md gate directive rewritten to describe the new comment
    format, the MUST-echo rule, the dev/prod visibility split, and a
    concrete example using daily-rampup's real current hash.
    
    Tests:
    - send.test.ts: 10 new cases for stripHashGateComment covering top-of-reply
      strip, emoji-less variant, multi-line comment, unrelated comments passed
      through, no-op when absent, dev-mode pass-through, non-dev modes strip,
      fail-closed on missing env var, multiple gates in one reply.
    - Two new sendMessage integration cases: strip happens in prod mode,
      preserves in dev mode.
    - test_gateway.py: updated _build_installed_skills_section assertions for
      the middle-dot separator and no 🔐 in bullets. Integration test
      test_write_workspace_guidance_uses_plow_owned_agents_template now
      asserts the new directive text (hash-gate HTML comment format,
      PLOW_LAUNCH_MODE=dev mention, concrete daily-rampup example) and
      regexes the first-party bullets for the middle-dot format.
    
    Verified:
    - cd app/openclaw/channels/plow-imessage && npm test → 52 passed
    - cd app/plowd && just test → 413 passed, 7 pre-existing failures
      (all unrelated, same set tracked all session)

    * chore(skill-manifest): self-review cleanups on PR #271
    
    Three cosmetic cleanups from a self-review of the skills-manifest PR,
    all non-behavioral except the frontmatter quote-stripping:
    
    - send.ts: drop redundant `\n?` at end of HASH_GATE_RE (`\s*` already
      matches newlines). Pure noise, behavior is unchanged — the trailer
      was consuming whitespace twice.
    
    - AGENTS.md template: soften "you cannot fake the hash" to "the gate
      is a forcing function, not a cryptographic proof." Accurate — an
      agent with any file-read tool can compute sha256 without going
      through `plow skill print`. The real mechanism is that producing a
      matching hash requires touching the file, which is exactly the
      intent (load the body into context, not prove cryptographically).
      Avoids overclaiming a guarantee the gate doesn't provide.
    
    - gateway.py `_parse_skill_frontmatter`: strip a single matched pair
      of surrounding `"` or `'` quotes from parsed name/description. The
      previous behavior preserved quotes literally in the manifest bullet,
      which rendered as `` `clock` — "time is 10:00 today" `` — visible
      oddness if a skill author reached for quotes to escape an internal
      colon. Flipped the existing lock-in test
      `test_build_installed_skills_section_preserves_quoted_colon_in_description`
      to assert the new unquoted rendering, covering both `"` and `'`.

    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * plow-activate: replace tail+grep+head monitor with polling loop
    
    The Step 5 activation-code extraction was using
    `tail -F | grep --line-buffered | head -3` wrapped in a Monitor task,
    and silently missed two back-to-back codes (OK3RW, then IM19S) in a
    single session. Diagnosed root causes:
    
    1. head -3 exits as soon as three lines match and tears down the
       upstream pipe before the Monitor framework flushes stdout. Combined
       with grep's residual buffering, a single match can be produced,
       consumed by head, and the whole pipe torn down before any event
       reaches the watcher.
    2. rmup deletes the Application Support dir, so app.log's inode
       changes. tail -F polls by name but has a ~1s window where lines
       written via Swift's appendAppLog (which opens a fresh FileHandle
       per call) can land on the new inode before tail reopens it.
    3. If a first activation code times out and the installer retries, a
       second `Activation created:` line appears in the same log. head -3
       from the top might capture the stale one.
    
    Replace the pipe with a polling loop: `grep | tail -1` re-opens the
    file each tick, always picks the freshest match, and has no pipe
    state to lose. This is the Option A fix documented in the post-mortem;
    Option B (Swift writes a structured pending-activation.json) remains a
    follow-up.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * refactor(gmail): route all URL lookups through settings, drop parallel constants
    
    Root cause of the test-scenarios Gmail failures: the connector module had
    two parallel sources of truth for Google/Gmail URLs — module-level
    constants in api/plow/config.py AND matching fields on the Settings
    class. The connector's kwarg-threading scheme was half-implemented: 4
    of the 13 public functions accepted a `token_url=` / `api_base_url=`
    kwarg defaulted to the module constant, but the other 9 hardcoded
    GMAIL_API_BASE_URL directly in their bodies. Even for the 4 functions
    with kwargs, the router at api/plow/connectors/gmail/router.py never
    passed them, so every data-path call hit real Google regardless of the
    compose.test.yaml twin URL override. In tests this surfaced as
    "Google OAuth token refresh HTTP 401: invalid_client" against the
    dtu-google-oauth twin expecting a different client.
    
    This refactor deletes the parallel track:
    
    - api/plow/config.py: drop GOOGLE_OAUTH_BASE_URL, GOOGLE_OAUTH_TOKEN_URL,
      GMAIL_API_BASE_URL module constants. Inline their default strings on
      the corresponding Settings fields. Settings is now the only source of
      truth for these URLs.
    
    - api/plow/connectors/gmail/connector.py: import `settings` directly
      instead of the three dead constants. Delete the unused
      GOOGLE_OAUTH_AUTHORIZE_URL module constant. Drop the
      `oauth_base_url=` / `token_url=` / `api_base_url=` kwargs from
      build_gmail_oauth_url, exchange_gmail_authorization_code,
      refresh_gmail_access_token, fetch_gmail_profile, list_gmail_messages,
      get_gmail_message, and send_gmail_message — 11 kwarg lines removed.
      Every URL reference in every function body now reads
      `settings.google_oauth_base_url`, `settings.google_oauth_token_url`,
      or `settings.gmail_api_base_url` directly, including the 9 body sites
      (reply, forward, get_attachment, labels, modify_labels, list_drafts,
      create_draft, send_draft, delete_draft) that were hardcoded to
      GMAIL_API_BASE_URL and therefore impossible to override by any
      caller. Matches the existing settings-import pattern in
      provider.py and router.py.
    
    - api/plow/connectors/gmail/provider.py: drop the redundant
      `oauth_base_url=` / `token_url=` / `api_base_url=` kwargs from the

    * fix: persist env-derived URLs before macOS can strip --env on restart
    
    plow-activate kept losing the VM API URL after macOS relaunched the app
    for a Full Disk Access grant. The chain:
    
    1. `just app rmup` launches Plow Dev wt3 via `open -W --env
       PLOW_VM_PLOW_API_URL=https://plow.ngrok.io ... Plow Dev wt3.app`.
    2. The first process has the env var set, but nothing calls
       `ServiceURLs.vmPlowAPIURL()` on that process — the only callers live
       in `DaemonClient.daemonLaunchConfig`, which doesn't fire until after
       activation succeeds.
    3. macOS grants Full Disk Access and restarts the app via
       LSOpenCFURLRef. The restarted process has zero PLOW_ env vars.
    4. Activation eventually completes, `daemonLaunchConfig` runs, and
       `vmPlowAPIURL()` is called for the first time — on the *second*
       process, with no env var, so it falls through to
       `cloudAPIURL()` and plowd writes `http://slowdown:8000` into the
       VM's `openclaw/gateway/plow-api-url`. The OpenClaw plow-ws client
       then fails to reach the API and the agent never greets.
    
    The four getters that VMManager happens to call in its init
    (`plowdPort`, `gatewayPort`, `vmShellPort`, `cloudAPIURL`) don't hit
    this bug because their persistence side effect runs on the first
    process, before the restart. `vmPlowAPIURL` was the odd one out:
    nothing read it early, so its persistence path was dead on first
    launch.
    
    Fix: add an explicit `ServiceURLs.captureEnvironmentForRestartSurvival`
    that reads every env-derived URL/port once so each getter persists to
    disk, and call it from `PhoenixApp.init` before anything else runs.
    This consolidates the "capture env vars early" concern in one place
    with documentation, instead of relying on the implicit coincidence
    that VMManager's init happens to read most of them.
    
    Ran `just app test` → TEST SUCCEEDED.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * Address PR #201 review: schema tightening, reply-all To/Cc split, CLI cleanup
    
    - Add min_length=1 to GmailSendRequest.to, GmailForwardRequest.to, and

      a (to, cc) tuple: the original sender stays in To and the original

      addr-spec, quoted display names with commas, primary-is-self promotion,

    * Address PR #38 follow-up review: reliability + robustness fixes
    
    Seven distinct fixes grouped because they share the same review thread and
    touch overlapping files. Each is scoped narrowly to the concrete bug.
    
    1. Surface a 502 when every Gmail account in a multi-account search fails
       (api/plow/connectors/gmail/router.py). _search_single_account now returns
       (messages, err) so the aggregator can distinguish "no results" from
       "every account errored". Partial failure still degrades gracefully and
       returns what succeeded; the 502 fires only when there is nothing else
       to show. Masking a broken refresh token or a rate-limit as an empty
       200 OK is worse than telling the caller the request failed. Covered by
       a new test_search_returns_502_when_all_accounts_fail router test.
    
    2. Unify the settings source inside the Gmail router
       (api/plow/connectors/gmail/router.py). _require_gmail_connection now
       reads request.app.state.settings like _get_all_gmail_connections, instead
       of the module-level plow.config.settings. Test harnesses override
       app.state.settings via _make_client, so the previous import meant
       single-account code paths silently ignored test overrides. Dropped the
       module-level import since it has no other uses.
    
    3. Extend the advisory lock to every connector_tokens write path
       (api/plow/db/connectors.py). Extracted _lock_connector_row helper and
       called it from upsert_connector_token, delete_connector_token, and
       set_default_connector_token. Previously only upsert held the lock, so
       two concurrent set-default calls (or a delete that triggered
       _promote_default_if_needed racing with an upsert) could both clear and
       re-assign is_default and violate connector_tokens_one_default_idx. The
       partial unique index would catch the collision, but the loser would
       surface as a 500 instead of serializing cleanly.
    
    4. Drop the _EmptyBody sentinel from the Gmail CLI
       (cli/plow/commands/gmail.py). api_post already accepts BaseModel | None
       and emits "{}" when payload is None. The CLI was instantiating an
       _EmptyBody for the disconnect and set-default calls, which served no
       purpose beyond satisfying the old non-optional signature. Passing None
       directly removes dead code and the pydantic import.
    
    5. Fall back to stripped HTML when quoting a reply or forward whose
       original has no text/plain part (api/plow/connectors/gmail/connector.py).
       Added a small HTMLParser-based _HTMLTextExtractor and _quotable_body
       helper that prefers text_body and degrades to HTML. Before this, users
       replying to an HTML-only newsletter got an empty quoted block with no
       explanation. Uses stdlib html.parser — no new dependency.
    
    6. Replace startswith-based subject prefix checks with regexes
       (api/plow/connectors/gmail/connector.py). _RE_SUBJECT_PREFIX matches
       re/aw/antw with optional [n] or (n) suffixes so replies to already
       threaded mail ("Re[2]: subject") do not become "Re: Re[2]: subject".
       _FWD_SUBJECT_PREFIX covers fw, fwd, and wg.
    
    7. Cap attachment size in _get_gmail_attachment
       (api/plow/connectors/gmail/connector.py). Added MAX_GMAIL_ATTACHMENT_BYTES
       (32 MiB — Gmail's own ceiling is 25 MiB, with headroom) and raise
       GmailConnectorError if the server-reported size is over. This also
       bounds forward_gmail_message's per-attachment fetch loop so a multi-
       attachment forward cannot balloon memory on an API worker.
    
    Tests: api test-fast = 515 passed, cli check = 47 passed, lint + basedpyright
    clean in both projects.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    * app: variant-aware `just app test` + ruff format follow-up
    
    Two small follow-ups from running the full root `just test-fast` for the
    first time in a fresh worktree:
    
    1. `app/justfile` `test` recipe was the last Xcode-touching recipe that
       silently fell back to the non-variant `Plow Dev` / `co.plow.app.dev`
       when no `PLOW_VARIANT` was resolved, AND did not pass
       `-derivedDataPath`, so xcodebuild wrote the test host into Xcode's
       global DerivedData. Exactly the gap flagged in section 1 of
       `plans/2026-04-10-variant-aware-everywhere.md`.
    
       Repaired to mirror the variant plumbing used by `up` / `build` /
       `package`: resolve variant from an optional positional or `.env.local`,
       derive `variant_id`, `variant_name`, `effective_bundle_id`,
       `effective_app_name`, and per-variant `derived_path`, then pass
       `-derivedDataPath "$derived_path"` to xcodebuild. `variant=""` still
       works for CI / release contexts but now refuses to proceed when the
       machine has any `co.plow.app.dev.*` Application Support dirs — if
       variant data exists on the machine, running the non-variant bundle is
       almost always a worktree misconfiguration, and the error is more
       helpful than silent cross-variant corruption.
    
       Prints a one-line banner before invocation so the operator sees
       exactly which variant / bundle / derived-data path the test host is
       about to use, and `-quiet` drops the per-test chatter now that the
       banner carries the context.
    
       Verified: with `PLOW_VARIANT=pr38` in `.env.local`, the whole root
       `just test-fast` chain now runs clean in a fresh worktree and lands
       the Swift test host at
       `../.build/xcode-derived-pr38/Build/Products/Debug/Plow Dev pr38.app`
       with bundle id `co.plow.app.dev.pr38`. No touches to
       `~/Library/Application Support/co.plow.app.dev/` or to other
       worktrees' variant dirs.
    
    2. `ruff format` wanted one line in `api/plow/connectors/gmail/connector.py`
       collapsed from a multi-line `raise` into a single line. Harmless
       mechanical reflow; root `just test-fast` runs `ruff format --check`
       and would have failed without it.
    
    Root `just test-fast` on this worktree now passes end-to-end:
      api 515, cli 47, dtu-linq 22, dtu-gmail 22, dtu-google-oauth 13,
      plowd 6, Phoenix (variant-isolated) exit 0. All lint + basedpyright
      clean across every subproject.

    * api: variant-aware _ensure-db{s} + test-fast (drop hardcoded 55432/55433)
    
    Before: `api/justfile` had `_test_compose := "PLOW_DB_PORT=55432
    PLOW_TEST_DB_PORT=55433 docker compose -f ../compose.yaml"`. This hardcoded
    host ports for every `just api test-fast` invocation and — more importantly —
    never set `PLOW_COMPOSE_PROJECT`, so compose fell back to its default (`plow`)
    no matter which worktree triggered it. Two worktrees couldn't run tests in
    parallel: the second would recreate the first worktree's containers and they'd
    race on the host ports.
    
    Meanwhile `compose.yaml` is already variant-aware (line 3:
    `name: ${PLOW_COMPOSE_PROJECT:-plow}`, each service's `ports:` reading
    `${PLOW_*_PORT:-...}`), and `api/justfile`'s `up` recipe already uses
    `.plow-dev-env` via `docker compose --env-file`. The test recipes just
    skipped that machinery.
    
    After:
    
    1. New `_ensure-dev-env` helper regenerates `../.plow-dev-env` from
       `PLOW_VARIANT` (or `../.env.local`) idempotently. Same pattern as `up`.
    
    2. `_ensure-db` and `_ensure-dbs` are bash-script recipes that depend on
       `_ensure-dev-env` and use
       `docker compose --env-file ../.plow-dev-env -f ../compose.yaml`. Each
       worktree's test stack lands on its own project name (`plow-pr38`,
       `plow-wt1`, …) with disjoint host ports derived from the variant slot
       hash. Parallel `just api test-fast` across multiple worktrees is now
       safe — verified locally by watching `docker ps` show both `plow-pr38-*`
       and the legacy `plow-*` containers coexisting on 18952/18953 and
       55432/55433 respectively.
    
    3. `test-fast` is now a bash-script recipe that, after `_ensure-dbs`
       brings the containers up, sources `../.plow-dev-env` and exports
       `TEST_DB_PORT` and `DB_PORT` to match the variant's test-db host port.
       `api/tests/testenv.py`'s `setdefault` honors the exports over the
       committed `.env.test-common` values, so pytest connects to the right
       container.
    
    4. Dropped the `_test_compose` constant — nothing references it anymore.
    
    CI path is untouched. `test-ci` (the recipe CI uses) does not depend on
    `_ensure-*`, and CI boots Postgres service containers directly on host
    55432/55433 before exporting DB_PORT/TEST_DB_PORT itself. `.env.test-common`
    keeps 55433 as a bare-`pytest` fallback for that flow.
    
    Verified: root `just test-fast` in the `pr38` worktree runs clean —
    api 515, cli 47, dtu-linq 22, dtu-gmail 22, dtu-google-oauth 13, plowd 6,
    Phoenix variant-isolated, all lint + basedpyright green. Pre-existing
    `plow-db-1` / `plow-test-db-1` containers left alone.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * connector: revert subject-prefix regex, keep simple startswith
    
    Reverts the regex-based Re:/Fwd: prefix detection from fix #6 of the
    PR #38 follow-up review commit. Going back to `startswith("re:")` and
    `startswith(("fwd:", "fw:"))`.
    
    Why: the regex was cosmetic polish, not correctness. Gmail threading is
    determined by In-Reply-To / References / threadId, not subject text, so
    the only thing a prefix check controls is whether the sent folder shows
    "Re: Project status" or "Re: Re[2]: Project status". The regex added a
    maintenance burden (two patterns, whack-a-mole for every localized prefix)
    for zero functional improvement, and carried a minor false-positive risk
    on subjects like `re:port:`.
    
    If someone ever complains about stacked prefixes on a localized thread,
    the fix belongs next to a real test case, not as preemptive i18n.
    
    `fw:` / `fwd:` detection is preserved — that was already a `startswith`
    tuple on the tip of the branch before fix #6.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * gmail: stop threading forwards into the original conversation
    
    forward_gmail_message was passing threadId on send, which appended the
    forward into the source thread. Native Gmail forwards break the thread
    and start a new conversation; doing otherwise surprises both senders and
    recipients (and contradicts the PR description, which already claimed
    this behavior).
    
    Drop the threadId branch from the forward send body and add a regression
    test asserting forwards never carry threadId.

    * gmail: surface per-account failures via DataResponse.meta.degraded_accounts
    
    Multi-account search aggregated per-account failures, logged them, and
    returned 200 OK with a silently-truncated result set. A client looking
    at search results had no way to know one account had silently dropped
    out — "no mail" and "your other gmail token was just revoked" looked
    identical.
    
    Add an optional `meta` dict to DataResponse (existing clients ignore it)
    and populate `meta.degraded_accounts` on partial failures with the
    account identifier and stringified error per failed account. Full
    success keeps `meta` absent. The all-fail 502 path is unchanged.
    
    Cover both cases in the router test: partial failure asserts the
    degraded entry is present; full success asserts meta is None.

    * db: scope list_connector_tokens by user_id to prevent IDOR
    
    list_connector_tokens(session, connector) filtered only by connector,

    * app: isolate `just app test` DerivedData from `up`/`build` to stop FDA churn
    
    The `test` recipe forces `CODE_SIGN_IDENTITY=- CODE_SIGNING_REQUIRED=NO`
    and, since 6ba6e312, was writing into the same per-variant DerivedData
    (`../.build/xcode-derived-${variant_id}`) that `just app up` and `just
    app build` use. That meant a `just app test` run would overwrite the
    dev-signed `Plow Dev (variant).app` bundle with an ad-hoc-signed copy,
    flipping its cdhash and the designated requirement TCC matches against,
    which broke the FDA grant on the next launch.
    
    Point the test recipe at a sibling `…-${variant_id}-test` (or
    `xcode-derived-dev-test` for the non-variant case) so the test host
    build never touches the bundle the user actually launches and grants
    permissions to. Costs an extra DerivedData tree per variant; eliminates
    the cross-contamination.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * app: give `just app test` a distinct bundle id to stop FDA churn
    
    Follow-up to b8826826. Separating DerivedData paths was necessary but
    not sufficient: the test host and the up/build bundle still shared
    `co.plow.app.dev[.variant]`, so LaunchServices kept both registered
    and could launch either one under the same bundle id. When the test
    variant (ad-hoc signed, no designated requirement) got picked, TCC
    stored or matched its csreq against that ad-hoc cdhash, and the next
    dev-signed rebuild no longer matched — Full Disk Access silently
    reverted without any user action.
    
    Give the test target its own bundle id (`co.plow.app.dev[.variant].test`)
    and its own .app name ("Plow Dev [variant] Test") so LaunchServices
    and TCC treat them as two different apps. Drop the now-obsolete
    non-variant collision guard it was compensating for.
    
    Verified end-to-end: `just test` passes against the new naming, and
    `/plow-activate` successfully re-grants FDA against the dev-signed
    binary without the test host stealing the bundle id.

      require_scope so reply/forward stop carrying unused _read_auth/_att_auth
      parameters; existing test fixtures keep working because the primary scope
      still routes through require_scope.
    
    * plans: multi-account Gmail routing design + 402 cross-reference
    
    Spec for fixing the silent fall-through-to-default-account routing bug
    that surfaced on chat_1 msg_88–90 as "those messages may live in a
    separate mailbox the Gmail API can't directly retrieve" (real cause:
    messages.get routed to the wrong connector token because the OpenClaw
    tool plugin has no way to pass account from a search result).
    
    Design:
    - account required at every layer (API schemas, FastAPI route,
      CLI parser, OpenClaw tool schemas)
    - messages.list stays optional-account for multi-account fan-out,
      which is the mechanism the agent uses to discover which account
      a message lives in
    - PLOW_GMAIL_DEFAULT_ACCOUNT env var as a CLI-only human convenience;
      never used on the agent path
    - CLI api_post emits structured error JSON on stdout before non-zero
      exit so the tool plugin returns typed error fields to the LLM
      instead of a stringified shell error
    - TOOLS.md/AGENTS.md/USER.md updates teach the agent the routing rule
      and the "report tool errors verbatim, never fabricate" rule
    
    Also cross-references the agent-402 bug doc so the shared
    hallucination meta-bug isn't split across two unlinked plans.

    * cli(gmail): resolve account from -a or PLOW_GMAIL_DEFAULT_ACCOUNT, no silent default
    
    Replace _require_account with _resolve_account:
      1. --account / -a beats everything
      2. PLOW_GMAIL_DEFAULT_ACCOUNT env var as a human convenience
      3. Error out with a message naming both mechanisms
    
    Every non-search gmail subcommand (get, send, reply, forward, attachment,
    labels, label, archive/star/read/unread shortcuts, drafts, draft-create,
    draft-send, draft-delete) now resolves the account before building its
    request. search is exempt — its account stays optional so server-side
    fan-out still works. set-default keeps its own strict 'account is
    required' path (no env-var fallback) because 'make unknown account
    default' is nonsense. disconnect keeps its explicit ?account= query
    param.
    
    The env var is a CLI-only convenience for humans running 'plow gmail' in
    a terminal. The OpenClaw tool plugin does not set or read it, so the
    agent path (Task 5) always passes an explicit -a.
    
    Previously-passing test_reply_without_account_falls_back_to_default and
    test_labels_without_account_falls_back_to_default were documenting the
    OLD silent-fallback behavior that caused the chat_1 routing bug — they
    are replaced with test_*_without_account_exits_with_error counterparts
    that assert SystemExit(1) and a helpful stderr message.
    
    Four new positive tests cover env-var resolution, explicit-beats-env
    precedence, and search's exemption from the rule.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * cli: emit structured JSON error on stdout in api_post before exiting
    
    The OpenClaw tool plugin (Task 6) captures plow CLI stdout as the tool
    result. Previously an HTTP error turned into a shell-exit-1 with a flat
    stderr string that the plugin wrapped into 'plow exited with code 1:
    /v1/... failed (502): ...'. The LLM then paraphrased that into
    'returning 404' or 'messages live in a separate mailbox the Gmail API
    can't directly retrieve' — because the status code was buried in prose,
    the LLM had no typed field to latch onto.
    
    api_post now prints
      {\"error\": {\"path\": \"/v1/...\", \"status_code\": 502, \"detail\": \"...\"}}
    on stdout before exiting 1, and keeps the human-readable message on
    stderr. The tool plugin (Task 6) parses stdout regardless of exit code
    and hands the LLM typed fields.
    
    Two new tests cover the JSON shape (with a parseable detail body and a
    fallback where response.json() throws).

    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * openclaw(plow-cli): parse structured CLI errors and expose for testing
    
    runPlow no longer rejects on non-zero exit. The CLI (cli/plow/client.py
    api_post, Task 4) now emits a JSON error payload on stdout before
    exiting 1, and makeToolExecute tries JSON.parse(stdout) first. A parsed
    object with an 'error' key is returned verbatim — the LLM sees typed
    fields like error.status_code=502 and error.detail='Gmail API error:
    ...' instead of a pre-stringified 'plow exited with code 1: ...' shell
    error.
    
    The hallucinated '404' / 'different mailbox' paraphrase in chat_1
    msg_90 was possible because the status code was buried in prose; now
    it's a typed integer the LLM can read directly.
    
    Fallback paths:
      - stdout parses as JSON, no 'error' key → success payload
      - stdout parses as JSON, has 'error' key → error payload (as-is)
      - stdout doesn't parse, exit 0              → { output: stdout }
      - stdout doesn't parse, exit != 0           → { error: { kind: 'subprocess', ... } }
      - spawn-level error (ENOENT, timeout)       → { error: { kind: 'subprocess', message } }
    
    index.test.js uses node --test (built-in, zero-deps) and covers:
      - every required-account gmail tool lists 'account' in schema
      - plow_gmail_search and plow_gmail_status don't
      - makeToolExecute round-trips a structured error payload
      - makeToolExecute round-trips a success payload on exit 0
      - makeToolExecute falls back to subprocess-error on non-JSON exit != 0
    
    makeToolExecute and __setRunPlowForTests are exported for test-time
    substitution; _runPlowImpl is a module-level mutable reference that
    defaults to the spawn-based runPlowReal and can be swapped for fakes.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * openclaw(agents): teach the agent gmail multi-account + error-reporting rules
    
    AGENTS.md now has two new sections that close the behavioral half of
    the multi-account routing fix and the broader agent hallucination
    meta-bug:
    
      Gmail — multi-account rules
        - call plow_gmail_status first to discover connected accounts +
          default
        - thread 'account' from plow_gmail_search results verbatim into
          follow-up tool calls
        - pick the from-account explicitly for send/draft_create
        - never reuse a message_id across accounts — guaranteed 502
    
      Reporting tool errors
        - read error.status_code and error.detail literally, no paraphrasing
        - 402 means out of credits; tell the user, do not retry, do not
          call another LLM-backed tool in the same turn
        - no fabricated recovery narration ('maybe it lives in a different
          mailbox', 'the connector might not support this')
        - no pre-tool preamble ('forwarding it now' before the forward
          tool returns)
    
    test_installer_view_source.py now contains two string-assertion guards
    (test_agents_md_has_gmail_multi_account_routing_rules and
    test_agents_md_has_error_reporting_rules) so someone editing AGENTS.md
    can't silently delete the rules.

    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * fix(ws): force-kill half-open WebSocket on close timeout
    
    When the backend connection dies silently (TCP half-open), ws.close()
    hangs in CLOSING state waiting for a close handshake that never comes.
    The heartbeat detects the dead connection via pong timeout, but the
    socket stays stuck for minutes until the OS TCP stack gives up.
    
    Add a 5s close timeout that force-kills the socket and triggers
    reconnect if onclose doesn't fire after ws.close(). Worst-case
    detection drops from 10+ minutes to ~30 seconds.

    * fix: address PR review — migration precision, CLI JSON errors, routing distinctness
    
    Five fixes flagged in PR review:
    
    1. Migration backfill: only mark the oldest token per (user_id, connector)
       as default. The old UNIQUE (user_id, connector) constraint made the
       blanket update safe in practice, but a more precise SQL form is robust
       against stray rows and documents intent.
    
    2. CLI _resolve_account errors now emit structured JSON on stdout so the
       OpenClaw plugin can read typed status_code / detail fields instead of
       scraping stderr. Without this, the hallucination fix broke down for the
       "missing --account" failure mode specifically — which is exactly where
       the agent used to invent "404" paraphrases. `exit_error` is extended
       with optional status_code and path kwargs; existing callers unchanged.
    
    3. require_connector_token now raises ConnectorAccountNotFoundError when a
       specific account_identifier was requested but not found, and the Gmail
       router maps it to HTTP 404 with a status-checking hint. Previously both
       "nothing connected" and "wrong account name" collapsed into a single
       503, making typos look like transient outages.
    
    4. GmailMessageSummary.account is now required (no `""` default). The
       connector layer stamps it from connection.email_address at construction
       time, so every response path sets it explicitly — `_with_account` is
       gone. A routing bug that skips this step now fails Pydantic validation
       at construction instead of silently emitting an empty-string field.
    
    5. Slack provider validates account_identifier at the source: if Slack
       accepts the OAuth exchange but returns neither a team nor a user id,
       the provider raises 502 with a Slack-specific message instead of
       letting the empty string reach oauth_callback's generic check.
    
    New tests:
    - api/tests/db/test_connectors.py: require_connector_token raises the
      right exception for "nothing connected" vs. "wrong account."
    - api/tests/connectors/gmail/test_api_router.py: wrong-account → 404.
    - api/schemas/tests/test_api_schemas.py: missing account on
      GmailMessageSummary fails Pydantic validation.
    - api/tests/connectors/slack/test_provider.py: OAuth response with no
      team/user id surfaces a typed 502 at the provider.
    - cli/tests/test_gmail_command.py: stdout JSON payload verified for
      reply, labels, and set-default missing-account paths.

    * refactor(gmail): split connection types, cache OAuth tokens, add Depends factory
    
    - `GmailConnection` now carries a freshly-validated `access_token` and a
      required `email_address`. The pre-profile-fetch state moves to a new
      `GmailUnboundConnection` so the type system enforces "every connector
      call has an owning mailbox" instead of running asserts at runtime.
    
    - `token_service.get_gmail_connection` reads `token.access_token` /
      `token.token_expiry` and reuses the cached value when it's still valid;
      otherwise it refreshes against Google and persists. The connector
      module no longer refreshes per call — every call gets a ready-to-use
      token, eliminating one OAuth round-trip per Gmail API request and
      ~8x for multi-account fanout.
    
    - New `require_gmail(...)` Depends factory replaces per-endpoint
      `_require_gmail_connection(...)` boilerplate. Endpoints now declare
      their needs with `Depends(require_gmail("messages.get"))` and call
      `await gmail(body.account)` to resolve. The shared
      `_require_gmail_connection` helper remains as a single seam for tests.
    
    - Aggregate attachment cap (`MAX_GMAIL_FORWARD_TOTAL_BYTES = 50 MB`) on
      `forward_gmail_message`, plus a `_post_raw_message` helper that DRYs
      send/reply/forward/draft-create's identical send-tail.

    * refactor: rename account_identifier → account; drop derived Swift state
    
    The connector_tokens DB column is named `account_identifier` for migration
    history reasons. The Python attribute, function kwargs, and request bodies
    already use `account` everywhere they touch users — this commit aligns the
    remaining seams (model attribute, repository, OAuth provider results, raw
    helper kwargs) so the DB-column suffix stops leaking into router/Swift code.
    
    The model uses `mapped_column("account_identifier", String)` so the DB
    column name is preserved (no migration). A new `test_models.py` case
    asserts the mapping in both directions to lock the contract.
    
    Also drops the `agentReady`/`warmupStatus` derived state in `SettingsView`
    that the recent `RuntimeHeaderState` unification made redundant. `agentReady`
    now reads `client.headerState == .running` directly, which is the canonical
    "VM ready and connected and not degraded" signal.

commit e2cef32dec7dfde6a73283bed553691b85ad7eb7
Author: swagatpatel <swagatpatel@users.noreply.github.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 9 22:24:12 2026 -0700

    Fall back to nearby host port when OpenClaw gateway port 18789 is taken (#199)
    
    * Fall back to nearby host port when OpenClaw gateway port 18789 is taken
    
    If the user already has another OpenClaw gateway bound to 127.0.0.1:18789
    (e.g. installed separately from npm), Plow's VM Bridge D silently failed
    to bind and downstream clients either got connection-refused or — worse —
    talked to the wrong gateway without anyone noticing.
    
    Now, before binding Bridge D, PhoenixVMManager does a POSIX bind probe
    starting at the preferred host port (default 18789). On conflict it scans
    forward up to 10 consecutive ports, emits a loud WARNING log with a
    greppable [GATEWAY-PORT-FALLBACK] tag, setenv's PLOW_GATEWAY_PORT so
    subsequent in-process readers and the soon-to-be-launched plowd child
    process inherit the resolved port, and re-persists via ServiceURLs so the
    choice survives macOS-initiated restarts.
    
    Pair fixes:
    - Bridge D (and the VM-shell loopback bridge) now attach a
      stateUpdateHandler that loudly logs NWListener .failed/.ready/.cancelled
      transitions instead of swallowing async bind failures.
    - ServiceURLs.env is now a dynamic computed property so setenv() is
      actually visible to subsequent gatewayPort() callers.
    - DaemonClient pins PLOW_GATEWAY_PORT explicitly in plowd's launch env
      for belt-and-suspenders coverage alongside env inheritance.
    
    The in-VM gateway still binds guest-local 127.0.0.1:18789 unchanged —
    it's hardcoded in openclaw-start.sh's --port flag and the init socat
    bridge. Only the host-side Bridge D listener moves. Bridge D's vsock
    port is also still 18789 (vsock namespace is isolated from host TCP),
    so no VM image or rootfs changes are required.
    
    PortScanner is a small pure helper with unit tests covering the
    happy path, single-conflict fallback, multi-conflict fallback, and
    exhaustion error.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * debug(ci): drop -quiet from test recipe to surface DiagnosticsBundler failures
    
    The App build (macOS) CI job has been red since #194 merged because 21
    DiagnosticsBundlerTests fail on the macos-15-arm64 runner but not on any
    local dev machine. With -quiet, xcodebuild only prints compile warnings
    and the final "Failing tests" list — no XCTAssert messages, line numbers,
    or stack traces. This makes the failures impossible to diagnose from CI
    logs alone.
    
    Temporarily drop -quiet so the next CI run prints per-test output.
    Will re-add -quiet once the underlying tests are fixed.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
    
    * Fix DiagnosticsBundler main-thread crash in writePermissions
    
    NSApplication.activationPolicy is a main-thread-only API, but
    DiagnosticsBundler.writePermissions was being called from bundle()'s
    background cooperative queue. On Xcode 16.4 / macOS 15.7.4 (the CI
    runner) Main Thread Checker catches this and aborts the test process
    with SIGABRT, crashing 21 DiagnosticsBundlerTests. Newer Xcode builds
    on macOS 26 beta apparently don't enforce the check, which is why this
    was green on author and reviewer machines.
    
    Fix: make writePermissions async and hop to MainActor.run just for the
    NSApp?.activationPolicy() read. The other permission checks
    (AXIsProcessTrusted, CNContactStore, AVCaptureDevice, CG screen capture)
    are thread-safe and stay inline. Update the writer closure in bundle()
    to await the now-async call. All 31 DiagnosticsBundlerTests pass
    locally after the change.
    
    Also re-add -quiet to the test recipe now that the debug trip is
    complete.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

    Co-authored-by: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>

commit bb156adf52d533a4deb04a1c6d061aab24e45c71
Author: swagatpatel <swagatpatel@users.noreply.github.com>
Date:   Wed Apr 8 13:05:44 2026 -0700

    Fix menu bar dot invisible in production + onboarding interstitial race (#169)
    
    Two follow-up fixes from PR #145 review:
    
    1. MenuBarIcon: the composited NSImage used isTemplate = !isDev, making
       the green/red connection dot monochrome (invisible) in production.
       Switch to a SwiftUI ZStack overlay so the dot is a real colored Circle
       rendered on top of the template icon — visible in all builds.
    
    2. Onboarding race: hasCompletedInstall was used to both gate the
       interstitial and mark runtime readiness. If the VM finished
       downloading before the user completed activation, completeInstall()
       fired and the interstitial was skipped entirely. Add a separate
       persisted hasPassedInterstitial flag so the two concerns are
       decoupled — the interstitial is always shown on first install
       regardless of runtime timing.

commit 7f6e540a4a9b46758d4e0829da5eedc2f51e27aa
Author: swagatpatel <swagatpatel@users.noreply.github.com>
Date:   Wed Apr 8 09:05:52 2026 -0700

    Fix audit log: parse ISO 8601 timestamps with fractional seconds (#163)
    
    * fix: parse ISO 8601 timestamps with fractional seconds in activity log
    
    The daemon (plowd) emits timestamps via Python's datetime.isoformat()
    which includes microseconds (e.g. 2026-04-07T22:55:52.348123+00:00).
    The default ISO8601DateFormatter in Swift cannot parse fractional seconds,
    causing all activity log entries to fall back to "just now".
    
    Add a parseISO8601 helper that tries fractional-seconds format first,
    then falls back to the standard format for compatibility.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Paperclip <noreply@paperclip.ing>
    
    * test: add XCTest unit tests for ISO 8601 timestamp parsing fix
    
    Tests cover ApprovalRequest.parseISO8601 with fractional seconds (Python
    daemon format), standard ISO 8601, Z suffix, empty/invalid strings, plus
    AgeDescription and TimestampDescription fallback behavior. All 49 tests pass.
    
    Co-Authored-By: Paperclip <noreply@paperclip.ing>
    
    * test: expand ISO 8601 timestamp test coverage for edge cases
    
    Added 7 new test cases across 3 new scenarios:
    - ISO8601ParsingTests: fractional seconds with Z suffix, milliseconds
      (3-digit), negative timezone offset, and sub-second precision
      preservation
    - ResolutionDescriptionTests: full coverage for
      ApprovalHistoryEntry.resolutionDescription (fractional, standard,
      invalid, empty) — previously untested
    
    Co-Authored-By: Paperclip <noreply@paperclip.ing>

    Co-authored-by: Paperclip <noreply@paperclip.ing>

commit 9a7590373e3ba40e3c9c8760e0c25e2ae7e9feea
Author: Sam Odio <sam@odio.email>
Date:   Mon Mar 30 10:45:14 2026 -0700

    Gatekeeper VM split: parallel VMs with S3-downloaded images (#63)
    
    Split the single Alpine VM into two parallel VMs — OpenClaw (Alpine) for the
    gateway and Gatekeeper (Debian) for Camoufox browser automation. VM images
    are no longer bundled in the app; they are downloaded from S3 on first launch.
    
    Architecture:
    - OpenClaw VM (Alpine, 2GB): runs the OpenClaw gateway with baked-in binary
    - Gatekeeper VM (Debian, 4GB, 2 GiB RAM): runs Camoufox via Playwright with
      baked-in browser binary, communicates with OpenClaw via cross-VM vsock bridge
    - Both VMs boot from tar.zst images downloaded from S3 (~280MB + ~915MB)
    - App bundle no longer ships VM images — much smaller install size
    - Local dev bypasses S3 via PLOW_VM_BUNDLE / PLOW_GATEKEEPER_VM_BUNDLE env vars
    
    Build pipeline:
    - build-vm-image bakes OpenClaw tgz into Alpine rootfs
    - build-gatekeeper-image bakes Camoufox zip into Debian rootfs (preserving
      chmod +x for zip archives that strip Unix permissions)
    - Both scripts produce tar.zst tarballs and write SHA256/size to manifest.toml
    - generate-runtime-manifest.py reads both manifests to produce runtime-manifest.json
    
    Swift app:
    - RuntimeDownloadManager downloads VM tarballs, extracts via /usr/bin/tar,
      sets verified flags eagerly on background queue (no SHA256 on main thread)
    - VMManager and GatekeeperVMManager accept vmBundle URL parameter
    - DaemonClient gates OpenClaw VM on openclawVMReady, Gatekeeper on
      gatekeeperVMReady + OpenClaw VM running (prevents startup ordering bugs)
    - Installer advances past download screen once OpenClaw VM is ready;
      Gatekeeper downloads in background
    - Rootfs copy verified immediately after copyItem with retry on truncation
      (works around APFS deferred allocation producing partial copies)
    - Cross-VM CDP bridge uses bidirectionalRelayFDs with proper fd lifecycle
      (closeOnDealloc:false, single teardown closure, no double-close)
    - Polls for Camoufox WS endpoint file instead of hard-coded 20s sleep
    
    VM init scripts:
    - Removed runtime-cache virtiofs mount and artifact extraction from both VMs
    - OpenClaw and Camoufox binaries are pre-installed in the rootfs
    - Preserved DHCP networking fix (sleep + verbose dhclient) in Gatekeeper VM
    
    Packaging:
    - plowd-package-runtime no longer copies VM images into app bundle
    - plowd-validate-package checks runtime-manifest.json entries instead
    - justfile sets VM bundle env vars in dev mode, runtime recipe builds and
      deploys VM tarballs to S3
    
    Other:
    - Renamed camoufox_cdp_url → camoufox_ws_url (it's a Playwright WS endpoint)
    - GatekeeperVMManager.stop() simplified (removed dead isRunning check)
    - Gatekeeper VM memory bumped from 1 GiB to 2 GiB for Camoufox headroom

    _ensure-db and _ensure-dbs pass explicit PLOW_DB_PORT=55432 and
    PLOW_TEST_DB_PORT=55433 when starting compose, matching the ports
    in .env.test-common. Without this, compose defaults to slot-0

    and doesn't call _ensure-dbs.
